O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, dearest sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the knowledge of medicine together with its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and interpretations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And I saw in a vision that you should complete this with the treatise which is part of the work of hands, namely 'surgery'.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is greatly neglected in our region and has been entirely abandoned everywhere, therefore its science is lost and scattered, and there remains nothing except small descriptions about it in books moved by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this have come error and vanity, thoughts are closed off, and the science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	But it seems to me that I want to revive this together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of explanation and interpretation and abbreviation; and I will also include the shapes of cautery irons and other tools for the work with their explanations and preparations as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of hands in our time, the art of medicine has been abandoned.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And whoever undertakes this must rise to the knowledge of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgement of members, their shapes and connections and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and the number of joints, and the movement and location of moving and resting veins.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore Hippocrates said that a name without a deed is much, but with the deed it is little; and this is especially true in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not familiar with what has been said before should guard against falling into error and killing people, just as I have seen many times those who undertake this science but abandon it through lack of knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish physician who cut off an ulcer from the neck of a woman and cut the arteries of the neck, so that so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another physician who removed a stone from the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; but he took with it a piece of the bladder wall, and the man died three days later.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for to remove it, and saw the state of the sick man and the size of the stone, and knew well that if he cut him he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another physician who took in charge one of our dukes who had his leg broken, and with the breaking there was also a wound. And the doctor, full of ignorance, tied the break over the wound with strong bandages, and did not leave any linen on the wound, and left him like that for some time. And he commanded that it should not be untied, and so the leg became completely swollen and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come and untie the leg; and when I had loosened it, he felt at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the pathways were already corrupted in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop progressing through the member until the whole limb was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another physician who opened an engrained ulcer and then burned it with the wickedness of his skill.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For when a chancre is purified from melancholic humor, it should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all the corrupted matter can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: namely, that which involves danger in many situations; and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, you should be careful lest foolish physicians speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	So take your arms in hand, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that through the grace of God you come to health and are praised; and leave alone illnesses that cause great anxiety; and put away your weapons from what causes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the next one in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on severe illnesses, lest you be called a foolish physician."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauteries of fire and cauteries with medicated water, and it is arranged from the head down to the feet. It includes the shapes of instruments and implements for cautery, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, bloodletting cups, wounds, extraction of splinters, and similar things. It includes the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twistings, and similar things. It is arranged from the head down to the feet, with the shapes of instruments included.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell you about the qualities of each temperament and their benefits and harms.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest and most subtle part of this science, and its secret responses. Many wise men have spoken about it, and they agree on these things. But I will keep my words short, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally all temperaments where there is matter, except for two: namely, the hot and dry temperament without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	Some authors have divided the hot and dry temperament with matter into two parts. Some say that cautery is of great help in this temperament, while others say that cautery is not useful for illnesses caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat hot diseases with heat or dryness; and he who says otherwise claims that cautery greatly helps hot and dry diseases that come into the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the body and moisture of man to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it several times by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And moreover, let no one meddle therein who has not tried it and who knows not well the treatise of cauteries by long usage, and the diversity of the temperaments of men, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the relapses and the seasonableness of the time; we fear not concerning other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors assembled and agreed upon cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know, son, that cautery of fire together is among the secrets of healing and has greater efficacy than cautery with a medicinal fire.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not go forth from one member to another unless it be called forth, nor injures any other member if none call for it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Hot medicinal substances spread from limb to limb in misaligning them and cause difficult healings; and sometimes they kill the sick person.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire because of its height and the goodness of its substance does not do harm unless there is excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is upon the truth of things. And therefore I excuse myself for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret which belongs to fire and the quality of the work, how it drives out diseases from bodies, as philosophers say in demonstrating; now receive these thoughts into your mind.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know, son, that they agreed upon the time when cauteries should be made and chose priests.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable in all seasons because the evils which occur are overcome thereby with the help of cautery; especially if the cauteries are necessary and urgent for pains which cannot await the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish doctors do; for the disease which is healed by cautery has no relapse. And they say thus: but it is not so as they believe, because cauteries are not medicines that alter the temperament and dry up the humors which cause pain, and they are worth more than medicines because of their speed in action, their power, and their sovereignty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that sometimes disease comes according to the temperament of the sick person and the place of the disease and its power. And superfluities are gathered together in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in a place where there are few superfluities and moisture, such as those for toothache and similar diseases, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauteries are worth anything after medicines, because their intentions are mistaken, and cauteries are called the last resort of medicine because when we have administered various treatments for some disease and they do not work, then we apply cauteries, and they are effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries of gold are milder than those of iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and its high substance. They said that the place of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true, for I have tested it and found that it is true in some people. And cauteries of gold are worth more than those of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	Moreover, when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot enough because of the color of the gold, and it soon cools down. And if it is heated too much, it will melt in the fire, and there are many inconveniences to this method.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use iron cauteries which we have prepared more appropriately for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter from head to foot so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	About olive-cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two kinds of it which are made:
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is thus: the patient should be cleansed by a dissolving medicine that softens the head for three or four nights, according to what the virtue and age and habit of the patient can tolerate. Then perform the cautery behind the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Next, make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, with their hands resting on their knees. Then place the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their two eyes; where your middle fingers meet is where you should apply the cautery called "olivary," as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on the designated ink mark, and move your hand downwards and outwards little by little while twisting. Then raise your hand gently, and examine the mark to see if you can see the bone – just a little bit of it. If not, resume cauterizing until you do see the bone as I have told you. Next, take some flax, dampen it, wrap it in soft cotton, place it on the wound, and let it stay for three days. Then apply warm linen soaked in butter, leaving it on until the scab has fallen off. Afterwards, treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And as the ancients said, the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges itself; therefore, this treatment aids in that manner.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	Some of these people also say that the cautery should be kept on until part of the bone is burned. Then remove what has been burned from the bone and dress the wound to heal it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	Some others say that one should keep the cautery on until it burns away a piece of bone as large as a hazelnut, so that the humors can flow out freely. The wound should then be left open for an extended period before being dressed and healed.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	But I do not consider these two methods of cautery to be entirely good. They may be appropriate for certain people who are very afraid. However, I believe that in most cases, it is better to leave the wound alone because the flesh becomes weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we observe in other parts of the body. Therefore, in my opinion, the first application of cautery is more beneficial and gentle. That is the method I generally use.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Here begins the chapter on the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the head suffers from chronic and long-lasting pain, the sick person should use electuaries called "cochiae," as well as purgatives for the head, oils, and plasters. If cauterization is performed using the method we described earlier without success.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be careful if the patient's flesh is of strong nature and not too cold; in this case, you can cauterize using a little bit less heat than what we mentioned earlier.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Then perform cauterization on each of the patient's horns up to the bone, as we mentioned earlier. Also, perform one cautery on the spot called "vessel" where cupping glasses are placed. Be careful not to burn too deeply – the patient will feel more pain from this cautery than from the others. The cauteries on the horns should be gentler than those on the middle of the head, and here is how it's done:
dou cautere dou chief	"For the cautery of the head,"
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	"If sudden pain comes in one part of the head and extends to the eye, and the head is purged with medicines that remove impurities, and other treatments mentioned in the division of diseases have been performed but do not help: then cauterization should be done in two ways, namely using hot medicine or fire."
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	"For cauterization using hot medicine: Take an almond seed, remove its skin and crush it into two parts; then make a hole in the temple where the pain is felt such that you can place the almond seed underneath the skin. Then tie it tightly with string and leave it for twelve hours. After this time, untie it and rub the almond seed with garlic oil, leaving the wound open for two or three days. Then apply a cotton pad soaked in butter until it sticks out of the wound."
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	"After treating with ointment until healed, if you see fit to apply any burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines."
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	"The cauterization using fire is done as follows: Heat the cautery tool, which has this shape:"
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	"And it is called 'closed' because the head of the cautery tool is shaped like a cloak with a slight curvature on one side and a small protrusion in the middle. Place it on the painful spot and turn the fire gently so that half of the diameter of the heart is burned, but do not let your hand touch the artery, which is located further away from the skin. Then lift your hand to prevent the blood vessels from burning excessively."
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	"After that, apply cotton soaked in saffron water to the wound for three days. Then apply cotton moistened with butter and continue treating the wound with ointment until it heals. If you wish to cauterize this migraine using a cautery tool called 'cultellare', which has a sharp point, be careful not to cut into the old artery in this migraine."
de emigraine	"of migraine"
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	"If when treating migraine as we have previously described in the section on dividing diseases, you find that it is not improving and that the cauteries made of medicine and iron do not help, then you must heat the cautery tool called 'cultellare' until it turns white. Then press down firmly with one line of half an inch length on the painful spot, without cutting too deeply to avoid hitting the artery or bone. Be careful not to touch the jawbone that moves when chewing and make sure the nerve does not spasm causing paralysis of the face. Also be careful not to cause excessive bleeding from the artery once it is cut, especially if you are not experienced or practiced in this procedure. Leave the wound open halfway, but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut and show you where to find this information in this book."
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	"And if you find that these cauteries do not help the disease and the patient is suffering, then cauterize him on the head as we have described previously, and continue treating the wound until it heals. If you still see no improvement, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, using a tool with two blades; this cautery is better and more helpful than the previous one."
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	"on ear pain caused by coldness"
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold pain comes in the ear, and medicines are applied there, both soluble ones and other treatments mentioned in the division, but the pain does not decrease, then heat this cautery called "pointe":
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the cautery all around the affected ear, or around the two joints if pain is felt on both sides, then move it away a little from the root of the ear and mark the spot where you start. Apply ten points to each ear; afterwards, cleanse the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Only those tortures that move from the eye can be cured by cautery; those that come from heat and spasm of the nerves should not receive one.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this appearance of torture that moves from the eye with eyewashes and head sprinklings and gargarisms, but it does not improve, then it is necessary to cauterize the affected area with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little beyond the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips. Place the cautery on the healthy part that is exposed, and make the cautery at the top of the ear just above the corner of the head, and another on the temple as long as one finger; leave the cautery until half of it has burned. This is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the appearance of the cautery that we have shown above, but it is a little more refined and the knife should be a little thicker. After cauterizing the area as I have said before, cleanse it until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have said, but there is no improvement and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one on the area called "vessels" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; cure it as we have said previously.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large syrups and pills made from Mondifia for the brain. Then raise the head of the patient completely, and place on the occiput the plaster of mustard that is written about in the treatise on plasters; perform it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is cured this way, that's good; but if not, apply three cauteries from the middle of the head down to the neck, with a space of two fingers between each cautery. Cure it as the others were, and if you see it joined together, and the patient is suffering, then apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, apply two more on the two corners of the head, and cure until it is healed. Use the cautery called "olivary" as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed with syrups and the things we have mentioned before. Then raise the head of the patient, apply a cautery in the middle of the head and on each corner, one behind and three on the spine of the neck; if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, then apply four cauteries on the spine of the back. Leave it until half of the cautery has burned, then lift your hand. After that, cure until it is healed, using the cautery called "olivary" that we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not be cauterized with anything other than the flebotomistic cautery. First, cleanse the brain with syrups and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and suffers from taking medicines.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot endure it, then apply gargarisms and mastication that cleanses the brain frequently with good foods. Then raise the head in the middle, apply one cautery according to what we have said before, and another on the vessel, and on each corner; and if the patient is severe and suffering, then apply cauteries as I have said for paralysis and limpness of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, using the olivary cautery according to the manner that I have mentioned.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excesses or corrupted moistures and thick blood, then cauterize with several cauteries as we have said for paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy there is a decline towards melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give them something to drink by which the brain can be cleansed, according to what has been mentioned before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After raising the head of the patient, make one twisted cord of well-made linen, like a circle, and place it on the head. The patient should sit cross-legged and be held firmly on all sides. Then present the linen bandage, melted with old sheep butter; heat it moderately over fire so that the patient can bear it when poured onto their head. Afterward, empty the circle inside the head and let it cool. Do this to the patient once a week with other good governance until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or if you wish to cauterize while making more points along the entire cautery, this manner of cautery moistens the brain increasingly. Then place on cotton moistened in butter and grease of jelly.
de l’awe des eulz	of inflammation of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When inflammation first comes to the eyes with the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin by giving the patient something to drink that cleanses the head and keeps them from all moistures. Make them sweat or take baths several times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterward, have them raise their head, apply a cautery on the head, and apply two cauteries on the temples if the inflammation descends to both eyes together, or one if it is only in one eye. Cut all veins and arteries that are under the heart along the entire cautery, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple. Be careful not to cause bleeding, and if too much blood comes out, then stain it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	"And I will teach you about the extraction of arrows and how to incise cauterization, and how you should stretch it; and sometimes a cautery or caustic is applied beneath the two bones behind."
dou cors des larmes	"tear duct"
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When tears of the eyes are chronic and habitual and appear on veins, or near arteries that are visible at the forehead's surface, and it is seen that they are cold, watery superfluities, then apply the cautery as mentioned at the beginning: one cautery among the eyebrows descending towards the eyes; two cauteries above each temple; and two cauteries behind below the two bones. And if more are needed, cauterize along the eyebrow with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	concerning the body's tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	But when you apply the medicines as we have said in the division and they do not help, then give the patient three ounces of hemp juice to drink. Afterwards raise his head, and cauterize him with an olive-shaped cautery at the middle of his forehead; and make two cauteries called "clavilis" above each eyebrow, a little below the eyebrows; but beware not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	"And this is the shape of the cautery called 'clavilis':"
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery called "olivare", here is its shape:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	"And if you see that you make two cauteries on the two eyelids as long as the eyelashes are, and do not leave your hand until one-third of the paper is burnt, according to the manner I have said."
dou poil qui point l’oil	"of the hair that protects the eye"
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	"Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes turn towards the partedens and prick the eye, and in this case cauteries are made in two ways: either with fire or with burning medicine."
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	"Or the cautery of fire commands the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their birth, he should restrain his eyes so that they do not move until they are born."
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	"When they are born and grown even, then the patient puts on his nightshirt. Afterwards he places on the paper of the eyes a figure that is like the full moon, with the beginning of the sign near the hairs; then he puts damp cotton in egg-white and musk-mallow on the eye, then he heats the cautery, which has this form:"
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"After cauterizing on the figure you have marked little by little many times until the skin is burnt there; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper withdraw, and the hairs raised at the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put damp cotton in butter until the burning is gone; afterwards cure with ointment until it is healed."
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	"And if afterwards the hairs come again, and the paper is softened, then recommence the cautery on the same place as you have done first; and if the hairs are few, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye."
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	"The cautery of burning medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a form of parchment like the full moon. Then take three ounces each of soap of France and live wax, and grind them together well; and do it hastily so that it does not cool, then spread on the form that you have made like the full moon, and place it on the paper of the eyes; and if the patient has only one eye, one should operate on one, and if both, on both. And put damp cotton in egg-white under the eye; and let the skin of the patient be in his nightshirt and put your two fingers showing on the medicine, and press a little each time that the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for he feels the biting like fire."
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	"When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger."
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when the biting has passed, then lift up the eyelid and see if you see the paper lifted as if it were lifted by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is thus, it is good. If not, put more medicine on the place where the medicine did not act until your work is even, and your eyes are sharp; then put damp cotton in butter until the burnt skin has fallen off, afterwards cure the place with ointment called 'dyafenis' and others, until it is healed."
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	"And if you need to take great care with your work that no medicine falls into the eyes. And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick the eye, then recommence the medicine on the place which is softened by the paper properly, as you have done before; afterwards cure until it is healed; and this is the form of the full moon."
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	"And know that the eyes of people are diverse in size and smallness, and according to that make your constraints; and do not be satisfied with the right way for him who has the study of this art."
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Here is a translation of the text you provided about the treatment of fistulas using cautery:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the section on diseases, and your treatment does not help, then you must perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Tell the patient to place their head on your hand. Then hold the patient's head with both of your hands so that it does not move or turn its head. Afterward, moisten cotton with egg white or onion juice and apply it to the eye. Next, heat the cautery instrument, which is shaped like a chicken feather, including the tip of the cautery. If you look closely, it should be pointed from one end to the other, resembling a tent. However, whichever shape suits your purpose will do.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing on the fistula if it is open to remove and dry out the pus, and if it is closed, then make an incision and draw out the bowel. Next, apply the heated cautery firmly onto it, keeping your hand on the handle of the cautery near the eye so that your hand does not slip. Insert the cautery into the fat around the eye and burn it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you cauterize up to the bone at the beginning, that would be good. If not, repeat the cautery one or more times as necessary and leave it for three days. Then apply moistened cotton soaked in butter and continue with the drying ointment treatment until healed. If it is not healed after forty days, apply a corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed. Follow this treatment according to your judgment.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients mentioned. First, identify the fistula and make an incision in it; afterward place one of these small, delicate instruments into the opening:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they do it with the quantity of a half penny; and hold your hand firmly over the cauldron, and let not the patient move or twitch, lest the molten lead run into his eye; and one must put moistened cotton in the egg or water: the lead thus applied heals the fistulous ulcer marvelously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	But if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have described, that is good; but if not, then one must administer a probe to the nose and bring the fistula back into its proper place in the flesh according to what it should be in its own proper position.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Cracks on the lips that are called "splits" occur very frequently, especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat one small cautery scalpel according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly in those cracks until it comes into contact with the flesh; afterward dress the wound with cerate until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the boil on the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When a boil comes at the root of the throat or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it becomes gangrenous and rotted and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have described in sections, and it does not improve: then one must have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterward bore or probe the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron comes into contact with the front and behind of it; and do this once or twice, afterward dress it with what we have said in treatments until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, that is good; but if not, then one must uncover the wound and remove the rotted bone, according to what you will find about it in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but it's ineffective, then place the head of the patient in your lap. Afterward, heat the cautery whose shape will be described later so that you can put a cannula on the tooth; and quickly insert the heated cautery inside, keeping your hand there until the patient feels the warmth reaching the root of the tooth. Then lift your hand and repeat the process according to your desire. Afterward, have the patient rinse their mouth with salted water, and let it sit for an hour and spit it out forcefully.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving becomes fixed, and the softened gum becomes firm, and the corrupting moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, whether it's caused by cold or wind, and treatments with medicine are ineffective, then there is need for cautery in two ways: cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is done as follows: take virgin butter and put some on the tip of an iron or brass spoon. Then take cotton, wrap it around the end of a needle, dip it in the melted butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth until it cools down. Repeat this often so that its effect reaches the root of the tooth. If you see that wetting the linen and cotton with cold butter does not help, then take a red-hot iron and hold it near the tooth until the heat reaches the top of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	Combined fire cautery is done as follows: take an iron or brass cannula that is thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient. Afterward, heat the cautery, whose shape will be described later, and place it on the tooth while keeping your hand there until the cautery cools down. Repeat this often, as the pain will be relieved the same day or the next day. The patient must fill their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then spit it out forcefully. This is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	Make a cautery of whatever size you wish, according to your ability; and this is the shape of the cannula:
des scrophules	scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and does not respond to treatment with medicines, then heat the cautery described below, which has two openings for smoke to escape from the other end of the cautery. Place the hot cautery on the boil once or twice until it reaches its base. If the boil is small, use a smaller cautery and leave it in place for three days. Then apply cotton soaked in butter until the burn is healed. Afterward, treat the wound with ointments and bandages until it heals completely.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the lung, especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then the patient should first be purged with solvent medicines. Afterwards, apply a cautery to the root of the throat, but make sure not to reach the throat itself, and only singe a little of the heart. Then apply another cautery at the joint of the neck and the top of the spine, using the cautery called 'clavile', of which we have the shape before us. And treat the area until it is healed.
de la toust	Of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	If the cough and lung disease are caused by cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or shortness of breath, and the disease is chronic, then apply two cauteries on the back at the kidneys; and another cautery between the breasts near the nipples. Use the cautery called 'clavile', as shown in the figure before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	"And if you see, make the cautery incision with all of the cautery that is called 'poins', the form of which is shown above in the ear disease; and let the points be up to thirty, or around that number. Afterwards, treat the area according to what is said before, and let there be three rows of cauteries according to this form:"
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	"And because the cauteries are lighter, make three at once."
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	"of the dislocation of the jaw joint"
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	"When the jawbone is dislocated due to moisture and is put back into place but cannot remain there and keeps dislocating with even small movements, as we have experienced, then it becomes necessary for you to first reset the dislocation."
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	"Then have the patient lie on their back and side. Afterwards, lift the heart that is inside the titillite with the two fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, heat the cautery that has two rows until it reaches this form:"
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	"And cauterize the heart until it penetrates to the side, and let the figure of the cautery reach four cauteries in total; and since this is done with the cautery that has three rows, the figure of the cauterization will be six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the thinness of a thread, which is the form of the cautery that has three rows:"
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	"And sometimes it is also joined onto this one nerve, so there are eight cauteries."
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	"Afterwards, apply a poultice made of bruised celandine with oil. Afterwards, let the patient rest and do not move their limbs for a long time until they are well comforted."
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	"And if it is dislocated upwards, which happens rarely, then cauterize on the thick part of the clavicle bone, or many cauteries in pricking. For the joint will be closed, the moisture will be removed, and the patient will be healthy."
dou cautere de pleuresin	"Of the cautery for pleurisy"
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The Ancients said that for pleurisy, one should make cauteries with the roots of aristologist, and in this manner: Take a long root of aristologist, as large and thick as you can find, and dry it; moisten it in oil and heat it on fire. Make one cautery between the navel and the neck, two small ones a little lower, below the beard; two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly backwards; one cautery inside the breast, another one above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders; two more on both sides of the breast near the cautery between the shoulders. Do not press your hand hard, but hold it at a distance, like when smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And some Ancients said that some people used a cautery resembling a razor's edge, heated it and placed it between the ribs until it reached the abscess; when the pain ceased, as we have said in the case of the liver abscess. But in this operation, there is danger or the patient may die now, or a fistula may develop which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Here is the text "de la mice" in proper formatting:
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the eye that we have mentioned under divisions of treatments, and it does not improve at all, then there are three kinds of cautery that are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	Of these, one manner is such that you make three or four cauteries, lining them up according to the length of the mouse, following the shape of the liver cautery which we have described earlier; and do not rush your hand through the entire cautery, and let the patient always lie on their back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two points, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is located near the mouse, where the rib of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevation by which you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After this, insert the two inflamed points until the heart is pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see fit, cauterize with a cautery of three points. Afterwards, when the wound has thrown off its corruption over time, it is worth more than any of the treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	de ydropisie
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	Cautery is not useful for dropsy except in the manner that is called "ascites". When you treat it according to the methods that we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment does not help at all, then you must make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the mouse, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cauteries be close to the space of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to discharge corruption for a long time, and do not leave off treating the patient afterwards; and healing will be hastened, and both intentions will come together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be like the key that we have shown before; and those for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been placed before.
de l’enfleure des piez	Here is how to treat swelling of the feet:
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical and filled with yellow water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning. And do not enter too deeply so as not to damage the yellow water, and let the cautery be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards make two cauteries on each leg, two cauteries on each leg at the point of the cuticle; and let one cautery be long below the knee in front and the other behind in the middle of the leg; leave the cauteries on for a long time without dressing until they are discharged; afterwards cure the rest as we have said.
de la menoison	of the wound
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the stomach comes from coldness and moisture to such an extent that the retentive and digestive virtue which is in the stomach and intestines is weakened, and cannot be cured by any kind of cure; and you see the patient suffering greatly but with great strength, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said about the cautery of the stomach earlier, at the circular cautery; and four subtle cauteries around the mouth, each cautery being like a nail, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the point of the hip, and one cautery on each thigh, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
