Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and are made up of large cold and moist corrupt humors, and have been cured by division as we have said but it is not helpful, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that one which is directly behind the neck at the nape of the neck and somewhat triangularly placed, and one below the mouth.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is cooled and the food does not digest well and you see swelling of the face, then make one large cautery on the stomach as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen, each cautery being like a nail; leave the cauteries on for a long time. Afterwards cure the wound until it is sound.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the softness called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut artery, then heat the cautery that seems like one razor, and then put it all ablaze on the cut artery; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the birth of the vein, where the blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there is much artery, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards cure with ointments until they are clean. And if you cauterize with a large cautery on an artery, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	Of poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then such an illness comes that it cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to someone and it is inflamed and filled with corruption and putrid moisture, you should probe the whole thing carefully with a fine probe, making sure you know exactly how deep it is. Afterwards heat the cautery that looks like one razor, and insert it into the fistula according to how much the probe has entered, and keep heating until all the corrupt flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times depending on what is needed; and be careful not to burn any nerves or large veins. If the fistula goes to the bladder or intestines, be careful in those places, and do not operate outside of an area that is thick with flesh, and think that it is not easy to heal; afterwards cure the wound until it is healed, and if the wound closes up and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the wound is entirely healed. But if the matter has not been removed, know that the wound is too deep, and the bone at the front is corrupt; and so do as we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Regarding kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	If cold pain comes in the kidneys and there is great windiness, and no woman's flow appears, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on the kidneys on one side and the other with the clavicle cautery we mentioned earlier; and if we cauterize it in the middle, it will have three cauteries in a row, which will be of greater help.
de la vessie	Regarding the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	If the bladder is weak and cold and moist so that the patient retains urine, then perform cautery on the front part of the bladder where the pubic hair starts, one on the right side and one on the left side, each cautery being as long as a hazelnut; and perform one cautery on the backside, or two if necessary, using the clavicle cautery according to the shape previously described.
de la marris	Regarding hemorrhoids (piles)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not permit conception because of it, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms delayed; and when they come, great pain is felt: then it is necessary that three cauteries be made around the pudendum, as we have said about the bladder cautery, and two cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be clove-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the groin
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous humors descend to the groin and cause it to move from its place, and the sign is that the thigh appears longer than the other when measured together; and if the location of the separation is found empty, then you must cauterize the patient above the groin with one cautery shaped like a circle, and extend it before the place around the groin as it turns, so that the groin is inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cautery be as deep as all the heart; and continue until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of groin pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the groin, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated for this with what we have said in the division but the treatment does not help, and the disease is ancient: then you must purge the patient of thick humors using foul-smelling pills or other good pills resembling them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, perform cautery: and the manner of cautery is in two ways: namely, together with medicines that burn, and fire cautery. Fire cautery has many forms, one of which is this: you make three triangular cauteries on the groin according to this shape, and make them well-profound and large, and have between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle on top of the head of the groin, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	"And if you see it, cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have mentioned earlier in the case of dislocation of the hip joint; but do so in such a way that the circle contains the entire hip joint, and all the sharp edges of the heart are burned."
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	"And this is the method that is used in sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip joint and does not reach the thigh or the leg. And if it reaches the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient feels the pain, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers to the left; and let the cauteries be elliptical, and burn the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends down to the foot or near it, cauterize there where they feel the pain with three or four cauteries called 'points'."
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	"And if it is necessary to do more; and if the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with an elliptical or circular cautery, but be sure in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on too long so as not to burn the nerves and large arteries, and so as not to cause greater harm and contraction to the patient."
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	"And I have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it on so long that the leg became entirely swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all over the foot. After this, he had a bowel movement from which he died."
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	"And if the pain is in two parts at once, make cauteries in both according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And let it be heated until it is entirely red and glistening with heat, then place it on the boil of the sick person's haunch, turned to face the sound side; cauterize once with one cautery iron, leave for three days, then make an embrocation of butter, allow the wound to remain open for a long time; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed."
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	"Albucasis says that we use this cautery rarely due to its intense heat, and it is scarcely used. Nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries when it can be endured, especially where it causes inflammation."
de la dolor dou dos	"back pain"
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar matter spread coldly, cauteries are of no use in any of these cases except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After the patient has been emptied of fetid pills or others like them, one should place them on the back where the pain is located, three lines marked with ink, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see fit, make three cauteries or four at the middle clavicle bone according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes upon young children, and the sign of its onset is that they have a narrow waist when they stand up, and are pale. And you find in the dorsal spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to cure it, cauterize with the cautery called "celcle" according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery touches each part of the spine equally. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the pointed cautery two or three lines, and let the points be close together. Afterward, dress the wound until it is healed according to what we have said, and take care not to apply a cautery in an area that has spasms of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	de la dolor des jointes
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pains in the joints are due to moistures that are spread throughout each member of the body, and when pain comes on in the feet, which physicians properly call "podagra," and when it is from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: Make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	"And if there is need to press upon the face of the foot, make the cautery completely as they call it 'point'. And if pains extend to the knee and other joints, which happens often, make three cauteries or four on each knee, all with olive oil; and if more are needed, then do more, but do not hold your hand too long until the heart's blade is burned."
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	"And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery which we have spoken of in its chapter. And if there is pain in the hands, make punctures around the fist two lines; and if there remains any pain on the arms, then make punctures on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the hips or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and give medicines. For if you provide good care and purge phlegm, it will be healthy with God's help."
de la routure dou syfac	"of the operation of the syringe"
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	"When operation comes in the anus, and the bowels descend to the thighs and this is newly begun, then it is necessary that when you see him cure himself, he does not eat that day, and let him use things that leave the belly so that the feces come down from his belly; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are relaxed, and stretch them out towards your two fingers, and press firmly below the operation on the bone of the thumb, and at each sign it should resemble half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery which has this form:"
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	"until it is white and throws off sparks. Then stretch the bowels back to their place; and the minister holds his hand upon them so that they do not return backwards; and open the thighs well for the patient, and put a cushion underneath him and one servant on each thigh, and another on his breast who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your might, and hold it with your right hand until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then begin again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bowels do not slip out when you make the cautery, so that you do not burn them, and so that by this the patient does not die or suffer some other harm."
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	"And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be thin according to their size, and those for large people also large according to theirs; afterwards three days after the cautery wound should be smeared with butter until the burn is healed; then cure it with other ointments until it is healthy, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his diet be restricted for a long time so that the bowels do not slip out when he gets up to go to the privy."
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	"And afterwards, forty days later when he wants to get up, let him bring him a well-made sling, and wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not work too much and be careful of excessive drinking and eating, and of raising himself up too high; and when he follows this teaching he will be entirely healed. And I will speak later about the cure of hemorrhoids in its chapter."
de la routure dou ventre	Chapter 45: Of the operation for piles
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	"If piles come in other bellies and are known to you, and you see that they do not grow any more, make one cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and burn the third of the heart; afterwards cure it as we have said; and some of the ancients say that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:"
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	"but first mark the place where it begins and make a line across its width above the piles, and another below, and hold your hand in with all your might during the cautery; but the first cauteries are lighter and softer."
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Chapter 46: Of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	"If pain comes in some limb, either from a fall or a blow, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cure with medicine is of no avail, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called 'the point', and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of twists and its pain. If it is healed from the first cautery, that's good; but if not, then begin another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom that it must move towards the limb that is nearby, therefore you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed."
de meselerie	Chapter 47: Of stitches
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	"Stitches are sometimes helped by cautery with great help, and especially the illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it to cauterize, take care if the illness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in its division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that corruption may affect the whole illness, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, and another towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and hold your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and so that the bark comes out so that the vapors of thick humors can escape from it; and cauterize it on the mouse according to what is in front."
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	"And if the stitches are spread out everywhere and it is manifestly lost, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery near the ear, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another beside it, and two on each shoulder; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the back of the calf, so that you do not burn them; and sometimes one makes a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver."
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	"And know that the more cauteries you make, the more help you do and move the profit; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already all corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauteries are large and small according to the members and the joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the irons. Afterward cure the place with barley flour with honey and other cures until he is healed."
de enfleure	Chapter 48: Of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	"When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines, oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then you make cauteries on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery be a little entering into the middle of the heart; then cure it with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes one makes a cautery at the hand, foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if the swelling is removed; and nevertheless no one should meddle with it if he is not knowledgeable of the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body."
de albaras	Of the ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" becomes inflamed, and medical treatments do not work, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep according to the thickness of the skin, until the blister is removed and its color changes; then treat it with a mixture of wheat flour and lentil flour with rose oil and plantain leaves, and pigeon blood and donkey blood, each one part; and mix everything together, and tie it with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of a chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre appears at the beginning and you see it stop, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles one circle all around the chancre. And furthermore, wise men say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, for I have seen it happen several times before. And it is more appropriate to cauterize around it with the cautery called "circule", as we have said concerning many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of inflammation that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	If someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it is delayed in dying, either due to the excessiveness of its condition or because of the coldness of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to the weather; and you see that it wants to die quickly: then cauterize it with many small cauteries around it. Afterward, leave it thus. For it will hasten in dying.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it entirely with the cautery, then heat the cautery of which here is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness which is called «adubelati» until the cauteries have pierced the heart, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels drawn towards them in such a way that the course of the corruption is alleviated. After the cure, once it is perfectly sound.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cautery with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	There is another type of illness called "corrodens", which is nothing but a consumption of the limb, for it consumes limbs just like fire consumes dry logs. If you see this illness in a place where cauterization with fire can be safely applied together, then heat the cauteries, both small and large, according to what is needed for the affected area; afterwards cauterize from all sides until all corruption has been removed, leaving nothing behind that is not consumed by the fire. And then leave it alone for three days, and apply compresses with oily substances that generate flesh for three days until the burns from the fire are healed, and all corruption is removed. After that, if healthy flesh does not grow after three days, repeat the cauterization on the remaining corrupted areas. This consumption has sometimes been cured with hot medicine instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is more helpful, as I have already stated in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Regarding swellings that come on one's feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times, an illness called a "clot" according to our understanding appears on the feet due to bad blood, and it is a large, broken thing that wounds the foot. The cautery for this illness is done in two ways: fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery involves heating one cautery the size of a chicken feather, made from good iron and with subtle edges, to fit around the clot on all sides; then place it hot on the clot and turn your hand around the clot until you reach the center; leave it like that for three days until it begins to discharge corruption. Then make a poultice of wild mallows ground up with salt, apply it overnight, and the clot will fall off and its roots will be removed. Afterwards, treat the area with flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if these growths appear on other parts of the body, such as hands or feet, many times, then you must bring a hot water cautery. Here's how it is done: take a cane made of earthenware or iron, or a chicken feather, and place it around the growth or verruca; put the cane on so that it surrounds everything, then pour some hot water onto it and hold your hand firmly, turning it while pressing so that the edges of the cane reach the root of the growth and the hot water can find a deep pathway to the root. Let the illness suffer this hot water bite for about an hour, then leave it alone and it will fall off completely with all its roots. Do this again and again until you have removed all such growths on the body; afterwards treat them with flesh-generating ointments.
li cure dou trembler	Here is how to treat trembling:
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shivers with coldness of nerves,
des pustules puans	of foul boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	No matter how many foul boils appear on the body, they should be cauterized as soon as possible with a pine wood cautery or a long root cautery of Aristologus, or a lenticular cautery. They must be cauterized at the beginning when they appear, and they will not grow any further but will be broken up and cleansed by removing the excess material from which they arise. However, this should only be done after the blood has been evacuated.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound on the surface or at the incision of an aposteme or at the cautery of a member, and similar things. It is very painful to endure.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	"And indeed when this happens to anyone, then you should hasten to place your two index fingers on the vein wound, and press firmly until the blood beneath is pacified so that no more drips out; then put in the fire olive oil cauteries of various sizes until they are all red hot; then take one, either large or small according to the wound size and where the artery is severed, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding stops."
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	"And if it happens that the cautery is exhausted when you lift your finger from the vein, then take another quickly from those in the fire."
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	"And continue doing this until the bleeding stops. Make sure that you do not burn the nerve nearby and that no other harm comes to the patient. Know that when blood spurts from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped unless one of the four methods we have mentioned is used: cautery, extraction if it has not been treated, tight binding with thread, or medicines applied which have the power to stop bleeding. And let it be tied and pressed appropriately."
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	"And bringing about cessation of bleeding through tight binding with rags or applying hot things on top, or other similar methods, will profit little if at all."
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	"And if this happens to anyone and there is no doctor or medicine present, then one should place their index finger on the vein wound as we have said, and press firmly until the bleeding stops. Do not move your finger but moisten it with cold water frequently so that it becomes very cold until the blood congeals and ceases flowing; and afterwards do what is necessary with regard to cauteries and medicines."
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	"Here begins the second book of the remedies for wounds from cutting."
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	"We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases which require cautery with fire or hot medicine, and we have described their causes and remedies and forms of cauteries; and I have placed this chapter at the beginning so that one may find more easily what one wishes to know."
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	"Before I begin this chapter, dear friend, you should know that there is more danger and fear in this one concerning cauteries than in the first, and therefore it requires greater caution."
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	"For in the practice of this chapter there are many occasions for bleeding from opening veins, and incision on apostumes, and wounds, and extraction of splinters, and incision on stone, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many people die."
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	"And I warn you not to undertake anything foolish. For many kinds of people come for treatment, and some of them are so eager about their illness that they die easily from the recklessness that comes from their disease and its severity; and one should fear such."
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	"And there are those who lose their senses and say: 'Wait, I am cured'; and the disease is stubborn. One should not consent to such people who come to you with this manner, but rather put more care into your honor than your greed, and do not open wounds recklessly but judiciously about those things which you are certain of and can gain praise and glory from; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your sick so that salvation may be obtained; and this will help you to gain good reputation, glory, and memory of praise."
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	"Dear friend, may our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen."
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	"Now I have arranged this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cauteries which I have already divided from beginning to end, so that you may find more easily what you need."
dou chief plein d’aigue	Chapter 1: Head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	"Know that this disease often occurs in infants at birth, when the mother's passage is too narrow for the child's head; and sometimes it happens without any known cause."
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	"And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than infants, and all those whom I saw died quickly; and therefore it seems to me that I may leave the treatment of such conditions alone."
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	"And I saw one child whose head was full of water and grew larger every day until it could no longer support itself; and the swelling became so great that it died, and this swelling gathered under the bone on top of the syphac, between the heart and the bone; and if the swelling is between the heart and the bone, and the aposteme is small, then you should make an incision through the middle of the head with a blade wide enough for the swelling to escape; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the swelling can pass through. Here is the form of the spatulum:"
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	"If the swelling is larger and the aposteme is bigger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:"
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	"And if the swelling is under the bone and you see the signs that the angles of the head are open on each side, and water jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, but nothing comes out: then you must make three incisions through the head according to this method:"
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	"And after the incision, remove all of the swelling outward. Then tie up the incisions with bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, leaving it like this for five days; then untie it and treat the wound with tents and ointments, keeping the head wrapped evenly, and give the sick person dry food to eat until their member is strengthened and healed."
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	"And another method of incision is to observe where the greatest enlargement of the aposteme and the gathering of water appear, for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right side, and sometimes on the left."
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	"Therefore cut there where the aposteme appears and the gathering of water, and make the incision according to what you can manage; and be careful not to cut the artery; and if a vein flows with blood, so that the sick person dies from the loss of blood and evacuation of swelling."
de reume	Chapter 2: Rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	"When someone has a disease called 'catarrh' in the ears or feet, and the illness is long-standing and does not improve with medicinal treatment, then the final treatment should be cauteries combined with ligating the two arteries."
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	"Therefore, when you tie the vessels, make sure that the sick person turns their head back; then rub the area with a rough bandage until the arteries appear, then wrap the sick person's neck tightly with one bandage. Then look where the vein is located and mark the spots of both sides after the ears, and press them gently with your fingers. Then sign the spots with a hot cautery, then cut both sides with a sharp spatula two parts deep until you reach the bone, and do this through the width of the head."
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	"And if you see, push the spatula underneath the artery and cut it above it, cutting also two fingers wide across."
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood spurts out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at the touch, you should measure three fingers' width of space, then cut until you reach the bone. The amount of blood that should come out is six ounces, but it may vary slightly more or less depending on what the patient can tolerate and how full the artery is. Then examine the wound: if there remains a point of the syphon on the bone, cauterize it with hot iron without coming too close to it. Then compress the wound and bind it, and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	"Of dislocations"
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dislocation and catarrh occur due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples, accompanied by madness and similar conditions, it is treated with various medical remedies but not all of them are effective. Therefore, we draw out the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient shaves the hair from their temples and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, for it beats well there, and is rarely covered except in some men who are very cold; and if it is covered, then the patient draws its neck with certain cloths, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the place with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatumile of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then gently scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then raise it with tweezers and carefully separate it from the tissues that are underneath each part; and if the artery is delicate, cut it off with the point of a needle, then cut that part according to the quantity of two fingers. For if it is not cut, all the blood will not flow freely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	"And draw blood from the.vi. veins, until.iij.; and if the artery is large, you should tie it in two places with a double strand of strong silk thread to prevent decay reaching the wound before the stitching, and let blood flow; then cut away the excess flesh between the two ties at that very moment, and then, if you wish, cauterize with the surgical cautery until the bone is reached; and this is the main procedure if the patient has no fever and is of warm complexion."
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Furthermore, cauterization aids in finishing off moistures (i.e., infections): therefore it is more helpful with moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When extracting arteries, one should fill the space with old cotton and place well-made bandages on top; once they are untied, cure it with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until it is healed. If blood flows from the artery while working on it, hasten to cauterize with a hot iron or pour vitriol into your hand and place it over the wound to stop the bleeding; if you don't have this available, rub the wound with your thumb until the blood congeals, then rinse it with cold water until the bleeding stops, and bind it as necessary. The best and easiest method for extracting an artery is to cauterize its channel with a two-pronged cautery iron, but make sure the prongs are well-spaced to retain heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the prongs are too thin, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be one finger's width of space between the two blades, and then once you have marked the two spots with the hot iron, place it on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the channel in two places; and let the two wounds be some distance apart because this cautery does not join them entirely together; and that is the shape of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears from the eyes flow down the channels that are above the forehead of the head, and it does not help to treat them with medicine, and you see the sick person's face becoming reddened, and feel on their forehead trembling like shivers; and if the eyelashes are thin and moist so that the hairs of the paper-like tissues have fallen off, and the papers themselves are heated and burned by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancients called this "treatment for contusion," and it is done as follows: shave the hair from the forehead of the patient suffering from this disease, then make three incisions on the forehead evenly according to its length; one incision should be two fingers wide running downwards from the middle of the forehead to the nose, and the other two should be two fingers apart above the eyebrows, being careful not to cut the arteries that are located on either side above the eyebrows; keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and each wound should be three fingers wide across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And prepare a sponge and many cloths to wipe away the blood, then take the scalpel with two prongs like this:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	Make the incision that is directly above the temple down to the second incision; then scrape away all the skin that is between the two incisions as far back as it reaches on the bone, and then make another incision from the middle one to the other second one, and finally extract this scalpel.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision the instrument called "cultellaria," which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, not sharp; this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the sharp edge of the instrument towards the flesh near the heart, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle incision. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to where it opens onto the brain, and then make another incision in the middle one until it meets the other; and then extract blood evenly, and squeeze the area for blood collection; then place a gauze of old cotton into each incision, and put moistened cloths made from wine, oil, and roses on top, making sure that no abscesses form there. And on the third day remove the stitches, and apply a great deal of cold water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	glaucoma
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When catarrh occurs frequently, and you see the eyes thin and small, and vision weakened, and the paper-like tissues burned; and the hairs fall out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the sick person sneezes; then know from these symptoms that these materials and this catarrh come only from many veins, and the remedy for it is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is as follows: have the patient lie on their back, then make a wide incision in the middle of the forehead and another one about an inch wide. Start from the left temple incision to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone; avoid the temples' nerves that move during chewing. Once the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then open up between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton and linen gauze inside it. Then tie moistened cloths made from wine and oil on top, making sure no hot abscess forms there; when removed, rub the bone until flesh begins to form, then treat it with drying agents that promote scar tissue formation.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster with them; apply it to these wounds to promote scar tissue formation throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	To treat ear blockages
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of these four things:
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When a stone falls into the ear in such a way that it does not fit properly and grows within the ear, place the ear toward the sun. If you see the stone, apply a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then proceed with extraction; during this process, cause the patient to sneeze, plug their nostrils when they do so, and wrap cloth or wool around the ear; keep the ear raised. Often heat comes from this treatment; if it does not produce heat, use fine forceps for extraction; here is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not come out with the forceps, it is good to proceed with extraction using fine tweezers with a small opening. If that still does not work, make a hollow reed and insert its tip into the ear hole, then seal around it with soft wax so that wind cannot enter along with the reed; then heat it strongly, as often heat comes in this manner as we have described; if it does not produce heat this way, take birdlime, such as that used by birds, and put some on an instrument sharp for this purpose, wrap cotton around it, then press the birdlime against the stone or whatever it may be and heat it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Even if it doesn't come from all these things that we have said, then quickly split the ear before an abscess becomes warm and causes spasm; and the manner of splitting is that you first make the patient lie on their back, and draw out blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear at the place where it hangs down; and let the cut be like a moon shape until you reach the bone, then break it according to your power, and quickly suck out the marrow."
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	"And if it's a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one thin, subtle spatula according to this form:"
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	"and make an incision of that grain. But do not do this if you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with fine forceps and suck out, as we have said, so that the extraction is complete."
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	"Therefore in the water that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sternutation at first, and fill the ear with old cotton. And let them lie on their side where the water is. If it comes out through this, then good; if not, then take many thin and light stones according to the length of your thumb, and heat them a little in the fire; and the patient puts one of these stones into their ear hole, and pushes it with another stone from the other side, and hits it with another stone that is in the ear; and do not cease this hitting of stone on stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will all come out; and if you see that some remains, then take a reed and put one end into the ear, and hold the other end near the fire until that end burns; then repeat with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stones."
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	"In the extraction of a beast, if it is small bodied, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in division; but if it is large bodied that you can feel it, then administer extraction with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear."
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	"In the extraction of earthworms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in division and in treating distillations, and if the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear towards the sun: if there are any worms visible, then extract them with fine forceps, and if none are visible, then take the tube that has this form:"
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	"And let it be narrow underneath and wide above. And put the most subtle end into the ear according to the quantity of suffering of the patient, then suck strongly through the whole tube; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey in coming out, then stuff around the tube with cotton as I said earlier; and if they still do not come out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in killing worms, and you will find them in treating distillations; and thus distil your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:"
