Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	"And let it be of silver or bronze, narrow underneath with one small hole, and above open for distillation; and for pressing inside the distillation there is one well-made instrument of brass for this purpose, and if you wish take one razor and wrap cotton thickly around its point; then throw your oil or juice and what you wish of medicines into the tube, and place the tube in the ear; then insert the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled well out of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little warmed by the fire beforehand before distilling it into the ear; and make sure that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be as good."
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Here is the section on "The Stopping of the Ears" from the medieval French medical treatise "La Grande Chirurgie":
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in its ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to injury of the ear, or flesh grown inside it, and some such blockages occur deep within the ear so that one cannot see them; and sometimes there is one pore missing from the hole, which is clearly visible.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, those that occur deep within the ear, so that one cannot see them, are difficult to treat in many situations, and in these cases it is necessary to put the patient's ear in the sun and look inside: if you see the obstruction appearing, then perform the procedure described below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	"And let it be sharp and cutting both before and behind, entirely full, so that it does not wound the ear; if the protuberance is of flesh born in the body of the ear, hold it with fine forceps, and cut lightly, until all that flesh is removed."
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	"And if the protuberance is deeply within the ear, take one fine razor and heat it a little over the fire, then place it on the body of the ear. If you feel the protuberance which causes the patient pain when listening, pierce lightly, but be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a plug according to the width of the hole, and fill it with Egyptian ointment."
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Continue doing this for a few days until the wound is healed. Then take a plug and moisten it with rose water, powdered vitriol, and place it in the ear. If you see that the ear is swollen, you must remove the plug and insert another one moistened with cerote made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling has gone down; then cure it until it is healthy."
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	"And if there is discharge of blood, dip a sponge in cold water and wring it out, then place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the discharge of blood, which can be found in treatises on distillations."
de la char des papieres	"It seems like you're trying to translate "de la chair des papelards" which means "of the flesh of paper". However, it doesn't make sense in this context. Do you mean something else?"
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	"This is the remedy for those boils that come on moist skin and then dry up: you must stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut them open with a spathaula from their roots; then sprinkle powdered vitriol on the wound."
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	"And if they burst open and bleed, cauterize them with a fine lenticular cautery, and then apply the cautery again after the incision. This is often repeated until nothing remains of their roots; and once they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return."
de la gresle	"Here is the remedy for hailstones:
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	"Many times hailstones come on paper which appear like hail in their shape and hardness, and therefore this disease is called 'hail'; it is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below; its treatment is as follows: beware if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is an easy thing to know; then make the cut wide, then gently scrape each part, then grasp it with pincers, and remove it. If you cannot remove it without piercing a bit of the paper, do not worry about the patient; and if the tear is large, then sew it together, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, no force should be used, for ointments will restore it soon enough."
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	"And if the hail is descending into the ear towards the upper part, invert the paper, and grasp the hail with pincers, and remove it and press on both sides; and if the paper is separated by the incision, do not worry; and when the hail has been removed, rinse the ear with saltwater, and treat the wound until the patient is healed."
de la graisse des eulz	"Regarding eye fat:"
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	"Eye fat is a substance that enters the paper of the eyes from above, and this happens more in children than in adults, and causes great discomfort to their eyes, and they have discharge in the mornings, and cannot look at sunlight because tears quickly come to their eyes; therefore they lie on their backs often, and sleep like that, and their papers under their eyebrows are moist, so much so that the swelling and appearance have been covered by eye fat which opens into the eye. And when you press the wound with your fingers and feel the eye fat between them."
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	"And the manner of treating it is as follows: the patient puts their head in your hand; then take one linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains eye fat on each side, then place it on them; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the eye fat gathers within the circle; then make a cut down the middle of the moistness with a sharp scalpel, making a wound no larger than the one made in the vein of wine; and cut deep into the skin until you reach the eye fat; and in various positions, eye fat comes out of the wound, resembling a piece of white fat."
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	"Therefore, extract it all with one piece of soft cloth between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to stick in the wound, so that you do not harm all the skin up to the eye, lest you injure it."
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	"And if the eye fat does not appear at the beginning of the wound, then slightly widen the wound lightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the wound, and squeeze out the bandages."
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if there are men who grind salt and place it on to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then treat them until they are healed. And if a hot boil appears on the wound, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed."
des poilz des papieres	"Regarding eyebrow hair:"
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	"If eyebrow hairs are born joined together abnormally and entangled, they cause harm to the eyes, and bring about conditions such as constant tearing and softening of the eyebrows and whitening, to the extent that it causes damage to the eyes; and there are four ways to treat it: either by cautery with fire together, or by hot medicine according to what is appropriate before or after cautery, and it can be done either by incision and stitching, or by tweezers, depending on what I will say."
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	"It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the eyebrow away from the eye with your left hand; if it turns well, good. If not, insert a needle with one thread onto it; and let it be near the edge of the eyebrow where the hairs are attached to those hairs, and draw one thread up over the entire eyebrow, and turn it towards the razor; then make an incision downwards under the eyebrow, under the joined hairs, all along the eyelid from the large tear gland to the small one; then extract one thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth underneath the eyebrow, then press on the eyebrow with your finger, like the lid of a mirror, and in any case the figure must be according to the quantity that you see raise the eyebrow which is separated from them."
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	"And if there are those who need to cut off a large quantity of the eyebrow according to how much it has softened; then make an incision all along the eyelid over the two lines that you have marked, starting from the large tear gland up to the small one; and let one of the wounds be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert a pin into one of the corners of the heart, then remove it completely; then join the two lips with a stitch using a needle and one thin thread of wool, and wipe away the blood, and dry up any excess threads on the eyebrows with any sticky substance if you see fit to do so; and if not, pay no mind, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching with drying and constricting things, because the eyebrow grows back at the closing of the wound and its union, but stitching is harmful (as the ancients said), and it is done without pain."
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	"And there is another way: and that is to mark the eyebrow with a figure like the lid of a mirror, as we have said, three threads apart according to the shape shown here:"
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	"Then cut what is above the small forceps evenly according to the shape shown here:"
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	"And if you lack the strength to hold the forceps and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread, and insert it into the figure; and insert another thread next to the large bell, and the second thread next to the small one, and bring them together evenly between your two hands; then raise your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have marked it, as we have described; then bring together the two lips of the wound by sewing, and care for it until it is healed; and if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar softening ointments."
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	"And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted (i.e., curled or raised): in such case, you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching is more complicated in one and the other."
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	"The cure for the canthus (corner of the eye) is as follows: and it is that you fold the paper and make an incision inside according to what I have said, and then make two threads by art, and two fine ties as long as the paper and the width of the spatula; and cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then join one and the other subtly on top of the oil paper, and tightly tie the two canthi from the two parts; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and shrivel and shrink until it becomes smooth."
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	"If it takes a long time, then cut with more force, and care for it until it is healed; and when the wound is healed and the paper is lifted up, the hairs will no longer point upwards; and this is the form of the two canthi that you should make according to this figure and this quantity of length and width:"
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	"The operation is as follows: take a fine needle and thread it with one soft and fine silk thread; then tie the ends together subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm in length; then prepare another fine silk thread briefly, and tie its ends to the first thread; then the patient should put their head on your shoulder, and they should stand near the sun so that the operation is illuminated, for it is a subtle and delicate operation; then take the needle all along the hairline close to the skin, and pierce it into the paper hastily until you draw it up above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the hairline, and put it back into the hairline if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out of the hairline onto the paper with the natural hair."
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	"And if the hairline is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the hairline down all along the thread that you have prepared, until the hairline comes out of the hole above and you can see it with the naked eye; then pull the hairline and the thread together, and close the eye and let it heal for two or three days, until the hair returns to its place and the skin grows over it; and if the hairs are sparse, accompany one long natural eyebrow hair, and lift it up with that one which you leave, so that it is elongated and then lifted up."
de la porriture de l’oil	de la porriture de l’oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" occurs in the eye where decay comes,
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of working on it is that you split open this joint, and separate the lips of it, and put linen wicks inside, and keep it until it heals; and indeed you should not use in its treatment things that dry out and constrict. For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but apply softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose water or aged ale and linseed cooked, and annointments of diachylon melted in some oils, and wrap a wick around it, and that is the treatment for it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you should be careful that it does not heal according to its former shape; and these operations that we have mentioned are only remedies for this illness, so that it does not return in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is beneath it is truly called 'axacrati', and it is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound or split or cauterization or similar things; and the way to work on it is that you take a needle with a doubled thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eyelid towards the right one, so that the threads come out in two places of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above entirely over the needle, and cut it with a broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns as it should, that is good; but if not, then take a razor and place it in the split, and twist the paper, and make two splits inside the paper on its sides; and let the openings of the two splits be at the two angles of the incision you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter called 'gamma' in Greek; then remove that flesh according to the quantity of its sides that is above it from what supports the paper, then join the two separated parts together, and sew them with a wool thread; then apply the treatment for it that we have mentioned concerning softening medicines and wrappings, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or stitches or cauterization, then you must make a full slit under the hair of the paper, and according to what is said above; then open between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters prepare ingenious devices with all their power so that they make the figure return to its natural shape; and the sick person himself, according to what he needs of operations and instruments, in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	de l’acuité de l’oil et du mouvement des esperitz
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this fusion occurs in many men in such a manner that the paper on top is stuck with the white of the eye, and it cannot move nor perform its natural duties, then you must insert the point of a razor underneath the paper, and lift it up; and stretch them with pincers until you reach that which is attached to the subtile spatula, which should not be too dull nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot bear the spatula being too dull nor cutting the eye; and let your incision be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all of this assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye they make salt water, and lift it with fresh water, and collyrium. Then put a linen cloth between the paper and the eye, and put on the eye wool moistened with egg albumen. And after the third day use collyrium and healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the corner of the eye is in two ways: it is nerve-like and similar to one hard skin, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles moist white congealed blood. When you touch it with iron and try to grasp it with pincers, you cannot do so; both these appearances begin near the large tear duct, and gradually grow little by little until they cover the whole sight and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: The patient should put their head in your hand, then open their eyes. Lift the paper with your hand, then grasp the corner with small pincers and stretch it up. Then take a needle, and on it place one horse, cow, or ox hair, and a strong thread. Double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the corner, piercing it entirely with the needle, and tie the corner with a thread and stretch it upwards. Then scrape along the entire length of the hair the side of the corner that covers the pupil and the iris up to the head. Then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct using the subtle spatula and small forceps, leaving the natural flesh in the tear duct so that the incision does not interfere with the normal flow of tears. Sometimes the corner is stretched only with the needle and thread, as we have said before. Then scrape it gently with the soft spatula, which has this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure that the spatula does not touch the delicate flesh and damage it, nor should the pupil be pierced. After the incision, sprinkle a little crushed selbroit into the eye, and apply collyrium made of lead ore, leaving it overnight. Then treat it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerve-filled,
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully raise the nail above it, and if you see that it does not thin out nor the reason press thereupon, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red ochre ground together, and stop up the eye until the next day; then recommence the same work according to this very same procedure, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything opposes you in the eye, such as a hot sore, then apply milk and first cure the hot sore until it is healed, then recommence the operation just as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid harms the eye greatly, then suspend it with a needle and cut off part of it but not all of it so that tears do not come from there; then distill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows upon the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	There are some men upon whom sometimes red flesh grows and covers the pupil and sticks to the papillae and turns towards the forehead, and it seems like a carbuncle; and this is the operation: let the sick person put his head in your hand, then let him open his eyes, and coil all that flesh with suitable hooks and hold it firmly; then cut off the first layer of flesh, and keep on cutting right down to the end, taking care not to injure the eye during the operation; and the incision should be like the one we have described for the nail, but smaller, like the forceps used to extract a tooth, as shown in this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, then fill the eye with ground barley or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines into it, and put cotton soaked in egg albumen on the eyelid to secure it from a hot sore; and if anything remains there, and the skin becomes hot again, and you suspect a hot sore, then leave the eye alone and treat the sore with things that cool heat; then return to your operation until it is healed, and do likewise for all flesh that grows in the eye in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless you should alleviate the cure of each weak eye by the natural way; and in case of an accident, operate with iron; and do not put your hand into any operation until you see that these members can withstand this operation.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The veins are red that cover the eye and hinder its sight and weaken the eye every day. Therefore it is necessary at first to examine whether the eye in which the vein appears is healthy, and if there is no other visible disease besides the vein; then coil it in this manner: command the sick person to put his head in your hand, then suspend these veins with a hook according to your skill, and the hook should be fine and doubled according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And there should be two hooks at intervals of one finger's breadth on the same body according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully tie those veins and squeeze out the blood hour by hour until you see the veins move away from the eye; and ensure that you do not cut the eye with the points of the spatumiles, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your task so that you only touch those veins; and when you have done this, then distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains of the seed.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect all of this in that hour, then apply a plaster to the eye made from soothing substances for eye pain, and leave it on for several days until the pain is eased and an aposteme is formed, then resume according to this method until it is healed; and this is the form of the treatment.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls a fistula "arissati": when you heal it with cautery and medicine that is very hot according to what I have said before, but it is not healed, then there is a device in it such that you must cut on the aposteme where it should die, and remove all of the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then take all of the instruments that are needed for this task; and they are called "aspre chief", and should be made of red iron with one sharp point like a file as it is in its present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the sharp point of the instrument on the bone that is corrupted, then twist it between your fingers and press your hand gently until you know that all of the corruption has been removed; and do this several times, then restore the wound with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is closed and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is healed, but after forty days it does not renew itself nor form an aposteme, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed. But if this is not the case, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to its original opening in the nostril according to this method: And you must uncover the bone a second time with iron and hot medicines, and when it is exposed take one spit according to this form, and let the point of the iron be at three angles, and let the stick be tapered to its head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the ear, and move your hand away from the eye one pace, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the wind entering if they keep their hand on their nose; and then return to the place of dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and the place hardens, then the matter goes to the nose; so it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens fully in all directions, and there is no obstruction to the nose nor diminution, then you must bandage the patient; then wash it, then place cupping glasses or leeches without wounding to suck; then put on the eye a plaster made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye, and cover it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, and double each one into four, and then place them on top of each other according to how much the eye needs; then strain it with a firm bandage, and begin again with the cupping glasses to suck without wounding; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the plaster melts, you must remove it frequently; then remove the plaster after the day and night, and if you see that the eye is healing, that's good; if not, begin again with the emplastrum and bandages and plaster and cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the prolapse of the rectum
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the prolapse of the rectum comes and opens, and paper comes out like grains of resin, and it is horrible to see; therefore if you see it happen, the operation is as follows: take a needle and insert it into the root of the part below until it reaches the part above, then take another needle with one double thread from the part of the anus; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to its position; then tie the loop of the double thread around one part of the rectum and strain it well, then remove the needle and place on the wound linen moistened in egg albumen; and let it remain until the prolapse comes with the rectum, then treat the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the rectum on each side with a band of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has great protrusion, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from far behind the eye, and draw out the moist albumen and allow the eye to descend, and enter immediately; then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eyebrow
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but the eyebrow that is gathered upon the eye, appearing like descending water, and this is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the operation is as follows: make the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and hold it until you see the eyebrow rise up to your eyes; then let it be inserted and do not allow it to descend nor become disorganized the light, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the eyebrow is not arranged as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and cut through the cornea tissue one point along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown until the eyebrow comes out; and when it has come out, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and mixed with honey, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have already described the types of waters in the eye and how to pierce them according to their nature; so do it accordingly. You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands away from sunlight, and tie the healthy eye tightly closed with a strong bandage; then place the paper for the eye on your left hand if the eye is left-handed, or on your right hand if the eye is right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right-handed; then place the tip of the instrument near the crown along the thickness of a hair at the angle of the eye on the side of the minor lachrymal duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" gently, and turn your hand so that it pierces through the angle of the eye, and feel that almagda has reached the empty space; and the measurement of the almagda passage should be equal to the length from the pupil to the end of the blackness; then you will see the bone in the paper through the transparency of the cornea tissue, then place the instrument where the water is, then express it little by little, one way after another. If the water flows out now, the patient will see before them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a brief rest, if the water rises up again through the second way, insert the wick with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise up, then remove almagda gently by turning your hand little by little; then place a drop of rosewater into the eye and wipe it from within. Then put on the outside of the eye cotton wool moistened in rose oil and egg white, and tie with the healthy eye. We, and those of our time, also place common breadcrumbs mixed with egg white on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then you should take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunctiva and do not go too deep, but make a fine cut, then insert almagda as we have described; and at the completion of the operation prepare for the patient a comfortable bed in a dark room where he should sleep on his back for two days, avoiding all movements, eating light foods, and not moving his head to the right or left, and tie him according to his condition until the third day. Then untie him in the same dark room, test his sight, show him some objects, then retie him until the seventh day; but do not perform this operation during the period of cure or immediately after the incision, rather do it beforehand because the water rises up quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If apostemes occur within the seventh day, untie the eye and apply remedies for soothing aposteme; when it has calmed down, then uncover the eye and cover it with an ointment made of rosewater for a few days, keeping him in the same dark room. Then gradually leave the house and return to his usual activities; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	"And one came to us who was from Jerusalem, who told us that in their land they use almagda to pierce through, into which water is sucked, but nonetheless I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a novel thing."
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	"And these are the likenesses of the shapes of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and let them be made of pure silver:"
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	"And let their fronts be of this same subtlety, and the back have three sharp corners."
de la char sor le neis	"of the flesh off the nearest"
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes there are born or close adjacent diverse flesh, from which some seem like scorpions with many feet; and there are such ones where the flesh is colored blackish, and there is soft flesh of good color. Therefore, in that one of these fleshes which is soft, and not blackish, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, drop oil on those fleshes, and rub it in; then scrape off what you can support with the subtly sharp spatula of one side until you know that all that flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be scraped off, open it with one of the light, subtle instruments until nothing remains; and if it swells up or becomes inflamed, then treat it as necessary. And if they are malignant ulcers, rush to cauterize them so that the blood is stanched and all the flesh is removed, then pour on them immediately oil and wine or vinegar
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nostril is open and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is clear; and if moisture does not reach as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so do not use the instrument to cut: therefore you must take one thread of flax a little thick, and wet it with hot water, and place between each knot some myrrh or less; and the patient should hold the end of the thread in his nostril with some force, and draw it back while smelling until it enters the mouth. Children at school often do this, and it is easy for whoever wants to perform it. Then grasp one end of the thread that comes out through the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and gently pull each knot towards you as they are on the thread. Do this until you know that the knots have rotted all the flesh. Then remove the thread, wipe off the blood, moisten it in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nostril as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded all remaining flesh. Then place a plaster of lead on the nostril for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them. This is the form of the instrument used to purge the head, through which oils and medicines are distilled
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp like a tube with the conduit also; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full in order to purge the head; and let it have many holes at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nostril
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there appears on the nostril a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large enough to be clearly seen; therefore you must cut it at its beginning, and remove all of its root, then apply cauterization or burning medicine to it. But if it is delayed until it is large, beware if it is hard, of dark color, and poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted aposteme. For when you cut it, great mischief comes upon the patient. And if the aposteme is soft to the touch, not dark colored, and you see that it can be completely cut, then empty out the nostril without fear, and cure it afterwards with drying and restricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nostril is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when inflammation continues into one of these cartilage parts, it does little good in most people. Therefore, whenever this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together with a stitch, then heal it until it is healed. And if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must scrape away all the edges of their skin until they are clean, then join the two lips together with a stitch and bind them, then sprinkle dragon's blood powder and crushed incense upon it. Then place a piece of plaster of fir or another strong plaster upon the powders, and leave it on until it sticks by itself, then heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is as follows: you can join the wound together using needles, as we have said in the case of abdominal suturing; or with thread, as I have already explained to you.
des apostemes des levres	Of the apostemes on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have hard apostemes on their lips resembling grains of wheat, some small and others large. Therefore you must turn the lips back and cut along each one with a knife, then grasp it with forceps and cut it in every part; afterwards fill the space after the incision with ground vitriol until the blood is stanched; then leave it alone, and cure it afterwards with drying things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there appears on the gums attached flesh, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore you must hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, then let the bow or blood flow. Then place ground vitriol or other restricting and drying powders upon the wound; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: for it will not return afterwards; these are the forms of the instruments used to cut it.
des sordens	Of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes the teeth in the head are joined together, inside the mouth between the gums, with rough and sharp scabs; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green and wormy, so that corruption reaches the gum and the teeth smell bad. Therefore you must make the patient sit between your hands, their chin in your lap, and scrape the teeth or scabs until there is nothing left of them. And do likewise with blackness and greenness and yellowness and other stains until they are cleaned; and if what was there at first is removed, it is good; but if not, then recommence on the second day and the third until you have everything scraped; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping according to what the task shows, because those used for scraping teeth from the front are different from those used for scraping between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating a toothache, you must delay extracting it as long as possible because this should never be done except in the highest degree of necessity.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to have a tooth extracted, you must be certain of the aching tooth. Many times the pain leaves the patient and they think it is in the healthy tooth, and have the good tooth pulled out; but nevertheless the pain does not depart by this means because we have often seen these same fools do so. And when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then scrape around the tooth on all sides with a sharp spatula to guard the gum from all parts. Then move it with your fingers or with fine forceps little by little until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the forceps; and let the patient's chin rest in your lap between your knees, and keep yours still so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extract the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these tools and gently insert it on either side, and with the lever use it as you have done before. And if the tooth is pierced and stuck in place, then you must fill the hole with wadding where the perforation is; and with fine forceps grasp it tightly so that it does not break while extracting; and one must work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care not to break it, and if a part remains and returns to the patient through the malice of the root cause them greater pain than before. And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeons who out of haste and recklessness sometimes break the jawbone, nor do they follow the methods we have described; but often bring about serious illness due to remnants of roots left behind or due to the jawbone being broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, then wash the place with wine or sage tea and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, then fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if that does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the tools with which one should extract teeth first are those with long points and thick handles so that they do not double over when pulling the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large members so they do not bend during traction, and made of well-smithied iron, and toothed for holding movement.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during traction, you must put on the spot moistened cotton with butter for one or two days until the spot is softened. Then insert the pliers called "algefri" whose jaws resemble those of a bird's beak; and let them be shaped inside like a rasp, this is its shape
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these pliers, you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root and place the tool called "althali", namely, the crowbar; this is its shape
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break. If the root jumps out with this, that is good; if not, help yourself with all the tools, of which their shapes come hereafter
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this tool that has two handles, this is its shape
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools that are in front of the root of the teeth, and this tool that resembles large pliers; this is its shape
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these tools be strong so that they cannot break. Know that there are many dental tools and also others not counted. And the wise and subtle master finds his own tool according to what his works and the illness dictate for him, because there are such illnesses where ancient masters did not teach any tool due to their diversity of today. And if he breaks neither cartilage nor other bones, then he seeks among the tools that are necessary, which I have told you about, and helps himself with gestures; this is its shape
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not slip away but can grasp and remove it. Then restore the place with suitable medicines for that location. And if there is decay in the bone and it is small, then remove it with all these tools
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to their natural course and are misshapen in form, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is close behind the other tooth and not in its proper place, so that one cannot be placed or polished: then rasp it. And if it is next to the tooth, take this tool whose shape is like a small beak and made of iron with a sharp edge at the top
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And strike the tooth gently with your hand every day to harden it and so that you do not move the others. And if it is visible so that it can be polished, then use this kind of file whose shape is like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.
