And it is also like the file used to make needles. And gently file the tooth little by little every day so that it does not move too much and then level it at the end with any plane or scraper. And if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then file down its sharpness until it is smooth so that it does not hurt the tongue nor interfere with speech
quant li dent lochent	When teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When front teeth are loose, either from an injury or a fall, and the person cannot bite into what they eat without them falling out, and you have treated them with medicines that tighten but it is ineffective; then they must be secured with a gold thread, because silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes. And let the wire be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth. If you see that the teeth need to be aligned, take the wire and a double-bend pliers, and place it between two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the loose teeth, one or more of them, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side. Then start wrapping the wire again up to where you started, holding your hand steadily and gently so that they do not move. And let your loop be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut off the ends of the wire with pliers and bend them together and place them between the healthy tooth, making sure it does not hurt the tongue. Then leave it as tight as possible for as long as it can last. If it becomes loose or the wire breaks, then reinforce it with another wire. It will remain like this for its entire life, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of two healthy teeth and two loose ones, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place little by little, as we have said. And only let those who are wise and careful handle it, and sometimes the shape of a cow's bone tooth is made and placed where the defect is, and it is secured with wire as we have described, and it remains there for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the frenulum of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes there is this frenulum that comes naturally from under the tongue at birth or as an accident from a healed wound. The procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth and hold their head steady while they raise their tongue. Then cut the thick nerve frenulum with scissors until the tongue is free from its attachment, being careful not to cut too deep so as not to damage the artery underneath. If there is hardness or a nodule present, which indicates a healed wound, use the thumbnail and cut it open with scissors. Afterward, rinse the area with rosewater and sage or cold water, then place a linen cloth under the tongue each night to prevent the wound from closing up again. If bleeding occurs, sprinkle powdered vitriol on the affected area. If bleeding continues, cauterize the wound with a lentiginous cautery, which is suitable for this purpose. Then treat it with other remedies until it heals completely.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it has a pale or black or hard appearance and the person does not feel it, do not touch it at all, because it is a chancre. And if it appears to be leaning towards a blenorrhoea, with moisture present, then scrape it off with an onion and make a subtle incision with a fine spatula and deliver it on both sides. If bleeding occurs from your operation, sprinkle powdered vitriol over it until it stops, then return to your operation and remove all the furuncle. Then rinse the area with sage and celandine and treat it with other remedies until it is completely healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	On swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	"Occasionally, bubbles called 'godath' appear in the throat, which are properly called tonsils. When you treat them as we have described earlier, if they are not healed, take note: If they are hard swellings with a dark color, do not touch them with iron. And if they are red and have a large root, do not touch them with iron either, especially for the flow of blood; but wait until they are ripe, and then you can cut them, or they will burst on their own. If they are white and have a fine root, prepare the instrument to prick, but first check if the swelling is calm and peaceful. Then make the patient sit facing the sun, with his head in your lap, and open his mouth; take the tool between your hands and press the tongue down against it, as shown here. Let it be made of silver or refined bronze, like a knife:"
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	"If you press the tongue against this tool and see the swelling, take the needle and insert it into the tonsil, then push it in further than you can. Then pull out some of the cloth with it, and cut with the tool, which has the shape of a forceps. Be careful though, as their tips are curved inward and they are very sharp. They are made of iron or steel:"
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if you do not have this tool present, use tongs, which have this shape:"
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	"And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other. And when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same manner. After the incision, the patient should gargle with warm water and sage, and if there is bleeding, he should gargle with water or cooked pomegranate rinds or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops. Then treat it until it is healed. And sometimes other swellings appear in the throat besides the two tonsils; cut these as you would the two tonsils."
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	"And I treated a woman who had a swelling that was born inside her throat, specifically one small swelling. It had grown so large that it almost completely closed off her throat, and she could not breathe or eat or drink, and would have died if left like that for one or two days. The swelling had already gone through both openings of the neck, with two veins having been placed in them. I hurried at once, inserted a needle into one opening, pushed it in, and cut off a large portion of the flesh. Then I did the same on the other side of the neck, opened her mouth, and pressed down her tongue. After that, I inserted the needle into this swelling and cut off a part of it, from which only a little blood came out. This way, the throat passage was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water then wine. But I kept cutting at this swelling for a long time, as it kept growing back and filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large. Then I tied it off and cauterized it inside her throat: That way, it stopped growing. And I left these parts, and I do not know what God did with her afterwards."
de l’uve	"of the eye"
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	"When the eyelid descends onto the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called 'perpendicular'; but if it is below, thick, and rounded, it is called an 'eyelid'. When it is treated as we have said in its division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the surrounding inflammation has subsided, but it remains subtle, then you must cut it; and that which is rounded together and not long; and if it is red or dark colored, then you should avoid incising it. For there is great danger to the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its manner of being inflamed and its length, make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then insert the awl into the eyelid, and draw it downwards, and cut through one or two instruments that I have mentioned in the incising of two grains. And you must not cut more than what is beyond its natural limit; for if you cut more, you will harm the voice and speech. And after the incision, use those things that we have said in the incising of two grains, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient fears being cut, then you should use an instrument for cauterization according to his fear. And the manner of cautery is with boiling water. And let the patient put his head on your hand, and then press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and mix it with boiling water, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and this is its form:"
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Et ait ou chief une cheveure où om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d'une cuillier, et met l'estrument a tout la medicine sus l'uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu'ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l'uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d'une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l'envoloupe sus certain estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l'estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s'aerde sus l'uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l'essue entor l'uve, de couton embut en burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arrosez d'aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu'il soit sanez."
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	"This cure is more powerful than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and mugwort and similar herbs, and assemble them all together in one pot. And put a hot ember into it, and let it boil well; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be one iron instrument made like this:"
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	"And it should be made of silver or brass, and one of the two ends should be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the tube until the eye is mortified. Then repeat this often until the eye dries up. And take care not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot boil, for many things can happen; and do not do it except when the boil is declining in heat. And if this instrument is not present, then take a tube and put an egg shell at its end so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the egg shell will not let the vapor harm the mouth, and this is good treatment together."
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	"Many times there is a bone stuck in the throat or spine of a fish, or some other thing. Therefore you should extract what you can see and press the tongue with the instrument towards the sun until you see it move. And what you cannot see but is stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge or a piece of flannel or a piece of lettuce root or a small piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it. And when it comes to the right place, it will stick, and then you can pull it out again. And if it does not come out from what we have said, then take one instrument made of lead in this shape:"
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	"And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can enter the throat more easily, and have the head raised high. And take care not to touch the epiglottis lest it close completely, nor push the bone inside. And it is better for the patient himself to insert the instrument in order to know where the thing is stuck; then he should draw it out gently with the instrument until it comes out."
de la sansue de la gorge	"de la sansue de la gorge"
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the blood is treated, as I mentioned in the division, by the remedy of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then examine the patient's throat towards the sun, after pressing the tongue with the instrument I told you about. And if you see the blood, then draw it out with a small forceps, or with fine tweezers suitable for this purpose. And if these are not suitable, then take a heated awl and place it in the patient's throat, then apply the tip of the awl to the blood vessel and do this repeatedly. And if the patient coughs all day long, then take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth, pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with assfetide, using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye. Do this many times, for it will fall without troubling. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take one pot with live coals inside, and let the bottom be covered by a pierced cloth in the middle, and place the pipe of the instrument through that hole; then throw your fumigation into it, and the patient puts the end of the tube into their mouth, closing the mouth so that no smoke escapes but reaches all the way to the blood. And the blood will fall now, and if it does not, then begin again with the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst and eat salty foods and almonds, and do not drink any water; and thus it will be necessary for the blood to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats blood is like this: when it can be seen, resembling curved tweezers for entering into the throat; and it resembles a crow's beak, and has sharpness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot let go. And here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter on Abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many abscesses are similar to one another, as is mentioned later in this book about various cases described here and there, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two kinds of them: one is identical to its appearance and consists of moist tissue. The second kind differs according to the location on the body where it occurs because abscesses at the top are different from those at the bottom, and those that occur near flesh are different from those that occur in joints. Each type has its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	"And it is not proper to pierce boils until they are completely ripe; and there are some which must be pierced when they are hard, even if they do not ripen completely, like boils near joints. For when a boil appears near a joint, and one waits until it is entirely putrid, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, causing contraction in that limb. If the boil is near the main member, and you delay piercing until it has fully ripened, it will harm the main member; but if it is near the fundament, pierce it before it has fully ripened. Do not pierce a hard boil without digestion being completed, except for one near the fundament which might otherwise become deeply buried and create a fistula, making healing difficult in the long term."
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you must know the hour for piercing a boil that has ripened completely, and this is when the pain subsides, and the fever departs, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the bursting and hardening at the top of the boil, and other signs; and you must make the puncture where the boil hangs down most or where it opens more readily, and the puncture should be long like a reed. If the boil is on the hands or feet, or in joints near nerves and arteries, or in any flat place without wrinkle."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	"In those that are pendent, according to the member involved. And when a boil is in a fleshy place, it's better to wait until it has fully ripened before piercing it, as we have said. For if you pierce it beforehand, the body of the venom will be elongated and filled with much filth; and perhaps the lips and depth of it become hardened. And there are some boils that should be pierced according to the width of the body, depending on what the member needs. And you must make small punctures in small boils, and large punctures in big ones, with many slits according to the size of the boil; and there are such boils where one should press down with a heart-shaped piece of cloth, and cover it when it becomes like a penny and is softened. And there are those that are cut into three angles, and there are some that are cut like the leaf of a mulberry tree, like the boils on the shins; and there are some where one makes a round cut, and other cuts with similar incisions."
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Those that have no head, like a soft superficial boil, it's necessary to pierce them flatly; and when the boil is large and has swollen greatly, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at once, but only draw out some of it; then plug the boil until the next day, then draw some more out again; do this many times gradually, until all the pus comes out. Especially if the patient is weak in strength, or pregnant woman, or small children, or old decrepit men. For sometimes the heart jumps with the issuing of the pus, which might suddenly kill the patient without you noticing. Therefore be careful with this chapter, and when you have pierced your boil, examine the wound to see if it is small; and if it's a clean cut, then apply lint made of linen or old cotton; but if it's a large boil with many punctures, then put in each one a piece of lint so that they touch each other. And if you've cut off some skin from the boil and removed it, then fill up the space with dry cotton or linen rag without moisture, and leave it for three days; then remove it, and apply ointment until it's healed."
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, then bring cold water and aisen, and moisten one piece of cloth, and put it on the bleeding area many times. And if the bleeding persists, then apply treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in many places in this book, and if it's in wintertime, and the area where the boil is very nervous, then you should put moistened lint and cloths in wine and hot oil; and if it's in summertime, and the area is fleshy, then you should put on moistened cloths in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for three days, as we have said; then remove the boil and cleanse and dress it, as it should be done, until it's healed."
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	"And this is what one must know universally about the treatment of boils: I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of boils, and here is that chapter."
des soros	"boils"
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	"Boils on the head cause small boils that are similar to those in the skin of a hen's egg membrane, and there are many similarities between them. Some are fatty and some have moisture like blisters; others are hard and bony at the cutting site, with no doubt that an artery opposes it. The procedure for cutting is to use any instrument called 'entromissoire', from which its shape comes later, whatever it contains. For if it contains moisture, cut it lengthwise on top. And when the moisture has been emptied, scrape it clean without leaving any skin that contained that moisture, because it quickly fills up again if you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; if not, in water and wine, and fill the wound and leave it overnight; and repeat this process on the second and third day until you know for sure that no more liquid remains; then dress the wound with suitable ointment until it heals. And do likewise for boils that contain fat, cutting them lengthwise, scraping off all the skin, and putting all your care into drawing out the fatty matter; if an artery opposes this, proceed as I have told you later. Do likewise for hard boils that are bony at the cutting site and in their dressing, as I have said."
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	"And when cutting into hard and moist boils, it is easier because they contain little blood. And there are some of these boils on the head that have no moisture, such as those I cut off from an old woman's head; I found the boil to be like a hard, sharp, and white stone, and could not be broken; if one had tried to strike it with anything, it would have made just as much wound as a stone. In other boils that come on the head, especially those that appear on children's heads and at the roots of the ears, keep opening them every day until they can drain out all the pus, and treat them as they should be treated."
des scrophules	"scrophules"
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	"Abscesses often occur at the neck, under the armpits, and on the limbs, and sometimes appear elsewhere on the body. They are numerous and varied in shape. Some contain moisture, while others are malignant and refuse to heal. Choose one that appears healthy to touch, is similar in color to the skin, moves freely from all sides and is not hard near the nerves of the neck or the artery or vein. It should not be deep. Cut it open from above and scrape its edges clean. If necessary, use tweezers to hold the lips of the wound open, as we have described for abscesses on the head. Remove it bit by bit, making sure you do not cut into a nerve or vein, and avoid using a spatula or scalpel that cuts too deeply."
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	"And if you cut into the vein or artery and cannot proceed, apply powdered vitriol or other blood-stopping powders to the wound, then bandage it tightly. Leave it until the abscess is reduced and the wound begins to rot. Once the bleeding has stopped, return to your task until completed. Then check your dominant hand for any small remaining scabs, cut them off and clean them out. If there is a large vein at the root of the scab, do not cut into it but tie it with a strong doubled thread and let it fall without harm. Then dress the wound with cotton wool soaked in Egyptian ointment."
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if you remove the entire scab, you must bring together the two lips of the wound and stitch them closed, since there may be no excess flesh remaining due to the size of the scab. You must then cut into the root of it and draw out pus, then stitch it up as we have said. Those scabs that contain excess flesh should be pierced where they appear fullest; pierce it in this way, depending on its location, then apply tents with ointment and similar materials so that it rots completely. Once the wound is clean, dress it with warm ointment until it heals."
de squinance	"Squinting"
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	"The ancients spoke of the cutting of the throat, but I have never seen it done in our land, and that is what their writings say."
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	"For those who squint, the epiglottis must be avoided; no help is to be given by this means, because all veins and arteries of the sick person are in the mouth or throat."
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	"When the disease is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis in order to avoid suffocation."
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	"It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we do so below three or four small incisions, or through a small transverse incision between two circles, or through the quantity of the slit of the soft palate, but not in the cartilage."
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	"These locations are suitable for cutting the epiglottis because there is no flesh present, and the vessels are long."
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	"And if the patient is fearful, you must stretch out the skin of the throat on one side as far as possible, then cut through the flesh until you reach the channel. Avoid the blood vessels, if any are visible, and then cut the soft palate as we have said."
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	"And it is demonstrated by the section of the throat artery that blood flows out through the broken point, and by the loss of voice."
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	"Leave the wound open for a while."
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when the danger of strangulation has passed, bring together the two lips of the wound in the chest and stitch them closed without including the cartilage. Then apply medications that promote the growth of flesh until it is healed."
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	"Albucasis says that one should not perform this procedure until the throat is completely blocked, the patient is judged to be near death, and the fault lies with the air passages."
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	"Therefore, cut the epiglottis when the patient cannot breathe and breathes through the wound, thereby avoiding death."
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	"And for this reason, the ancients commanded that the wound be left open until the worst of the disease has passed, which usually takes three or four days."
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	"And then they commanded that the wound be stitched up and dressed until it was healed."
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	"And now I will tell you what I have seen."
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	"I saw a young woman take a knife and stab it into her throat, cutting part of the channels of the artery;"
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	"And I was called to treat her, but found her already dead."
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	"I examined the wound and found that there was blood coming from it, and I realized that she had not cut any vein or artery except for the throat, and air was escaping through the wound."
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	"I quickly stitched up the wound and dressed it until it healed;"
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	"and the young woman was only left with a hoarse voice, but she recovered afterwards."
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	"So I say that one should not fear cutting the epiglottis."
de la grosse gorge	"Of the enlarged throat"
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	"This hernia of the throat is called 'goitre,' and it appears as a large swelling with a yellowish color, and is very common in women;"
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	"and it occurs in two ways: naturally or accidentally; the natural kind has no cause."
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	"And accidents occur in two ways: one resembles fatty tissue and the other resembles an aposteme that comes from an artery;"
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	"and there is no fear in this case, except for the small one, and it is proven and searched through the whole introitus;"
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	"If you find it like a knot of fat and not attached to any vein, cut it like a fatty tumor and remove it completely if possible;"
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	"And search carefully around it, dress the wound as necessary until it is perfectly healed."
des nous	"Of fatty tumors"
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	"There are many kinds of fatty tumors, all of which I will describe their similarities;"
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	"And now it is necessary for me to explain the difference between a nodule and an exostosis."
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	"I say that an exostosis is hot and febrile until the inflammation has passed, and the putrefaction is complete. Then the fever and heat subside."
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	"With a nodule there is no heat, fever or pain, and it contains fatty tissue enclosed in its own sac and has the same color as the skin. It begins like a bubble and grows larger;"
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	"And there are two types of them: fatty or moist, and most have the colors that I mentioned in the division."
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	"When you come to treat a nodule, it is necessary to first examine and explore the entire introitus with an instrument called 'intromitto'"
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	"And the manner of inquiring into the apostemes of the nose is that you take the moistest part you find in the aposteme, and turn your fingers little by little until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the aposteme."
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	"Then remove the trocar, and be careful about what spills out."
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	"If running moisture is corrupt, whatever its color may be, then drain it as I have said for other apostemes;"
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	"And if no moisture comes after the trocar, know that it is hard, so cut it in cross shape and take it with forceps, and scrape it lightly from each side and watch the skin where it lies as you pull it out cleanly with the nut;"
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	"And if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out in pieces until nothing remains."
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	"For if anything remains, the boil will recur many times;"
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	"and if a little remains and the skin grieves you, then fill the wound with some caustic waters and strain the wound, and put on soothing plasters for hot boils, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;"
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	"And if the boil is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it as one that enters flesh."
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	"And if the veins beat against you or otherwise, hurry and fill the wound with powdered vitriol, and let it lie for two or three days until the wound rots, and then rest the ebullition of the blood; then return to cauterize what remains of the boil."
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	"Here are the shapes of the trocar instruments, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small. And there are four square ones called 'albaret', and one called 'breb'. There are also three kinds for surrounding fistulous boils;"
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	"and they are also like the needles used to cut sorcerers' knots, and are made of citrine brass or iron or silver. Those that are gold colored are worth more, but those with black plating are more precious for encircling fistulous cavities;"
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	"And there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes."
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	"The shapes of the forceps are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small. And there are also forceps with two cavities of three kinds;"
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	"And there are forceps with three cavities that are also of three kinds; and there are forceps with two cavities and forceps with one cavity only, which are of three kinds. All these are necessary in their place."
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	"The tips of these instruments used for cutting are sharp. There are some that cut only on one side, which are used to excoriate boils so that the vein or nerve is not injured;"
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	"And among these trocars are the alembics used in hands so that the sick person does not perceive them at the opening of boils;"
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	"And there are three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see;"
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	"And they should only be used in thin flesh areas, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar places;"
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	"And sometimes another small instrument is used, resembling fistulous scoops, according to this shape, with which blood is wiped away:"
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is placed sometimes at the location where veins and arteries are cut, and sometimes they are made according to this large shape:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	"Sometimes the breasts of some men become enlarged when they begin to decay, so that they resemble women's breasts;"
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	"And remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them should follow this shape from line b to g:"
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"Then excoriate the fat and fill the wound with healing salve, then bring together the two lips of the wound to suture, and care for it until it is healed;"
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	"And if the breast hangs down and is softened by its size like a woman's, then cut it in two above at two similar incisions;"
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	"So that one holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger part contains the smaller according to this shape from line b to g;"
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"Then excoriate the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and bring together what we have said about suturing and powders, and do whatever is necessary for healing until it is healed;"
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	"And if it is not healed, or the incision was not made properly because the patient did not want to rest or because of bleeding, then you should fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive oil;"
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	"And leave it until it consumes the remainder and the fat, then heal it until it is healed."
des apostemes des asselles	"Regarding boils in the armpits"
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"These boils that appear under the arms are usually hard scrophulæ with corners, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	"Therefore those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape from line b to g:"
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when all the bone that is in the boil has been emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and heal it with appropriate ointment until it is healed."
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	"And if the boil resembles a scrofula, then cut it like we have said for incisions of scrofulæ, and if the wound contracts bone, then bring about cautery as we have said before."
de la routure de l’artere	"Regarding the rupture of an artery"
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	"When an artery ruptures and the skin over it is closed, boils often appear. The same happens with an enlarged vein and a boil;"
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	"And if one recognizes this when it is due to the artery, then the boil will be long and deep;"
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	"And when you feel it with your fingers, you will sense one instrument; and when it is due to the vein, then it appears thin and flat;"
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	"And it would be foolish to cut this boil, especially when it appears under the arms and angles or in the neck or many other places, where it is very large;"
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	"It is therefore necessary to avoid cautery with iron and also the one who is at the head. When it is due to arterial swelling, cut through the skin above the long boil;"
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	"Then open the incision at the corners and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed;"
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	"Then place one needle underneath it and pierce it through to the other side, and tie the artery with a doubled thread in two places according to what I have taught you regarding the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;"
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	"Then mark the place between the two ligatures with an introverter until the blood flows out of it and cut open the boil;"
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	"Then apply treatment as in other bone wounds, until the ligature falls off;"
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then apply ointment suitable for it until it is clean.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	"If an abscess forms due to cutting into the vein, then you must carefully remove all that you can feel from the abscess throughout its skin."
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	"Then insert the needle underneath the spot where you hold your hand, and make it pierce through, with one doubled thread, so that you can pull it out from the other side."
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	"Then tie up the abscess as I have told you, or bind one of its two ends with both threads."
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	"And if you doubt that the threads do not go through, then insert another needle with one thread under all of the abscess at the incision point of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places."
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	"Then cut off the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut off the excess of skin and leave what is tied."
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then put a wet cloth moistened with wine and oil on it, then apply dressings of compresses and ointments until it heals."
des apostemes des ners	"Abscesses of the nerves"
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	"So just like abscesses come from the artery and vein when they are pierced or by excessive work, abscesses also come to nerves when they are wounded, and similar things."
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	"And these occur more often in the joints, hands and feet where there are articulations, and this is a painful abscess with the color similar to that of skin, and it has many different sensations without pain."
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	"And when it is squeezed strongly, the sick person feels pain, but it is not deep in the flesh, but rather under the skin."
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	"And it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor below nor above, and one must not cut with iron an abscess that is on a joint, for fear of causing contraction."
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	"And those that are on the head or forehead feel the skin being stretched at the scalp."
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	"If the abscess is small, take it with tongs and cut off its root."
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is large, suspend it with the pincers and scrape it off, then lift it up and join the wound together with stitches, and dress it until it heals."
des grosses boces pendans	"On large hanging pouches"
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Once it happens in bellies and nowhere else,
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw one man who had two on his belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, they were white, they had a fine root, and they were newly split, and moisture flowed continually from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found that one was 18 ounces and the other 6. The effect of the incision is such that if you look at it you can tell if the patient is moist; the color of the flesh is white and moist with a fine root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the cut is wide and you are not in his presence with a cautery ready at the fire. For often there comes too great a flow of blood during cutting, and if the blood gushes out then quickly apply the cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision from the iron, then take one well-made thread of linen, and tie the flesh as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	And then tighten it, and do not cease pulling the linen thread until it cuts through the flesh, and each time cut without labor. And if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting even for the belly, but you can still well cut half of it;
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cauterize it so that it does not return. Then heal the wound, and make sure you do not cut the gland which is of fox-color and poor sense and full of milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an enchanted aposteme, and I will come to the cure of cancer later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or fissure of syphilis, and it is on the belly and in some cases it happens with other ulcers, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as has been said before, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is due to the ulcer of syphilis and from the outlet of the bowel, then the color of the aposteme resembles the color of the flesh, and it is light without pain and has various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the outlet of the intestines, then it is more diverse. And when you press it with your fingers it disappears and then returns. And sometimes it is hard and enlarged greatly at the entrance of the bath and from intense labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is light and opens well when you press it with your hand without constraining. And if it is due to blood, then the aposteme appears large and hard with these signs, and it is fixed according to its quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to flatulence, then it is soft to the touch. And the appearance is such that you should look to see if it is from arterial blood, venous blood, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then you should leave the cure. For there is doubt and fear about it, as I have told you in the chapter on apostemes, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the bowel, then you should command the patient to tie their loincloth and lie down straight. Then press around the boil on all sides;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then have him lie face upwards between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	"Then go around the place you have marked with the entire spatula,"
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	"Then raise half of the boil above the whole large unguent."
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	"Then tie it tightly with a strong thread or silk cord and let the knot be finished."
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	"Then open half of the boil and stretch it over the knot, and insert your index finger into it until you reach the intestine."
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	"If you find it caught in the knot, untie it, and bring the intestine out of the belly."
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	"And if you find the boil, grab it with forceps and cut away any excess."
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	"And if the artery or vein opposes you, carefully go around it, then return to your work and take two needles and tie them with two strong threads, and stick the two needles into what you have pierced in a cross shape."
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	"Then compress the boil at four points above the needles and if you see blood, remove the needles and leave them there until it stops flowing, and cut away the dead flesh."
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	"Or you can cut it when it is soft and flowing, then clean it as needed, and cut the boil as we have said."
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	"And remove the blood or moisture that you find, then clean the wound as necessary, and sew it up."
dou chancre	Here is an old French recipe for treating a chancre (a type of ulcer):
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	"Of the kinds of cancer we have spoken about in the section, and how one must treat them with medicines, and how to avoid the cure by iron; and we say that cancer which has invaded the marrow requires great caution in its treatment. The ancients said that when cancer is located where it can be removed, like those on the breast or hip, and similar locations, it should all be cut out at the beginning. But when it is large and old, do not approach it, for I have never seen anyone cured of it; nor has anyone else before me."
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And the operation, when it is in a location where it can be removed, as we have said, involves purging the patient of black bile. Then make him vomit if he shows signs of repletion, and then prepare the patient in a good place to perform the operation. Then cut out your incisions or cancer, and remove all hair around it, and remove everything without leaving anything behind. Let the blood flow freely, and squeeze the wound with your hand or some other object, and if the bleeding is too much from the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops. Then heal it with another cure until it is healed."
de ydropisie	I have not found any mention of "ydropisie" in the text you provided. Is there a specific section or topic related to this that you would like me to summarize?
