Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	"We have already spoken in the section about the similarities of dropsy, how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, as well as the cure that is done with medicines and that which is cured with iron. Only 'eclites' is mentioned; and one should not touch these two semblances with iron: tympanites and hippocrates, for they are deadly things. Therefore, when you treat this semblance of dropsy called 'eclites' with medicines, and the cure does not help, look to see if the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, such as asthma or diarrhea and similar things. Do not touch him with iron, for there is doubt; but if you see that the patient is strong and vigorous, and he has no other disease besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should operate thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	"Lift the patient up onto your hands, and have the assistant press the abdomen while forcing the water towards the lowest part of the chest. Then take a spatula shaped like this: it should be sharp on both ends but not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, nor cause injury."
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	"Then look to see if the dropsy has entered towards the intestines: you must make an incision about three fingers' breadth below and above the navel; but if the dropsy is due to a liver disease, make the incision on the left side of the navel, and if it's due to mucus, make it on the right side. Make sure that the patient does not lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not flow towards the weak part."
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	"Then pierce all the skin with the instrument and insert it, and lift your hand so that the spatula goes between the skin and the muscle, as in skinning, to the depth of a fingernail or somewhat more. Then pierce the muscle until the spatula reaches the empty space, which is where the water is gathered. Then remove the spatula and insert this instrument, of which the form is like a silver needle: it is made of brass or light copper, with a small hole at one end and three holes on one side and two on the other. The edges are cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that writers use to sharpen a quill."
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	"At the top of this instrument is a funnel-shaped opening. When the instrument reaches the gathered water, stop up its end with your finger; then draw out about half or one-third of the water, but do not draw out too much at once, for if you do, the patient may suddenly die from loss of his vital spirits, or faint, or approach death."
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	"But draw out according to the patient's strength and the signs of his condition and pulse. Then remove the instrument and keep the water in reserve; it will be kept back by the heart, which stops up the hole made in the muscle as I have described. Then start again with the instrument on another day if you see that the patient can bear it, and draw out a little more water."
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	"Do this several times, but be careful not to leave too much water in the patient. If you are unsure about the patient's condition and leave too much water, he may need a burial bandage or hot sand treatment, frequent sweating baths or sunbathing, or bleeding. Also use drying medicines until he is completely dry, and cauterize the stomach, liver, and spleen after removing the water, as I have said before."
de l’estopement de la verge	"Regarding the swelling of the penis:"
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	"Sometimes children are born without any opening in the penis, or with a small one, or one that is not in its proper place. In such cases, it is necessary to pierce the penis at once with a very fine spatula of this shape: then insert a thin platinum clip into the hole and tie it in place for three or four days. When the child needs to urinate, remove the clip and let him do so, then replace it. Sometimes no clip may be needed, as the urine that comes forth will keep the opening clear."
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	"Those whose opening is small will be helped by the platinum clip, as we have said, for it will widen. Those who do not have an opening in its proper place are to be pitied, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, which prevents them from urinating until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot urinate because the matter cannot reach the marrow, and this is a serious condition."
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And the method of operation is this: the patient lies on his back, then lift up the tip of the penis and cut it like a feather until the opening falls in the middle, as it should. Be careful not to let too much blood flow out, for this happens often; if it does happen, stop the bleeding with whatever stops bleeding, and heal the wound until it is completely healed."
des pustules de la verge	"Regarding the blisters on the penis:"
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Many times these blisters appear on the penis, forming an ugly appearance of skin. Some are malignant and others are not; they must be taken with a very fine onion, cut out, and all cleaned up, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then treat with diafinicon ointment until they are completely healed."
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the blister is malignant, of foul color and smelling bad, you must cauterize it. When you have cut it out, and if the blister is at the tip of the penis, with part inside the skin and part outside, you must first remove the part that is inside; and when it is completely removed, then treat the outside part. For if you treat them together, you cannot be sure that the tip of the penis will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come into the penis and the coition; so you must cut away everything that is black and corrupted, then tie in place a plaster made of honey, flour, and the rind of pomegranates and figs, and then treat it with other remedies until it is completely healed."
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	"And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this method: The cautery helps in two situations together: namely, for stopping blood flow and for gangrene; and if the head of the penis is gangrenous and retracted, you must insert a lead pipe into the urethra and have the patient urinate through it; and when the skin at the tip of the penis becomes dry, which happens to those who are uncircumcised, or due to wound or abscess, then you must cauterize it with one iron instrument until the adhesions are loosened, and relieve the head of the penis from all sides."
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	"And if it is difficult to separate them, then cauterize with one spatula some little at the head of the penis and the skin; then gently open between two [the glans and foreskin], and place one thin linen cloth moistened in cold water there so that it becomes wet again."
de la circoncision	"Of circumcision"
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	"Circumcision is not like other wounds that heal by themselves; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary to do the best and easiest work for salvation."
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	"I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children because it was not customary in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience."
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	"Because I have seen the greatest part of the masters and seniors who performed circumcisions using only one knife, sometimes for boys and sometimes with a novacula; thus it happens that the glans remains bare because there are two layers [of skin], and sometimes they cut the upper one and leave the lower one."
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	"But then they cover it [the glans], and the pain is doubled; and at the time of washing, the tip of the member is not securely exposed; and sometimes during the washing of the wound, the instrument slips and wounds the operation, and many times they are born like this so that they do not need any further dressing, as I have seen."
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	"Concerning the washing that is done on boys with all the length of thread, I have found through experience that this method is good because boys cut evenly both above and below."
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	"But when you press your hand [to stretch the foreskin], you can cut evenly in one single moment of time; but make sure that the thread is tightly wrapped around the skin; and regarding the manner of performing the first operation, if the child understands, have him believe that you are only tying a string around his penis, and then console him in every way possible."

Then tie a double knot with a thread around the base of the foreskin, then tie another knot below the first one. Hold the second knot between your thumb and index finger and cut between the two knots, then quickly lift up the glans and pull on the head of the penis."
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then let the blood flow a little at a time because this is good for the wound. Then apply some powder and on top of the powder apply a cloth glued with a mixture made from one-half of a cooked egg yolk without tempering it with rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil, and leave it like that until the next day, then clean the wound with another cleaning until it is healed."
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	"The form of the foreskin at the time of washing should be like this: the two layers [of skin] should be thin and cut evenly, and each layer should be as large as the middle finger."
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	"The error in washing is when the glans is inside the incision; therefore, you must stretch it with your thumb before the edges adhere and close up, then cut it evenly; if you cannot hold it with your thumb, use tweezers to cut it."
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	"And if three days have passed and the skin below the penis is swollen, let it be until the inflammation has subsided, then gently scrape off the scab; cut it as much as you can move it, but be careful not to harm the penis itself."

"Then treat the wound with the soothing powder that we have described earlier, and if too much of the glans is cut and it retracts upwards, do not worry about it; treat it as we have said until it heals."
dou retenement de l’urine	Of urine retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	"Urine retention is due to obstruction caused by a stone, congealed blood, or a bowel, or a birth defect, or similar things that we have mentioned in our classification;"
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	"and if the urine is not released, and you see that it is retained due to a stone in the neck or bladder, then the patient should be made to bend over on their knees; and have their feet placed on their back, and extend their belly from the part above the back, and the patient should restrain themselves as much as they can; and thus the neck of the bladder is forced open for the release of the stone above, so that urine is released."
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	"And if it does not come forth as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must use all of the instrument called 'syringe', whose form is as follows: it should be made of fine, light silver, like the feather of a bird; and its tube should be one-and-a-half palms long, and narrow at the end."
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	"And the manner of issuing urine is thus: take one doubled thread, and tie at its end a small bag of wool or cotton, and place the head of the thread inside the syringe; then cut off any excess wool and push it to the mouth of the syringe. Then grease the syringe with oil or butter and melted wax, and have the patient sit on a chair. Then raise the bladder and penis with warm olive oil and water."
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	"Then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis upwards towards the belly. et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	"and continue using the syringe until the bladder is completely emptied, and then have the patient lie down."
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When the bladder is injured or contains blood, or is filled with decay and you see water and medicine dripping out of it, then use all the instruments called "clepsydra", its shape is:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see. The raised places are such that the medicine's probe fits well without adding anything, allowing moisture to be drawn out and whatever is needed to be inserted.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see your medicines pouring into the bladder, place the tip of the probe in the moisture and draw out what is inside. Then squeeze the moisture towards the keystone, and then strongly push the probe back in. The moisture will enter and reach the bladder now, so that the patient can feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle enema used to administer an enema to the bladder:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	It is made of silver or brass and has its head higher up. de la piere	de la moistor
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of treating stones and extracting them together with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between stones that are stuck in the kidneys and all their signs, and in which stones surgery should be performed; and in the bladder and in the urethra; and I will tell you about it clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones which are stuck in the bladder happen more often to children, and this is a sign that urine flows out of the bladder appearing like urine in its fineness; and it opens easily, and the patient grates his urethra, and he frequently pants, and then he becomes rigid; and many times these are the cause of inflammation. And it is easy to cure stones in children until they are four years old, but difficult in old people, and moderate in young people, those between youth and old age. And it is easier to treat those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to remove all the feces that are in the intestines. For sometimes they hinder looking for the stone.

de la piere des femmes	Of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens sometimes that a stone becomes lodged in women, and if it does happen occasionally, its cure is difficult, and it is prohibited for three reasons: one is because perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-informed who dares to uncover herself before physicians, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you are urged to do this, then it is necessary that you find a midwife well-skilled, and barely will you find one, and if you cannot find one, then seek out a chaste and subtle physician; and present him with an intelligent woman who understands the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you order regarding the examination of the stone.

Then place the knife in the cut if you feel the stone; then widen the wound until the stone can come out; and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with roots. Know their appearances so that you may know how to proceed.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood flows too freely, then place ground vitriol in the wound and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops. Then return to your work until the stone is removed, and have at hand the instruments that I told you about concerning the extraction of stones from men to aid you in your task.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the bleeding continues, and it is coming from an artery that has been cut, then place powder on the wound and bandage it tightly with linen cloths, and do not begin again, and leave the stone alone and do not try to remove it, for fear that the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the wound can be borne again, then return to your task until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	About hernial protrusions
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquous hernia is nothing other than an accumulation of moist or white matter that is under the heart of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "spermatozoa," and sometimes it is actually in the wall of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg. And this is the skin of the testicle between the white spermatozoa that we have spoken about; and this does not happen unless there is pressure.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the cause of this hernia is weakness in the testicles, which allows this matter to become spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from an injury to the testicles, and this matter can have many different colors: sometimes it has a yellowish tint, or it may be red, black, or white like water. And these are the most common cases.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs by which one can recognize this accumulation: if it is in the white spermatozoa that we have spoken about, then the protrusion will be round, like an egg in shape and length, and the testicle will not protrude because it is surrounded by moisture on all sides.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper wall of the testicle itself, then the protrusion will be round with a portion of the egg inside it, and because of this one might think that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicle and the white spermatozoa, then it can be felt very well; therefore, to know the color of the moisture, one should express it through the four-sided intrusive shape that is shown here.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introduction, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	When we treat it with iron, the patient should be in good health according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then have him lie on his back on something a little high, and put many blankets underneath him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	Then sit on his left side, and command the servant to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart's edge;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the thin spatula and cut through the skin of the ribs near the long edge towards the knuckle, making a straight incision that divides the rib cage up to the white fascia. Carefully scrape it according to your ability.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the plain fascia with one large hole and extract all the water. Then place your tweezers and stretch the fascia upwards. Do not touch the rib cage itself, but only the fascia. Carefully cut through it little by little until you have completely severed it. Otherwise, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the egg jumps out during your work, sew it back in its place once you have finished working on the fascia. Then close the two layers of the rib cage with stitches and treat the wound like any other wound until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find that the egg is corrupted by another illness, then tie up the vessels hanging there to prevent bleeding. Then cut through the rib cage along with everything attached to it and remove the egg. Treat it as described above.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	If water has gathered in two places at once, know that these are two roots. Cut the other root just as you did the first one evenly. Then wipe up the blood and put a compress moistened with rose oil on the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	Then place another compress moistened with wine and oil on the wound, followed by two layers of gauze. Bind everything together tightly according to this pattern:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and stuff them with wool lint in this manner, sewing them together at the waist of the breeches; one should be placed on the fundament up to the back, and the other at the wrist; then fold the two ends over the two corners, and secure the entire bandage in the loop of the breech.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this remedy is applied with a caustic instead of an iron burn, and it should be done thus: take one fine cautery lancet, cut into the skin of the joints, and heat it as we have said, so that the white, fatty substance containing water is exposed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the cautery in this manner and prick the fatty substance several times with it, scorching it well with this fine heated cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	"And cut in all ways that you can, until you strip it bare; and ensure the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and move guarding against blood loss, and make sure the works of cutting are smooth."
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	"And if anything happens contrary to what you're doing, or there's a blistering wound, blood loss, or something else, then treat whatever is causing you trouble, according to what is said earlier."
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	"And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this operation due to its horribleness, then perform a puncture instead, as I will tell you, and it should be done when you are certain through the signs that we have said indicate that there is water in the wound."
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	If thou makest the sick man sit upon one raised seat; then prick the abscess on its lower part with all of the spatula wide, and place the perforation deep into the body's long bone; and let the hole be large, so that all the water flows forth.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton upon the spot, bind it, and leave it to allow for the rest of the water to flow out, then heal it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the white cloth does not allow water to exit from the mouth of the wound, then thou must insert a feather or the instrument used for treating hydrops, as described above; and widen one hole in the wound, and know that the water returns, and gathers after five months or thereabouts, and when it has gathered thus as before, so shall the sick person pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this branch there are many different positions, which is why it seems to me more appropriate to leave it as it is.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I shall tell you about the characteristics and similarities of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come upon the body, especially upon the testicles; this is very common.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to say that it occurs due to acidity and heat that has spread to the testicles, or from impact;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	"The color of the abscess matches the color of the body; it causes no pain, yet it is a serious abscess."
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	"And sometimes there is a hard, rough, and porous abscess with dark color, which may come from the arteries or swelling of the veins."
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	"When it comes from an artery, you can tell by the hot swelling when you press it with your fingers;"
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	"You should not touch it."
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	"One that arises from swelling of the veins is recognized by its appearance when touched with the fingers,"
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	"And one can make an incision on this type and others."
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	"First cut the skin around the eggs, then they come out with the egg white flowing out evenly and freeing the eggs from their membranes."
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	"If the eggs are already set among these roots, then you must pierce them and cut them out;"
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	"And if it is around the egg white or inside the vessels, you must remove all of that matter and cut it out completely."
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	"And if the origin of the growth is behind, you must cut it all out and remove the egg as we have said."
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And once your operation is complete, cover the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then dress it with other dressings until it heals."
de l’aposteme des coions	"Treatment of an abscess on the testicles"
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	"This is an abscess covered by a covering resembling a boil, with softening of the skin"
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	"The patient cries out in pain when they move."
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	"And the treatment for this illness is as fearful as that mentioned earlier,"
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	"Nevertheless, we will tell you about its cure, according to what the ancients did."
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	"You must make the patient sit on a raised seat, then hang the suspending bandage for the joints below their knees over your two arms,"
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	"and stretch them out evenly, with the master holding them."
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	"Then cut the bandage around the thighs with a sharp knife as wide as the distance across,"
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	"And then scrape each side as we have described in the extraction of arteries from the temples;"
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	"Then I insert a needle with a doubled thread and tie it at the first place where the vein appeared, then tie it again at the other end;"
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	"Then cut it evenly in the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt humors;"
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	"Then treat the wound like any other incision wound so that none of the veins nourish one of the joints;"
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	"because otherwise there is no harm done, and if blood flows from all the veins, then it is necessary to draw out the joints from all the veins;"
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	"So that the bone does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the veins, and they dry up and do not become inflamed."
de la routure dou syfac	"On the rupture of the sinews"
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	"The cause of this injury is the section that occurs in the sinew when it extends over the stomach in the region of the hips, causing one of the intestines to descend from that rupture;"
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	"And this rupture occurs either in the sinew itself or due to its extension, and these two kinds occur very often due to causes such as blows, falls, jumps, heavy lifting, and similar actions;"
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	"And the sign that it is a rupture due to the extension of the sinew is that it occurs gradually over a long period of time and does not happen suddenly;"
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	"And the inflammation extends as far back as towards the depth because the sinew presses on the intestine."
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	"And the sign that it is a section of the sinew is that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and there is diverse inflammation apparent under the skin near the surface, due to the issue of the intestine and the body's retreat from the sinew."
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	"And sometimes the loops also descend with the intestine, becoming trapped there and causing great pain to the patient, especially when they are pressed."
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	"And in these cases of iron poverty, why one must avoid this cure:"
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	"And the manner of the operation is that you command the patient to reach inside the wound with their hand and pull out the intestine if it can be reached;"
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	"Then have them sit on your lap, with their back between your hands, and lift up their thighs;"
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	"Then stretch out the chest upward and cut off all the skin from the length of the thighs;"
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	"Then insert awls into the groin with a hook to open the wound according to your need, and make them long enough for the bone to be able to come out;"
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	"Then peel off the sinew that is under the skin of the thighs until all sides of the white sinew are exposed;"
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	"Then insert your index finger into that which leads to the joint, between the white sinew under the skin of the thigh and the second sinew;"
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	"And separate that which is behind the thigh and between the second sinew; then move your right hand inside the thighs towards the joint, stretch out the white sinew upwards with your left hand, and lift up the thigh along with all the sinews towards the groin;"
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	"And command the assistant to stretch out the thigh upwards and untie that which is behind the joint;"
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	"And check with both hands whether there is any intestine wrapped around the hard white sinew. If you find any such thing, push it back into the abdomen;"
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	"Then take a needle with one thick thread made of ten strands and insert it into the rear part of the sinew that is after the skin of the thighs, near the groin, then cut off the threads that appear from the sides until there are four left;"
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	"Then tie them together in the form of a cross and use them to tie down the sinew that we spoke about earlier, which is under the skin of the thighs, with two strong knots;"
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	"Then wrap the threads around and tie them tightly with two knots so that none of the vessels that nourish it can enter inside, preventing inflammation from occurring;"
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	"Then place the second knot next to the first one two fingerbreadths away from it, and after these two knots leave some of the sinew that is under the thighs hanging down a hand's breadth;"
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	"Then cut along the curvature of the thigh as much as you can down to the skin and bone, as we have said earlier;"
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	"Then apply wool moistened in oil to the wounds, and put on the bandage that we mentioned."
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	"And sometimes the white sinew that we have spoken about is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding."
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	"Because this happens often and leaves the bandage until it falls off on its own. And if it takes too long to fall off, then rise it with warm water and apply what we have said until it falls off;"
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	"And then treat the wound with another cure until it is perfectly healed."
de hernie carnouse	Carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	"I never saw anyone who dared to perform this operation by iron."
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	"And the ancients said that it is performed like the hernia that is attached to the groin, by tying the vessels loosely after the groin on top and below;"
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then cut it in half and treat the inflammation that opens up until the vessels dry out, then treat it as we have said until it is healed."
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	"Sometimes the hernia comes out through the anus as we have said, and the spot opens up. And none of the intestines descends to the thighs, but if any do descend, it is little, and it repairs itself immediately."
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	"And even if it stays too long in this state, the skin or sinew becomes inflamed until the intestines descend;"
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	"And this happens due to the stretching of the sinew that is at the anus, as we have said, because it stretches out and then becomes softened and swollen, opening up;"
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	"And the cure is by cauterization, as we have said before. And sometimes it is cured with an iron in this manner:"
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	"And the patient lies on their back between your hands, then cut off the swollen spot of the hernia from its width according to three fingerbreadths;"
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	"Then expose the sinew that is beneath the skin that follows it, then take a spatula and press it onto the visible spot of the sinew;"
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	"And press it firmly against the belly wall, then sew up the two exposed spots of the sinew over the top of the spatula, and sew them together;"
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then extract the head of the vein, and do not touch the syringe or stretch the eye or other things, as I have shown you in the treatment of intestinal obstruction.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then treat it with wound care. And when you remove the stitches, cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syringe is tightly closed and has no opening during dislocation. The cauterization is done at this stage and is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin over the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin over the joints becomes softened in some people because the tissues inside are softened, and it is unpleasant to see. When you want to treat it, make the patient lie on his back, and cut away the softened skin from the natural skin. Then sew the two lips together with one stitch, and if necessary, first sew the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches. Then cut between the stitches and cure it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	You should know that castration is condemned by our law and I would prefer not to speak of it in this book. However, there are two reasons why it may be necessary: one is for the surgeon to respond when asked about it and its treatment; the other is because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cats, and others. So I will say that castration is performed in two ways: by traction or by incision.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites occur in two ways among men: one is that between the two testicles there opens also the figure of a woman's nature, with hair and sometimes urine comes out from it. And the other way is in women, who have on the thigh both a penis and two testicles. And the treatment for man and woman is to cut off all the attached parts and cure them like other wounds; but for those men whose urine escapes through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	Tengnèye
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tengnèye is an attached part on the natural part that is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the treatment. It is necessary to cut away the excess of tengnèye with your hand or scissors, cutting lightly; do not go too deep so that blood does not flow out, then care for it like any other wound until it is healed. And there is another type of growth that appears at the mouth of the vagina and the anus, and sometimes bursts forth, resembling the appearance of a cow, which is why the ancients called it «cow disease». It must be cut away just as we have said for tengnèye, and cared for until it is healed.
de erratique	Erratique
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratique refers to when the nature of a woman is not pierced or the opening is small; it is either present at birth or caused by illness, or it may be due to attached tissue, either thin or thick, and located deep within the vagina, on the sides, below or elsewhere. It prevents conception and childbirth, and sometimes causes infertility. Its presence can be detected by examining the entrance of the vagina with two fingers or a speculum.
des emorroides	Haemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Haemorrhoids are openings of veins which normally do not exist, and when haemorrhoids are old they become hard; and we have said in the division their semblances and signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment. I say that haemorrhoids and hardness, when they are embedded deep in the anus, and cannot be felt at all, then there is no cure with iron. Those that are at the mouth of the anus can be felt and are those that can be cured. Therefore it is necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the anal opening with forceps, and cut it at its roots, then pour on medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and frankincense and similar things; then let her sit for an hour with her feet towards the fire, then put her in cold water. And if bleeding comes, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gall nuts and similar things, and then take barley flour and mix it with honey and vinegar and make one plaster to put on her back. If it oozes, that's good. If not, apply leeches to her back and breasts without cutting; then take linen, moisten it in plantain juice or almond milk with old wine, and apply it to the area. And when the swelling has healed, cure it with ointment until it is healthy; and that which is called 'albathir' is red, and resembles a sharp head, so it should be cut like I said for hardness; and then cure it with ointment until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	"Regarding boils of the skin"
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many types of boils come in the skin, such as chancre and flesh boil and herpes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot boil, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. Therefore, it is necessary for me to discuss the hot boil that comes in the skin, which is not one of those boils that grow on the body; and if you want to know how to treat them, look at whether the boil is inflamed at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and turns red when you see it. Therefore, do not hurry to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain stops; then make the patient sit on one seat, and have two small seats where they can lie down, and support their back with a pillow and bring their feet together at the knee level; and spread out their thighs, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them securely with a good bandage. Then suck out the pus towards the right side, and prepare the instrument for opening the mouth of the boil, which I will describe later; and it is necessary that when you are preparing this instrument to insert it into the boil first to know its depth so that what enters does not go too deep and does not hurt the patient. And if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the boil with cloths so that the instrument does not hurt them. Then put the funnel of the instrument on top and soak the instrument. When the boil opens and you feel it with your hand, then cover its head with lint moistened in rose oil or dried green oil; and when the abscess is emptied, then put a bandage at the bottom of the boil and put clean lint soaked in warm water on top of the boil and on the edge. Then cure after two days with suitable ointment until it heals. And sometimes lift up the boil and the wound by giving an enema of water and honey, and then give an enema of water where lily roots and long aristologist have been cooked. Then return to the ointment. And if the wound closes in the boil, then you must be careful not to cauterize with fire, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Childbirth is a natural process by which a woman gives birth to a child after carrying the baby in her womb for approximately nine months. The following is an overview of the stages of childbirth and some traditional remedies used to ease discomfort:
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	"Firstly, the midwife must know the figure of natural childbirth, and the sign is when you see the woman pressing downwards and desiring to smell the air; then the infant hastens to come forth. Therefore, know that this birth is according to nature's figure, with the head coming first, and the afterbirth with it. When you see these signs, it is necessary to press her belly gently so that the child comes out soon, for when it descends onto its head, then comes the afterbirth also. The mother is cleansed of her excesses by good cleansing. And he who comes otherwise does not come naturally; sometimes he comes on his feet, with the body or the head coming forth first, and the hands, or sometimes on his belly, and occasionally turned around on his neck, and in other evil figures. Therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in these matters, and wary of error and deceit; and I will show you all the figures as they should be aided."
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	"If the infant comes forth naturally upon its head, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool or let women hold her; and raise her nature of oil or fenugreek cooked. Then place the little spatula between her thighs whose shape follows:"
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	"And split the afterbirth with it and cut as much of its edge as the moisture within runs out. Then take hold of the woman's belly until the infant descends; and if it does not descend, then one must enema the woman with a mixture of myrrh and fenugreek with sesame oil. Then have her sneeze with condisium, and hold her mouth and nostrils for an hour; now the child will be born. And if the two hands come forth first, then one must gently press them back little by little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a seat, and lift up her feet high; then knock down the seat upon the ground, and take care that the woman does not fall during the descent; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the wrist that is mentioned before, and extract the child, and press it back evenly."

de l’issue des gemelz	Regarding the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, sometimes two at a time, and rarely three or four; this is not uncommon
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are rare and do not survive unless they are named
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that if there are multiples, they are separated by the caul which divides them, and is attached to the lower jaw;

de plusors enfans	"of many children"
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	"Sometimes they are shaped in the womb for one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or even more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of its glorious head."
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	"And it is necessary that the servant know all this, for sometimes such things happen."
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	"So do accordingly what is necessary."
de l’enfant mort	"of a dead child"
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	"When you treat the woman for a dead fetus in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are compelled by duty to deliver by hand,"
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	"Then it is necessary that you know if the woman has a sound constitution, and does not have any accidents or fear of death."
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	"It is necessary for the woman to be positioned on her back, with her thighs inclined downward and her legs raised."
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	"and the helper should hold the woman by two parts, or tie her to the bed so that she is not harmed during the descent of the child."
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	"Then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oil made from mastic, fennel and flaxseed, and then anoint the servant's hands with this oil and these powders."
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	"Then insert your hands gently into the womb, then twist one way or another until you grasp the fetus with your fingers that are suitable for this."
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	"And be careful that the fetus is positioned so that it comes out headfirst."
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	"So hook the fetus with your fingers in its ears or neck or mouth or throat or beard or anus or near its ribs,"
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	"And if the descent is by feet first, hook it under the knees and bring it out sideways."
