puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	"Then heal it with clean bandages until it is healed."
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	"But if it does not heal, return to what was said before;"
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	"You should know that you have not gone deep enough:"
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	"So uncover and probe until you reach the bottom,"
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	"And remove all corruption, then replace everything in its proper place;"
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	"And if it is healed this way, that's good."
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	"But if not, know that the corruption goes too deep for you to reach;"
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	"So there is no other remedy but to leave it alone;"
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	"But if there is a small rotted bone, and you can grasp it with forceps,"
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	"then extract it using an appropriate instrument;"
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	"But if there are many bones, crush them all and leave none behind;"
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	"And if moisture hinders you, but there is no error or fear,"
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	"So cut the moisture, flesh, and bone, and deliver them all."
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	"And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something clean on the wound to draw out corruption;"
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	"and leave it until the area around the bones is rotted;"
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	"And then the bones will come out more easily;"
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	"If it is a large bone, such as one from the thigh or leg,"
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	"then scrape off only the corruption until all blackness is removed;"
puis restoure la plaie;	"Then close the wound;"
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	"But if much of it reaches the flesh on the bone,"
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	"It must be cut all the way down to the corruption, then healed until it is sound."
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	"And I will tell you about a fistula that once happened in a man's leg,"
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	"So that you may learn from it and be helped in your work."
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	"A young man of about thirty years had pain in his leg caused by something inside the body;"
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	"So that the matter came to the leg and there was a large swelling, but no obvious opening."
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	"But the physicians foolishly probed so much that the swelling broke open;"
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	"And in removing much matter, it became a fistula with many openings all discharging pus and moisture from inside the body;"
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	"Many physicians tried to heal it for over two years, but none knew how to handle it properly;"
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	"So I was called and saw his leg and the medications they were using;"
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	"And what flowed from the openings was very foul;"
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	"The young man's body became red and had a yellowish hue."
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	"I placed a probe in one of the openings and then sought out all the openings;"
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	"And found that each opening met with another from every part of the leg."
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	"So I hurried and cut into one of the openings until I exposed a portion of bone;"
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	"And found it rotted and eaten away, with corruption reaching the bone inside;"
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	"I scraped off what appeared to be rotted bone, thinking there was no other corruption besides that which I had removed;"償"I
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	"But after a long time of treating it with dry medications, it would not heal;"
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	"So I changed my approach and exposed the bone again as before;"
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	"And found that the corruption continued into the bone, scraped it off, removed it, and then tried to heal the area;"
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	"But I could not do so until I cut around an inch of bone and pulled it out completely;"
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	"Then I treated the area with medications, and it healed quickly and soundly."
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	"And there was no need to change my approach except for the patient's weakness, which prevented him from bearing treatment,"
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	"and for his fear of death, which I had instilled in him."
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	"For often bloodletting was performed, but he remained entirely healthy."
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	"And in place of the bone, hard flesh grew; it was well-disposed and caused no harm or damage whatsoever, neither at present nor to come."
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	"And if any bone in the body is broken, it should be treated this way:"
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	"Take a splint and bind it to the head of the exposed bone,"
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	"and command him to extend it upwards;"
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	"And place another, larger linen bandage above the first splint, and tie it over the flesh that covers the bone,"
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	"and stretch it so that you can pull out the corrupt flesh underneath,"
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	"and uncover the flesh over the spot where you see that the bone is not exposed."
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	"And place a hot coal or a red-hot iron underneath the bone to cauterize the corrupted flesh;"
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	"This should be done until one can see and feel that the corruption has been removed, and then it should be done once more."
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	"And if the bone is corrupted but does not expose itself, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,"
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	"then uncover all of the flesh; then place a hot coal underneath,"
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	"And then scrape away the corruption from one end to the other with a spoon that is as long as the corruption, as we have said;"
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	"If the corruption is at the joint, cut away the corrupted joint and scrape the bone that contains it on the other side;"
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	"And if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, then there is no other option but to cut it out;"
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	"But if the corruption is at the wrist or ankle, that is a very serious matter,"
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	"Nevertheless, you must inquire into this corruption and discover how it presents itself:"
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	"And cleanse it in all possible ways, but be careful not to harm the nearby tissue or nerves;"
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	"And know that there are many different types of surgical instruments and spoons for scraping these bones, depending on the position and appearance of the bone."
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	"and their thickness and thinness, and their length and shortness, and their hardness;"
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	"And therefore it is necessary to equip oneself with the appropriate instrument for each type of operation."
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	"and know that through practice you will learn which instrument to use according to your knowledge of this art,"
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	"and the evidence of the different forms of diseases;"
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	"So consider carefully which instrument you need according to what is appropriate for each case."
dou feu	"fire"
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	"The flesh decays either due to an internal cause or due to a deficiency of nourishment;"
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	"And when you have treated this corruption with medications and they do not help,"
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	"then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the point where the corruption starts,"
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	Therefore the patient escapes from death through this, or from the greater evil of limb deficiency.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	The sign is that the limb becomes black as if it had been burned by fire
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	Afterwards, corrosion spreads from one member to another
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and begins to spread throughout the body; then you must quickly cauterize
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	And if it is caused by the sting of venomous creatures such as marine scorpions and snakes and similar ones
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corrosion reaches the top of the thigh, cauterize it there but do not allow it to extend down towards the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	But if it reaches the hand, cauterize at the joint so that the corruption does not spread up to the arm
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it reaches the arm, cauterize at the elbow; but if it passes the elbow, it is fatal
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	For there are no remedies outside of the quantity of its virtue
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And likewise when corruption comes to the foot, if it reaches the first joint cauterize after the other joint
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it reaches the foot, cut off the whole foot
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it mounts to the leg, cauterize at the knee joint
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	But if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	The method of cauterizing or amputating a limb is to tie it above and below
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	And extend one cloth from the lower ligature downwards, and another cloth from the upper ligature upwards
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	Then cut through the flesh between the two ligatures with a broad knife so that the bone is exposed
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then cauterize or amputate it and place a linen cloth on each side so that the cautery does not touch the healthy flesh
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and afterwards another wound and inflammation will come to the patient
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs while you are performing this procedure, quickly cauterize the area
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or place some constricting powders upon it. Then return to your treatment until it is completed
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind the wounded limb with a suitable ligature and care for it until it is healed
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I shall tell you what happened to one man who had an injury on his foot
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He developed a blackness that seemed like a burn from fire
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	And this corruption first appeared on the top of his foot and spread throughout the entire foot
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	But when the man saw the corruption, he quickly cauterized his foot and it was healed
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And some time afterwards the corruption returned on the back of his hand and he came to me
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I applied things that repelled after cleansing the body, but the corruption did not stop
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	Then he wanted me to amputate his hand, but I refused because I had hope of driving back the matter
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the man’s strength was weak; and he became completely despairing and returned home
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he quickly cauterized his hand himself and it healed
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I have told you this story so that others may learn from it in the future if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an inflammation comes on a fleshy part and remains for so long that it produces a large boil
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then it bursts and opens up, and the boil jumps out and the area stays empty like an ulcer
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin on top is as thin as a piece of delicate silk fabric
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	It does not reach down to the bone or nerve, and such an illness is called "healthy."
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	"and is not called 'fistula'";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	"But if it is so long that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called 'fistula';"
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	"And the skin should be cut all around, and even more so when it is thin, just like a drapelet;"
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	"But it will not harm because of its corruption."
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	"And if you fear that the skin may be harmed, and the corruption is not deep,"
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	"and the skin is thick with flesh, cut it this way for a clyster:"
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	"Observe if the breast is large and the belly that contains it has an unpleasant smell,"
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	"then administer an Egyptian clyster made this way:"
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	"Take equal amounts of hellebore, oil, and litharge, and melt them together in one vessel over the fire,"
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	"until the medicine is red-hot and becomes as thick as honey;"
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	"And then take some according to your need, mix it with water and honey,"
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	"and administer the clyster through the breast, closing the opening;"
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	"And leave the medicine in for two hours, then draw it out by pressing."
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	"Do this many times until the breast is softened and the pus is removed;"
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	"And sometimes administer a clyster of ash water,"
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	"when this medicine is not available, take ashes from burnt grapevine wood and pour water over them;"
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	"then strain it and administer the clyster until you know that the breast is well cleaned;"
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	"And if the patient cannot tolerate it or neither Egyptian medicine nor ash water,"
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	"then administer a clyster of water and honey with a little crushed litharge;"
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	"or use a clyster of honey and mixed wine, where the honey has properties to cleanse and wash."
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	"And the wine makes the flesh tough;"
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	"And when you have done this, and you are confident that the breast is well cleaned,"
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	"then administer a clyster of oil which brings forth flesh;"
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	"And take diaphoretic plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine;"
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	"Or administer clysters of other medicines and oils of which I have spoken their properties in the treatise on ointments;"
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	"And if the opening of the breast is small and the tube of the clyster cannot enter,"
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	"If you widen a little with an iron tool, and place a cloth soaked in Egyptian ointment upon it,"
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	"or basilicon ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	"And if the wound is too wide, then leave only enough space for a finger or the clyster to enter;
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	"And if the opening that casts bile is above, then cut it at or below its current location."
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	When bile is deep, there should be no flesh left behind.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	"If you cannot cut it beneath the breast as you see fit,"
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	"then prepare it in such a way that bile flows to its lowest point."
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when bile is deep, no flesh should be left behind
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cut beneath the breast as you see fit
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then prepare it so that bile flows easily downward, and leave nothing of the bile behind.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	And take consolidating medications to place on the breast
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and then apply one linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	Then cut again with force near the opening of the breast, about a finger's width wider than before
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply soft salve on another cloth according to the size of the opening
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the opening of the breast to alleviate bile flow; do not remove the large outer cloth except once after many days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And that which is on the opening of the breast should be removed often to remove bile
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	Know what kind of bile comes out: if it's venomous or little or abundant, digested or undigested
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	And beware if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	When this medication has been applied in such manner, and you see that something comes out of the opening of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	Know that if the breast swells up, and approaches the armpit;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then you untie it in the morning or on the third day, and when you remove the bandage,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Change one other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes bow-shaped after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons come afterwards after a long time, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For the closer is health. For there are men whose wound flesh heals slowly, and others who heal quickly;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if undigested food suddenly jumps out of the chest after many days, know that the chest has not opened.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the chest is slow to heal and remains open, apply dry medicines with moist substances but dry virtues
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	like diaphoretic ointment, because it contains much vitriol, which is the last medicine
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphoretic ointment and make it with rose oil, and mix it equally with old wine in substance
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook and use it. Also do the same for honey that is better cooked and thickened
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When diaphoretic ointment is not available
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on honey when it is hot on the fire
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then apply a cloth dipped in it to the chest, and let it stay there once or twice daily
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the lily of the valley, which is also like flour of mustard and centaury
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And use simples or composites: grind them, make a powder, and mix it with the honey I mentioned earlier
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the cure is prolonged and not accomplished by this cure
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption has gone deep and has made an impression on the bone, or on hard members or ligaments
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If it is a fistula cure, as we have said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	To treat a boil on the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	A panarice is a boil that develops underneath the nail of the thumb
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the big toe, or sometimes appears on other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	"And when it becomes inflamed, if one does not pay attention to it, then there appears a large boil."
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	"They scratch and bite until they reach the root of the nail, sometimes biting off the entire thing."
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	"And corrosion reaches down to the bone causing foul-smelling pain. The skin becomes thin and reddened, with a yellowish hue."
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	"When you treat it as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not help,"
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	"then you must cut away with an iron instrument all the excess flesh that remains from the nail."
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	"then cauterize the wound afterwards."
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	"A large cauterization is very helpful if the bone and nail are sound;"
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	"and if the nail presses on the flesh causing it to swell up and form a boil,"
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	"then you must place hot coals under the nail that is pressing on the flesh."
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	"And lift it up, then cut away that delicate and tender flesh carefully,"
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	"and put hot, corrosive medicines on the remaining flesh to remove all of it."
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then treat it with ointments until it heals."
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	"And if the corruption has reached the bone, cut away the affected part and scrape it clean, for as long as there is rotting in the bone, it will not heal."
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	"If you see that both sides are corrupted, then cut them off with hot iron instruments, as was said earlier,"
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	"then treat it until it heals."
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	"And if it is infected and causes great pain when pressed, you must cleanse it first,"
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the big toe at an angle across
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and ensure that the cut does not go all the way to the flesh beneath the nail, as this would cause great pain for the patient.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it does happen, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain in the wrist
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Some people may have a double joint that arises from their hands by chance, which is all fatty tissue
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there are bones present, and rarely a nail
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	None of these arise from the root of the joint or are located in some of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that appear on any knuckle do not move
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that appear at the joint of the finger sometimes move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The cut for one that is fatty tissue should be done in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: you must take care of this.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	If it occurs at the back or front of the neck, then first cut around the flesh up to the bone
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then cauterize it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	A dislocation that occurs at both knees simultaneously comes from birth, or from a wound, or from burning by fire, or from similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary to cut this dislocated joint so that the limbs return to their natural forms
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between both a bandage or cloth moistened with rose oil so that they do not fuse together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between them two thin slices of lead until the joint is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a dislocation occurs at one of his knees with the palm of the hand, cut this dislocated joint in the manner that is appropriate.
Des vils	Worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	They are large bags filled with melancholic superfluities, which come into many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purge of bile, and then heal it with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is by cutting them and drawing out the black blood with a feather;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is to raise the bag and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision should be made in this manner: first, raise the leg with hot water very vigorously until the thick blood is thinned;
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then hold the patient's leg above the thigh down to the part below the knee joint.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then press the dislocation into one of three places on either side, with a wide grip,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then wipe away and draw out the black blood by your hand from one side to the other until as much blood comes out as the strength of the patient can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then rinse it off, and order that he be wrapped in meat around the black bruise.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and resume evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The lifting of his leg is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg if there is much hair
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and then raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, heat it over the fire, then cut around the vein on the long bone at the top of the knee, or below at the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then scrape off the skin with the scalpel and strip the vein from both sides until it becomes visible to touch.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it appears like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then press down on the joint until it rises above the skin, then bend it slightly backwards,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then cut it in another place three inches further on; then scrape off the skin over the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift up the vein, as you have done, and bend it at another angle, as you have done first
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then cut another size, or several if needed, then lift it up, and cut it at the two ends of the feet
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then draw it out and raise it to the second size; then pull it out size by size until it comes out completely, then cut it
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot draw it out and lift it up, then insert a needle with a strong doubled thread
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it out, and place one foot underneath the needle, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	Be careful not to cut it off because if it is cut, you cannot pull it or lift it up and this causes harm to the patient
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it all, then put on the wound a piece of wool moistened in wine and rose oil; and dress it until it is clean.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped around itself, and it is not straight as we have said
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you must cut it crookedly but do not cut it off; then pull it out as we have said before
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the blade used to cut veins is curved so that it does not cut into the vein
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it has a large curve because if it were thin, it would cut into the vein but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the venous ulcer
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is inflamed in legs, in warm regions where no herbs or trees grow, and on land with no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And sometimes, it occurs elsewhere than in legs, which happens due to corruption occurring beneath the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	Just as it comes into the body like a serpent and vermin, wedged between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the sign of the beginning of this inflammation is that there is a very great swelling in the leg
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the location changes and the inflammation begins to come outwards, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the skin opens up, then you must wrap around it a piece of linen measuring about one and a half to two feet long,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the linen hang down against the leg; each time that it becomes soaked with fluid from the wound, wrap the linen around it, and renew it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a piece of it, and wrap the remainder around; do not cut off at its root until all of it has come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it off, it will retreat into the flesh and cause an abscess or corruption in that place, leading to illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, it must be treated little by little until its end is reached, so that none of it remains on the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this inflammation, once treated for five or ten palms’ length,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and there was once a man who came to me with it extending ten palms’ length; when you cut it off, it makes one large hole or opening, and goes all the way down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	So that it all comes out; then empty out the matter that is inside, and apply medicines around it to prevent corruption for a few days, after which treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this inflammation has many holes, especially when it opens up at the ankle of the foot or on the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	"And then much rain comes, and he jumps suddenly; therefore treat him as we have said before."
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	"Worms that are born between skin and flesh"
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	"This illness is called in our land 'cattle disease' because it happens often to cattle,"
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	"and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down,"
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	"And one feels him well when moving from limb to limb, until he reaches the skin where he is about to come out, and jumps forth;"
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	"and is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, such as those that produce worms and serpents and flies and roundworms in the belly;"
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	"and there is doubt about its harmfulness because when it goes through the body, it ascends to the head and comes to the eye,"
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	"...and sometimes enters it and destroys the eye; and this happens often."
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	"When you see him being cured and drawn out, one cannot doubt that when he goes:"
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	"...therefore it is necessary for you to tie the opening above and below with a strong, tightly-woven bandage,"
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	"then cut on top and draw him out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it,"
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	"...then cauterize with fire until he dies;"
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	"and the greatest harm that it does is that it blinds the eye, as we have said;"
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	"And if you see him coming near the head towards the eye, tightly tie down the eyebrow below him and then cut on top and draw him out;"
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	"and it is necessary to use remedies for cleansing the body of putrid humors with soluble medicines,"
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	"And beware of eating meat that causes putrefaction."
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Here is a possible translation:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	"This illness is called 'vakivir' in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs,"
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	"And then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I tell you."
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	"I was called to see a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the hollow of her arm;"
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	"And shortly after, it climbed up like a worm onto the shoulder,"
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	"Faster than anything else, just like molten silver when it moves from one place to another;"
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	"The pain left that place and fastened itself onto the shoulder,"
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	"And then shortly after it spread throughout her body, until it reached the other arm;"
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	"Then she told me that it was constantly turning around her body, just as I saw."
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I marveled greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner before."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	"Nevertheless, I had often seen that pain could move from one place to another,"
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	"But I had never seen it happen like this in a woman."
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	"And I thought that perhaps it was because the woman had a dry body and exposed hollows,"
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	"and for this reason appeared that constrained swelling;"
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	"And it does not appear in the same way to those who are well nourished and have moist bodies and covered hollows."
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	"And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have described,"
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	"if the swelling rises above and below rapidly, and then suddenly bursts open so that the constrained swelling disappears from its place;"
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	"And cauterize the spot; if you do not see it with your own eyes,"
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	"if the cure is through those means that reduce swellings, such as fetid pills and pills of saffron, and others like them."
Des saiettes	"Of Sweats"
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"Sweats are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body where they flow."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	"The diversity of their shapes is such that there are those which have large points, small ones, hairy and smooth;"
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	"And those with two angles, those with tongues, and those with fragments;"
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	"and that which falls upon any limb does so in one of two ways: either it flows from the principal member,"
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	"such as brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar members;"
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	"When it flows from any of these parts and the signs of death that I will tell you about appear:"
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	"then beware of removing this sweat, for death follows in many different ways;"
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	"And when this bad sign does not appear and the sweat is not deep, then treat it and heal the wound."
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	"When sweat flows from the brain and pierces the bone, and the soft fontanelle that is on the head becomes displaced,"
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	"and there appears sudden darkness before the eyes and loss of consciousness, redness, violent trembling, pale face and congestion of the tongue with inflammation, spasm and disturbance of reason, vomiting of bile;"
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	"and perhaps there is fever in the nose or ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost;"
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	"And from the wound flows moist white blood resembling poultice, and then also like boiling flesh;"
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	"and if this sign appears to you, then beware of treating it, and remove the sweat only if it is not inside."
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	"The signs that indicate when sweat flows onto the heart are: it is near the left nipple and seems as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;"
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	"And perhaps the sweat moves like poultice, and dark blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come forth with syncope;"
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	"You should then be sure that death will ensue."
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"And the signs of sweat that affects the lung are: foam flows from the wound without pain, the throat swells, the patient changes color and sighs loudly while seeking cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	"And if sweat flows onto the covering of the lung, near the little ribs; there will be great pain and distress with sighing; and all the members of the shoulders move."
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if sweat flows onto the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will flow from the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if sweat flows onto the belly and much feces flows out through the intestines, there is no hope for recovery or removal of the sweat."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	"And if sweat flows into the bladder and urine flows out with fever, and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is deadly."
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"Other members such as the face and neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary muscles, spine of the back, buttocks, thighs and legs, and similar members are safe according to many different conditions."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When sweat is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me so that you can do likewise."
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	"It happened to one man that sweat fell onto his eyelid at the root of the nose;"
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	"I tested it and removed it on the other side beneath the ear fat without any harm."
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	"And in another case I removed sweat that had fallen onto the ear fat beneath the skin;"
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	"and the sweat was deep and I could not reach it except for its tip towards the cheek,"
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	"and the arrow was large, like a Turkish bow's, with one light feather on either side of its ears; the wound was clean, and no bad accident occurred."
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	"And he drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with feathers:"
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	"I felt his beard and searched carefully until I found it; and the Christian was healed."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	"And he drew an arrow from one man which had fallen into his belly; and he thought that he would die;"
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	"but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change."
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	"I cut through the arrow with a knife and extracted it, and drew it out backwards; there was no bad outcome."
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	"And if you see one man into whose back an arrow has fallen, and the wound has become inflamed;"
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	"and the arrow remained inside him, and his natural condition did not change,"
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	"he found no harm in any of his natural works."
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	"And he saw another man into whose face an arrow had fallen and the wound became inflamed;"
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	"and it remained thus without causing him great pain; and many others like this happened."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	"And he drew an arrow from one of the king's nobles which had fallen into his nostril;"
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	"and it was slightly inclined towards the right side, and the arrow was entirely embedded."
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	"I was called to attend him three days after it had fallen; I found the wound very narrow."
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	"I searched for it carefully but could not feel it at all;"
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	"and he felt pain and discomfort beneath his right ear."
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	"I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow"
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	"I applied to the spot an attraction plaster made for digestion, so that the place would not become inflamed;"
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	"and then the arrowhead appeared."
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	"I applied the plaster there for several days; and the wound healed again; and the sick man remained thus a long time,"
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	"until he felt the arrow one day inside his nostril; and he told me so."
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	"I applied a corrosive ointment to the wound for many days until it was opened;"
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	"and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrow sticking out at that spot."
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	"then with the aid of this corrosive ointment I opened the wound until the tip of the arrow became clearly visible;"
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	"And it took about four months to heal completely."
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	"and then the wound healed so much that I inserted pincers and pulled it from side to side; but I could not get it out;"
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	"so I kept trying in various ways with different instruments until I succeeded in grasping the arrowhead securely with well-made pincers one day;"
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	"as will be described at the end of this chapter; thus I drew it out and healed the wound."
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	"And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:"
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	"So I healed it, and the wound closed up; and the patient recovered completely."
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	"Now I have told you about the extraction of some arrows,"
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	"So that you may apply your care to what I do not mention, for books cannot cover everything;"
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	"But wise masters compare little things and what is present and lacking,"
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	"and find nine works and nine instruments according to the circumstances of foreign cases that happen in this art."
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	"I say that arrows leave the member they are stuck into by two ways:"
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	"either through the spot where they entered or through some other part;"
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	"And those that come out through the spot where they enter are called entering arrows and often come out in this manner."
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	"And if it does not come out at once, let it stay until the flesh is corrupted around it, and the exit is cleared;"
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	"And likewise if it is stuck in bone and cannot come out, let it stay for a few days and moisten it each day;"
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	"And then it will come out; if not, make an incision all around with a fine needle until the spot is widened, and then draw it out."
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	"And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bone of the skull and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain,"
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	"and some of the symptoms that I mentioned appear in the patient; then do not draw it out but let it stay until it becomes equalized after a few days;"
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	"for if the arrowhead reaches the sinus, death will ensue."
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	"And if the arrowhead is stuck only in bone and does not reach the sinus,"
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	"and the patient remains without bad symptoms for a few days; then attempt to draw it out."
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the arrowhead is very deeply stuck and cannot come out; then apply caustics around it as I told you; then treat the spot until it heals."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	"And if the arrowhead is buried in the flesh and cannot be seen; then search for it carefully all around;"
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	"and if you feel it, draw it out with some convenient instrument;"
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	"And if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead,"
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	"then make an incision until the wound is large enough;"
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	"And draw out the arrowhead if you can; and if there are barbs on it that prevent its withdrawal,"
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	"then cut off the flesh that is stuck in two places on either side that you can reach;"
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	"And then break or bend the barbs of the arrowhead so that you may draw it out."
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	"And be careful not to break the arrowhead while drawing it out; for it will come out more smoothly that way."
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot draw it out at once, let it stay until the flesh around is corrupted; then draw it out, for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	"And if bleeding opposes you, apply what we have said about treatment in its chapter;"
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	"and beware of cutting the nerve and vein; and devise how you may draw out the arrowhead safely."
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	"Soon or late, firmly or gently; place the patient according to his position when the arrow struck him;"
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	"for that is the greatest help there is; and if you cannot do this, then place him according to what the signs indicate."
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	"Arrows that come out through another part or show some sign of themselves, or cause the skin to swell at that spot which can be seen or felt,"
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	"then make an incision until you can grasp it with pincers; then draw it out; for it will come out now."
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	"And if the arrowhead is held in bone, turn your hand around until it enters the bone and widen the hole; then draw it out."
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	"And if it cannot come out, let it stay a while longer; then resume extraction until it comes out completely;"
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	"If the shaft of the arrowhead is there, throw away the entire shaft;"
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	"And if the shaft has fallen off and you see that pressure should be applied, then apply a hairy instrument;"
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	"So that the tip of the arrowhead enters into the hairs of the instrument; then push it out."
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	"And if the arrowhead is barb, then insert an instrument with a pointed end into its shaft to facilitate extraction."
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	"If the arrowhead has touched a nerve, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the nerve lies if possible;"
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then heal the wound as it ought to be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the stone falls into the bladder, the kidneys, the belly, or the cost area, and it is nearby, you can grasp and remove it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And guard yourself from cutting the vein and the nerve, then extract it, then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the healing will be healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used for extraction is like a bird's beak, and here it is depicted:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the stone.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the catheter tip is also like the feather of a bird
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to insert at the point of the stone, as depicted here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for inserting and extracting is shown here
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	There are 31 veins from which one can bleed, with 16 at the head
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	namely: 2 temporal veins located behind the ears, commonly known as "temple veins";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are visible in the two foreheads;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and 2 veins located in the inner corners of the 2 eyes, commonly called "the temples";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that runs along the forehead; and the vein at the back of the neck
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins located in the neck
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins located above the lips of the mouth, commonly known as "the cheek veins";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One of them is the cephalic vein, located on the outer side of the left arm and commonly called "the vein of the head" by lay people;
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the median vein is called the "fastest," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilica veins;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the lay people call it "vein of the heart"; and it is located on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it "belly vein," and it is above the bladder
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one which appears visibly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvation vein is the vein between the little finger and ring finger, and has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and there are three veins in the leg and foot: one is below the bend of the pouch on the left side
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second is the saphenous vein on the right ankle; and the vein called "cave" which is in the ankle of the other side
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and there are three veins beneath these ones in the other leg
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein that is after the ears helps with ancient catarrh and headache
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the vein, as I told you, are such that if you raise the head of the patient
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	you wipe the place where the veins are with a rough cloth, then make the sick person strain his neck with a towel
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then press them with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse underneath your thumb, then squeeze firmly
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand upstream along the entire vein
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through skin and vein well with two fingers of the cross, and let blood flow until you see enough;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then compress it and bind it, so that it is completely healed
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken about the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The two arteries that are in the two temples help with ancient headaches
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sciatica, and customary ophthalmia, and to the body of tears of the eyes
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of this vein are such that
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is necessary for the sick person to strain his neck until both veins appear clearly
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse under your thumb, then squeeze firmly
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then raise the heart above the vein with your index finger and insert the lancet underneath
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein and cut it as you did with the other two veins, then let the blood flow according to your need
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the sick person, put your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it tightly and leave it until it is healed. We have already spoken about their cauterization and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein in the forehead is equally useful as the temporal vein for treating old facial diseases, headaches, and redness
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its qualities are such that if the sick person strains his neck by twisting, the vein will appear
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fosseur," of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	"And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow out according to the amount you desire;"
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	"Then untie the bandage from the patient's neck, and tie it around the vein until it is secure, sometimes using a wide flame."
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	"Nevertheless, the bandages should not be too tight, and tie them diagonally because the bone is close by, and sometimes the bandage breaks when it's thin."
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	"The bandaging of the two veins that are in the two arms helps with swelling, inflammation, redness, and pain in the eye, and with diseases of the face."
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	"And the quality of their bandaging is that the patient twists his neck away from the affected side, as mentioned earlier;"
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	"Then apply the bandage diagonally, a little long and wide because there is not much flesh."
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	"And if the bandage is thin, it might break. Then wipe away the blood until you have enough, and then tie on cotton, tying it securely."
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	"The bandaging of the vein in the nose is useful for treating ague, sudden frenzy, and diseases of the face,"
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	"such as migraine and redness that appear on the face, especially when it's chronic;"
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	"And the quality of this bandaging is that the patient tilts his head back, then presses his nose with his left hand,"
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	"then take a long thin bandage and insert it into the space between the two nostrils through the upper lip;"
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	"because the vein does not open well there, and blood will start to flow now."
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	"And do not insert it too deep, then wipe away the blood according to your needs, then tie it on and leave it overnight because it heals quickly."
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	"and this is how you shape the bandage:"
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	"The bandaging of the two arms helps with stretching tendons, starting to learn fencing, and many diseases, including impetigo, corrosion, herpes, and eczema;"
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	"And the quality of this bandaging is that the patient stretches his neck to both sides, as we have mentioned before;"
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	"and let the master stand on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair,"
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	"then bandage the vein in the long arm a little wide, then wipe away the blood temperately or as much as needed;"
