puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	"then repeat on the other vein, then untie the bandage and bind it between the two veins moderately."
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	"so that the patient is not strangled, and leave it until morning when the wound will be healed."
De la sainie des leivres	"About bandaging lips"
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	"The bandaging of the veins above the lips helps with colds in the mouth, gum corrosion, cracked lips, and around the nose."
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	"And the quality of this bandaging is to have the patient sit before you, then stretch their neck as I've mentioned;"
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	"then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and one on the left,"
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	"And recognize them by their dark color and the small dark veins around them;"
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	"then tie one or both of them, and if you don't know how to do it, be uncertain,"
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	"then tie the largest one on each side, and also tie the two veins above and below in the same manner."
De la sainie desoz la lengue	"About bandaging under the tongue"
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	"The bandaging of the veins under the tongue helps after the cephalic bandage and is used for stretching the throat, eye diseases, and mouth diseases."
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	"And the quality of bandaging is that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, raises his tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein:"
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	"then tie both of them, but do not insert too deep because the arteries are below."
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	"The veins of the neck that are commonly bandaged are done in two ways:"
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	"either with one large mirror-shaped bandage or with an olive-shaped thin bandage like a cutting edge, called 'anesil';"
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	"And they are wide and thin according to the width and stretching of the veins."
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	"The shape of the mirror bandage is very well-known and is wide as you can see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	"And it's necessary to open the smooth scalp veins that contain thick and turbid blood;"
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	"And this is the shape of the olive bandage:"
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"It's more pointed and thin, used for bandaging small veins with clear yellow blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	"The bandaging of the basilica vein helps with diseases below the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen;"
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	"And it's important for the bandager to tie tightly and be careful not to mistake the artery that is below."
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	"If he ties the artery, blood will start flowing, so it's important to compress it as I've mentioned;"
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	"and the bandage should not be pointed but cutting like an 'anesil'."
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	"And if the basilica vein is not visible, you must stretch it out and change to another one;"
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	"or choose any branch of it or bandage the vein in the elbow instead."
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	"And tie it with the 'anesil' bandage as we have mentioned."
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	"If you want to recognize the bandaging location, first stretch out the arm and touch the spot until you feel the pulse;"
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	"then mark the starting point with a pin, then tie the arm and bandage the vein with the 'anesil' bandage."
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	"And be careful not to hit the artery when you see the spot swollen, because it's the artery: avoid it."
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	"If you see something like urine from a child coming out at the top and the blood is red and thin, know that it's arterial blood:"
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	"then quickly place your finger on top and remove it if the bleeding stops, which happens often;"
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	"then tie the arm again and leave it like that without moving. The patient should be calm and not move until healed."
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	"If the bleeding doesn't stop and you're alone without a doctor nearby, tie the artery if it's visible because its head retracts. Then compress the bleeding."
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	"And take half of a fig tree bark, split it open and use one half to tie tightly until the next day;"
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	"If the bleeding stops, that's good. If not, treat it with powders that stop bleeding as we've mentioned."
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	"And compression is not always useful in many situations for small wounds and the strength of the arm tie."
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	"The bandaging of the vein in the middle helps to treat bleeding from the head above and the body below;"
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	"because it's composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have mentioned;"
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	"And the bandager should be careful not to insert too deep and find the nerve underneath;"
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	"and if it swells the healing will be hindered, and sometimes it can't heal."
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	"and this nerve is visible many times. If it's not visible in some people due to its thinness, you must bandage it with the 'anesil' instrument and avoid touching the nerve as much as possible."
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The pulse of the cephalic [artery] helps to draw blood from the head and aids in healing.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	It is necessary to cauterize with olive oil flame or myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one should seek the lightest place and not worry if it fails the first time, and start over
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes the place may swell in some people when it fails the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of cauterization depends on your skill.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about cauterizing is that it is never done except for the sake of health
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent future illnesses
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	Cauterization should be performed on one of the three veins found in the elbow area, namely the cephalic, basilic and median cubital vein
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it should be done at the beginning of Lent, in autumn and winter after meals, when the sign of digestion appears
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	Cauterization should be done on the first or third day, after two or three hours from noon.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The cauterization performed for the treatment of diseases does not have a fixed duration, but rather is done according to necessity, day or night, at any time.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	One should not cauterize children under the age of 14 nor women who are pregnant except from the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old people who have passed the age of sixty should not be cauterized.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wishes to be cauterized in any way, they must first cleanse their bowels with a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	Otherwise, if there is an abundance of retained feces, the veins will not be able to draw out the superfluities that could harm the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One should not cauterize someone who is too fond of meats or someone who is drunk at that moment, nor a dropsical person;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And one should beware of cauterizing someone after a sudden pain in the colon, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive menstruation, hard labor, watching, fasting or any loss of strength from an injury to the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then carefully remove the humors by diet, drink and medicine if you have the ability;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter a warm bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtly heat up the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and cauterize one of the veins on the arm near the third, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself that day from hard labor, excessive eating, sexual activity and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be calm and joyful, and let the cauterizer stand higher than the person being cauterized, and let them rub the arm two or three times with a cloth beforehand;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then strain the vein in the middle, for when it is too narrow or poor, blood cannot flow properly.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the joint with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then dampen the flame of a small amount of old oil with your left hand and place your thumb on that vein below the joint where you want to cauterize;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	that the vein may not clot or fail at striking
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like strings to the bladder, and some such that are full of windiness
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	such that when one puts out the flame, it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus some are of these;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	If he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow; therefore, the surgeon must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If the vein opens on the first attempt, that is good. If not, try again a little lower or higher, but avoid inflamed areas.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	"And if the place is swollen, and the patient is afraid,
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance, boils may appear; do not enter a bath, then resume bathing if he wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it is not so much blood as you see, then fear for that very opening directly into all the flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And quickly close the wound before the area becomes swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not resume bathing, and apply a little oil plaster; for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place, the oil has healing power.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the oil plaster in every bathing of the veins to stanch the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same thing can be done with bruises and blows from falls when applied to the area; for it makes blood flow subtly and spreads it out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there appears a large boil which happens many times, especially when it is not bled any other time besides the first opening of the vein.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	Then hurry, and apply to the area a warm sponge moistened in water and salt, and leave it on for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the blood has flowed from the vein; and if it remains on the area for some days with a black or green color, do not worry.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see that there is no improvement, apply something made of aloe or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, masterwort, or the like.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an boil appears during the bleeding of the basilica vein; then place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft under pressure from your hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not apply anything we have mentioned, for fear of causing an artery to burst; but instead make a dry plaster with one egg and harden the area, then cauterize it with another cautery until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And let each person bleed according to the strength of their constitution and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if it is thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is full and fat, and needs bloodletting, make the cut larger and use a wider lancet.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite; let them bleed less often and in smaller quantities, and they should be bled by making a transverse cut, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding prevents the loss of too much blood and damage to nerves, and is better than long or wide cuts.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for one whose body is weak from bleeding, give them bread moistened in pomegranate juice to eat; if they are feverish, bleed them three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they are of cold temperament, let them eat before bleeding bread moistened in musk syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they faint during bleeding, after losing much blood, it is necessary that they inhale broth of meat and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things we have mentioned in the section on syncope for reviving them.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to vent his arm and bleed again later on, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed little by little according to his remaining strength continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to vent their arm after the first bleeding and has a strong body, should bleed again seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to wash themselves elsewhere should do so on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is much blood inside the body that has already heated up and causes fever; so it is necessary to draw out a large quantity of blood and widen the incision until it flows freely.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	After you have fulfilled all the requirements for washing yourself and placed your hand on the patient's pulse when they wash themselves, be careful that the mouth does not come into contact with the blood.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when the washer is careless;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not suffice to simply untie the arm and let blood flow a second time if the incision has closed up, then you must press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	unless he is hunched over; then he should extend his arm hastily, for that would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave him until he has washed himself the second time; or you can prick him with the point of the flame until the blood that has congealed at the opening of the vein flows out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place over it one handful of fresh linen soaked in water and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, then leave it alone and do not squeeze it too tightly until the boil is healed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to draw blood a second time, then wash him in the same spot or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm can be washed instead of the vein in the head because it is composed similarly.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method for washing is that the sick person immerses their hand in warm water until the flesh is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then they tie it moderately so that the vein appears well, and then wash it across, not from side to side nor lengthwise;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the incision wide and wash it well near the joint of the hand; if blood cannot flow out, then immerse the hand again in warm water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer time, then do not immerse the hand again in warm water, for one immerses it more often in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the washing of this vein is safer than all other veins because there are neither arteries nor nerves present.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The washing of the salvation vein on the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Wash your hands and immerse them in warm water until the vein has swollen and can be seen;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and wash across it, and if you cut all along it, nothing will be harmed.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep, for the nerves lie beneath every skin of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then immerse the hand again in warm water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as necessary, then place oil and linen on the vein to bind it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The washing of the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mice (gout), and do everything as I have told you concerning the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The washing of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all diseases that are beneath the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the womb, retention of urine, disease of the reins, and old diseases of the thighs and legs.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of this washing are that the sick person immerses their foot in warm water and rubs the vein until it appears;
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and tie above the ankle; the vein is at the ankle, and many veins go upwards on the foot;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	therefore wash either the larger vein or that at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you wash it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and cut across it as in cutting, and make the wound shallow.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if blood cannot flow out, then immerse the foot again in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the washer fails at first, then recommence on a little higher up, for the place is saline;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not fear the nerves, as we have said, and do this equally with the saphenous vein of the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and its washing is beneficial for pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of this washing are that the sick person enters into a bath and washes over the ankle four times while twisting it;
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein does not appear; and if it appears, then wash it in all ways that you can, and especially across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is better that you cut it, for the place is without nerves, and many people are afflicted by it.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then wash any vein that appears on the back of the foot and near the little toe, but beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And draw out as much blood as you see fit, then untie the linen, and place cotton on it and bind it tightly; now it is washed clean.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or earthenware, or glass. Cupping is performed in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping that is done without striking is performed in two ways: either with fire or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	Cupping performed by striking and bloodletting is done at fourteen locations on the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is entirely on top of the head; another is in the nape of the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others are on both sides of the neck; and the cupping glass under the chin
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glasses on the shoulders; and those on the elbows.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cupping glasses on both arms; and those on both legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the cupping glasses on both ankles; and this cupping does not draw blood except from the small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And therefore it does not weaken at all, unlike bloodletting from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping should not be administered either with fire or without fire in any disease that comes from repletion until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness or custom cupping must be performed, then administer it once at the beginning and once at the end of each month, and also every four days.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some people who, when they need to undergo cupping, have heavy heads;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and others find repletion and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness before the eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And some people experience a taste of blood in their mouth, have swollen tongue, and vomit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream and see bloody wounds, dead bodies, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the month, we order cupping to be performed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding of the temple helps against headache … that comes to them, and it is not necessary that this be done after evacuation of the whole body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And cupping replaces bleeding of the temporal vein
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	nor should those who are cold in temperament or have catarrh make use of it, for it harms them greatly.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	"And therefore, old men should not use it, nor those with cold humors in their heads."
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who are often cured by it become accustomed to it, and therefore the cupping glass should be placed a little lower down out of fear of becoming accustomed."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Cupping on the neck is beneficial for treating conditions in the head and neck region, especially the throat.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	"And to cut the channel of the bladder, and to cough, and to be full."
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	"Then it is necessary to push gently, because if she holds too firmly, it will cause imbalance or harm to the stomach or heart."
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	"Winds that enter between two ribs of the neck cause headaches, ophthalmia, migraine, choking sensation, and pain in the roots of the teeth,"
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	"And it is in the place of the basilica's cleansing; and you must command the surgeon that he expresses his hand upon placing [it], so that he does not cut the artery nor allow blood flow."
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	"Winds beneath the chin are beneficial for mouth diseases, gum decay, and similar ailments that affect the mouth; they are located at the level of the two lips."
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"Winds on the shoulders are beneficial for diseases caused by heat and excess."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	"The winds on the ribs are as useful as three veins of the arm,"
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	"because it draws blood from these large veins;"
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	"And command the surgeon not to dig too deep, for this place is devoid of flesh and contains nerves and arteries."
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	"The cupping glass placed on the buttock is beneficial for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below. The cupping glass must be large and made of earthenware so that it may draw well; otherwise, if it were too delicate, it would break and cause great wounds."
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	"The cupping glasses on the legs draw clearly because they attract blood from the whole body and are beneficial for old back pains, sciatica, bladder pain, and they strengthen the joints. They are located at the level of the two sophenes and the two ankles. However, prolonged use can weaken the body and cause swelling in certain dispositions."
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	"The method of applying the cupping glass is to first place it empty and suc
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	"And if the blood is thick, one must strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood."
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	"And if the blood is very thick, one must strike a third time. And when we wish to draw only a little blood at a time, it suffices to strike once."
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	"And if we wish for much blood, we must strike often. And if the blood is thick, one should dig deep, with the intent that the skin be pierced suddenly,"
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	"and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have close pores, to anoint the places of the cupping glasses with oil that is aperitive and dissolving:"
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	"If it is in summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;"
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	"And if it is winter, use mustard oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one."
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	"And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones."
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	"And if one is treating someone with tender flesh and large pores, there should be no oil used at all:"
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	"but afterwards, they must wash the cupping site with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar ones."
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	"And those who have too much moisture, they should rise from this with oil of sage, or myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things."
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	"And those who have thick superfluities should rise with old wine, or barley water, or a decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things;"
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	"And one should not apply cupping before bathing nor in the bath, but afterwards, an hour or two after. And do not sleep after cupping,"
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	"And they must be careful when they are about to be cupped and when they are being cupped."
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	"And beware if the person being treated is choleric, and if their blood is too abundant and inflamed;"
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	"for they should take cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce with vinegar, and similar things;"
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	"And eat fewer pulses, and castrated male lamb meat, and moist meats."
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	"And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and medium-sweet perfumed wine that is between old and new, and eat little, and eat fewer pulses, small birds, and pigeons;"
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	"And on the day they are being cupped, they should drink more than they eat;"
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	"It is necessary to give some people, sometimes, treacle or musk before cupping, or afterwards, to strengthen the main members;"
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	"And let the blood be thinned, but those who are hot should not drink it."
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	"The cupping glasses that are placed without striking are those that are placed on the liver, the stomach, podagra, and on the belly, the buttocks, the loins, and the haunch, for these members cannot withstand being struck upon."
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	"And this is only done to attract blood from one member to another,"
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	"such as when we place them on the breasts when nursing a child; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, such as when we place cupping glasses on the belly and buttocks to reduce the member;"
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	"and it relieves pain, when there is congestion or hardness, such as by its attractive virtue it might remove the congestion, or dislodge the hardness from its place;"
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	"And likewise, it does when placed on the liver and stomach when there is retained flatulence,"
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	"and these cupping glasses are administered empty to simply suck, and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water."
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	"such as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water only, or with water in which appropriate herbs have been cooked."
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	"The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:"
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	"And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on the side around the middle one small hole, like that of a needle;"
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	"And let it be made of brass, polished beforehand so that it does not burn the patient when placed upon the member;"
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	"And have in the middle a transverse rod of brass or iron to hold an enclosed candle;"
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	"And let them be both large and small according to the diseases and the strength of those who use them;"
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	"for the cupping glasses used on children are different from those used on old people, and those used on thin people are different from those used on fat ones."
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	"And one should place this cupping glass upon the member thus:"
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	"insert a candle made of wax or linen, and put it inside the cupping glass through the transverse rod that is inside the cupping glass,"
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	So that the light shines at the bottom of the cupping glass so it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then place it on the limb, with your two fingers over the hole we spoke of, so that when you want to remove the cupping glass, steam can escape.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And use the compress as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	Therefore, in the case of the cupping glass used for pleurisy or acute disease, there is no stem or hole, and it is only filled with water when it is full, and placed on the limb simply;
et c’est li forme:	"And this is the form:"
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	"Sutures are performed only in members where it is not possible to place cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas."
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	"And in bare flesh areas, like the thighs or shins, etc."
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	"And the qualities of urine are such that when you find it without impurities, which are in clear sweet waters without residue, then take it."
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	"And put them into fresh water until they become familiar [with their surroundings], and have nothing in their bellies;"
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	"Then perform leeching and cupping, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and apply the poultices."
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	"If they are full [with blood] and fall off, and if it is a place where you can apply cupping, apply it, for this is very beneficial."
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	"If not, then lift the skin up carefully with tweezers, and then wet it with water, and then squeeze it."
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	"And if the wounds are too near to the body of the wounded, then soak one linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the blood is stretched out."
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	"And if the blood is abundant, then place powdered vitriol or salt and similar substances on it until it is absorbed."
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	"Or you can put half a handful of peeled fava beans on the wound and leave them there until they absorb into the wound, then it will stop bleeding."
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	"And if more are needed, take others."
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	"And if the wounds will not heal, rub fresh blood on the wound and insert a needle until the blood comes out."
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	"Then they put [the cautery] on [the skin], and as soon as it feels the blood, it becomes hot;"
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	"And when you see that they blister, sprinkle on a little powdered aloe and rue, crushed together with some ash, so that they may stop blistering."
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	"This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for fracture and dislocation."
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	"Know, dear son, that foolish doctors neglect this chapter because they have never seen any of the old books nor read a single letter about it;"
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	"And for this reason the knowledge of our land is strange, for I never found anyone good in it;"
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	"and know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated this subject with experience and practice throughout my life;"
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	"And I have described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and summarized it at the end, clearly showing the shapes of the tools that are arranged as I did in these two preceding chapters."
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book that those who seek understanding and remain faithful to the truth should study these pages and chapters so that those who are experienced may learn and teach this noble art to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	"I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or contusion occurs to anyone, you must quickly examine the injured person on both sides if possible, unless there is some obstacle such as weakness of body or infancy or old age;"
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	"or if the time is not very warm or too cold; and do not eat cold foods, that is to say cold drinks, and flesh of birds and hares, nor drink wine nor eat fatty meats until you doubt the formation of hot matter or swelling in the limb. Then return the patient to their usual diet."
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to unite, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with foods that promote growth and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, fish, and red wine, and similar things."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For by such nourishment the bones are strengthened and the fracture heals more quickly."
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	"And know that the bones of the elderly and infirm do not heal well nor unite according to their nature due to stiffness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender such as the bones of young children;"
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	"But have patience and wait until the bone has healed before removing the splint. Then do not cut away any of the callus that has formed, for it is necessary to nourish the patient with fatty foods as we have said."
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse and manifold in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For a fracture of the head is different from one of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the various types of fractures."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"For there are fractures that occur suddenly, like those caused by a fall or blow, such as cutting a feather in half with scissors."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And some fractures come with wounds while others have only a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	"And each type of fracture has its own method and appropriate tool for reduction, according to how the limb comes into its proper place;"
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	"and a fracture of bone is recognized by its twisted appearance and clear separation at the break point when pressed with the hand;"
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	"and if there is no twisting or sound upon touching and the patient feels little pain, then there is no fracture."
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	"But it can still have torsion, a crack, or a small fracture."
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb yourself but apply the medicines mentioned below and then gently immobilize it with bandages."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	"And know that fractures that occur suddenly and cause dislocation of two parts must be realigned evenly before hot matter collects at the site;"
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	"and if hot matter collects, allow it to cool for some days until the inflammation subsides;"
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	"then realign the limb gently and evenly and know that reduction is easier in such cases than those with disarticulation. Then immobilize it as necessary."
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	"And if there are fragments of bone broken off, then extend the limb on either side if it is an arm or leg, or grasp it with your hand for smaller members, or use two strings or one string and your hand;"
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	"and align the limb according to its natural shape so that when the broken parts are disarticulated, gently replace them in their proper places without causing injury or pain to the patient;"
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	"And carefully fit together the two ends of the bone according to the best shapes."
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"And feel with your hand whether it is well aligned or not: if it does not seem so, then straighten the limb gently without immobilizing it too tightly nor pressing on it as some do to cause inflammation and contracture of the limb, as we have said many times before."
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	"And when the limb is properly aligned, then instruct the patient to keep it still and not move it while awake or asleep, turning in bed, or in any other way;"
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	"and make sure that the limb is securely immobilized so that there is no pain."
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	"For if there is any pain, then it is not properly aligned, and you must place the limb in such a position that there is no pain;"
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	"And make sure that it is placed correctly so that there are no twists when it is reduced;"
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	"And the quality of a fracture depends on what I have told you."
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that fractured limbs are diverse in size, length, and shape."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	"For small members such as arms, legs, and similar ones must be wrapped with soft, thin linen cloths;"
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	"And large members such as thighs and legs must be wrapped with wide, firm bandages because they encircle the entire limb evenly without any gaps;"
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	"then wind it with light bandages three or four times according to the size of the limb and tighten your hand slightly around the entire bandage. Then go above the fracture site and loosen the bandage a little so that the fracture gap opens a bit;"
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	"and soften the bandage gradually until you grasp much of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wind it again around the fracture site;"
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	"then go back to the area below the fracture and immobilize it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said earlier;"
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	"then place linen or cloth bandages between the layers of bandage so that it is all even, then secure everything with one final bandage, and finally apply well-made splints if there is no inflammation or swelling."
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	"If there is inflammation or heat at the fracture site, apply something to reduce inflammation and heat, then leave it on for some days;"
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	"then immobilize with your splints, which should be half the width of a large cane or staff, or made from palm ribs, and they should look like this:"
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	"But the splint placed directly over the fracture site must be slightly thicker and wider than the others;"
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	"And it should also be long enough to fit the size of the limb;"
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	"then immobilize with splints just like you did in the first layer over the fracture site, then secure it with linen bandages as before;"
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	It is narrower above, always less so; and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is too thick, as I have seen some foolish workers do who tie their laces with twisted linen cords, which is a great mistake; for the lace cannot be even if it is too fine, and it must not be less than two fingers wide between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the edges of the stitches after tightening in place, then put underneath them wads of linen or wool gauze so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that you should not tighten all the bandages on the broken limb immediately on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, you should not put on bandages until after five or six days have passed, or more according to the heat of the swelling.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and behold here is the manner of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations and twists: take of gum arabic and myrrh and aloe and aloeswood, each .v. oz.; frankincense, also .v. oz; galangal, viij. oz; and grind them into powder, mixing it with albumen from an egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and swiftly restores broken bones, useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method for treating dislocation: take mugwort and wormwood, each .X. grams; myrrh and aloe, each .VIII. grams; achyronacia six grams; Armenian bole ten grams, grind well, mix with vinegar or egg white, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method for dislocations and bones displaced from their places, to alleviate pain and inflammation, soften hard bones and reduce fractures: take fresh flaxseed, soak it in sour whey and warm oil, apply it on the location. This plaster does not restore dislocation but is good for alleviating heat inflammation and removes pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat broken bones: Take dried fig leaves and earth peony leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way to make a poultice for setting broken bones and easing the pain of bruises. Take equal parts of valerian root, chamomile flowers, violet flowers, and wheat flour; grind them together and mix with wine. If the limb is inflamed, mix instead with coriander water or water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	"Another method for stronger poultice than the first one, when hard abscess comes to restore the limb. Take roots of mugwort and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and sanicle, flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; grind, mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the limb and its rest."
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	"Hippocrates writes in his book that one should apply to the broken limb only cerate made from wax and oil, with nothing else added. He says it should be neither too soft nor too hard."
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	"And it seems Galen that one should apply to the broken limb for restoration dry things a little warm, like myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar substances, as we have said."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	"Another method for poultice that is good for wound and pain: take mullein leaves, chicken feathers or hairs of shaven men, mugwort and common sow thistle in equal parts, grind them, mix with the grease."
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	"And then remove it after a while, and make sure that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place. If so, do not remove it for several days."
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	"And if pain or itching comes to the place, with restlessness or swelling, then hurry up and remove it, and take away the poultice immediately. Then take a light cloth, damp sea sponge, dip it in water and apply it to the place until the itching stops and the pain is relieved."
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	"Then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply warm linen moistened in water or rose oil and wrap it around tightly until you are sure of having a hot boil."
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And let the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain be relieved, then resume the gentle wrapping, with a little poultice, without pulling too tight as before. Do this until it is completely healed."
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	"And if you see that the boil is hot and red and painful and swollen have all disappeared, and you need poultice and wrapping again, then resume it, just as you did at first."
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	"And if none of the things we have mentioned happens to the limb, do not remove it before three or four or five days have passed; sometimes you can leave it on for twenty days, depending on what you see, until the bone has healed and the flesh joins together."
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	"Then the wrapping should be tighter than before, and the flesh will grow bigger, as I have said earlier. But if you see that the place is drying out too much, know that no nutrition can come to it."
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	"Then apply hot water compresses every time you remove it, every third day, and loosen the wrapping a little."
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	"Through this treatment, nourishment will come to the limb quickly, and it will correct what foolish doctors do, who reset a limb incorrectly: that is bad, and they are cowardly, and I see no other way than to leave it alone and work correctly."
des diverses manieres de brisure	"Regarding the various ways bones can break:"
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	"There are many different types of bone fractures, with diverse shapes, each having its own causes;"
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	"Some fractures are caused by blows from a sword or an axe that cuts through the bone completely down to the marrow, like wood being chopped. This type of fracture is called 'haichure'."
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	"Or the sword cuts across the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called 'absolute'; both these fractures have large or small wounds."
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	"And if there is impact with embossed blows, or splitting or crushing from stones, or falls onto stones, or other similar causes."
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	"And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the periosteum under the bone or goes through it, this type of fracture has large or small wounds."
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	"And if there is a wound that penetrates into the bone as thinly as a hair, this is called a 'capillary' fracture because it is very small."
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	"And if the wound caused by a blow from stone or fall or similar enters the bone and pushes the bone fragment downwards, causing it to rise up like a cauldron being beaten on its sides, then the stones are trapped inside."
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	"This happens more often in those whose bones have moist heads, such as children's skulls;"
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	"And it occurs with all types of fractures where small fragments are broken off like stars. I will speak about this in its proper place."
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	"And we recognize all kinds of fractures by their displacement, inspection, and the corrupted flesh that is on them."
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	"A capillary fracture is recognized because when the bone is uncovered and rubbed with a finger, the fracture appears black."
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	"In treating a fracture, beware of complications from illness. If you see no signs of bad accidents such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, spasms, fever, eyes protruding and turning red, or other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt."
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	"But if you don't see any frightening accidents and hope for a good outcome, then begin the treatment."
