Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	"And when an injured person first comes to you in wintertime, it is necessary to reset the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury."
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	"And if it is in summertime, hurry to reset the bone before the seventh day, so that the periosteum under the bone does not become corrupted and the accidents we mentioned do not occur."
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	"And if the bone fracture reaches the periosteum that covers the brain, it is necessary for you to split the broken part in this way: take the head of the sick person and uncover the bone in every possible way, being especially gentle around the wound site."
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	"And if blood comes out or a large swelling forms when uncovering the bone, help it with what is necessary. Then fill the place with bandages moistened in rose oil."
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	"And let the wound rest until the swelling has subsided and you are sure that there is no bleeding. Then start resetting the bone in one of two ways:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he applies another cut, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is to have many cuts of varying sizes, some narrow and others wide, all pointed and made of fine iron. Work carefully so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	If the bone is hard and strong, it is necessary to drill around it before making cuts with chisels, taking care not to cut too deeply so that they pierce through the soft bone of the skull. Each chisel should have a guard or circle on top to prevent the point from penetrating too far into the bone. You should have several chisels so that each one fits properly in its place along the length of the bone, allowing you to have chisels for all types of skulls. These are the three ways to shape chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To drill around the fractured bone, place one chisel on the bone and twist it with your hands until you feel that the bone has been pierced. Then move the chisel to another location a little further away and continue drilling all around the bone. Next, use incising chisels to remove the strip of bone between the holes, working as carefully and gently as possible so that you can easily grasp the bone with your hands or with tools such as tongs or forceps. Be sure not to touch the cerebellum or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	Once you have drilled and removed the bone, it is necessary to scrape away any remaining thin layer of bone using an instrument resembling an incising chisel but finer and more delicate than others.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	If any small bones or bone fragments remain, carefully remove them using appropriate instruments. Then clean the wound with bandages and dressings as described earlier.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	The other method is that of Galen, which is quicker and involves using strong pressure, as he himself stated.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone where the break appears moved so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place underneath the head of this lenticular incision tool, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharp on both sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small hammer so that you barely touch the bone all around, and be careful of the tissue underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adherent to the bone, then scrape it gently off, for one can scrape it well without harm or injury.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not reach to the tissue, and the bone is only cut on top with small pieces, then cover that unevenness and remove the bone flakes with a fine razor file of which you should have several quantities to adapt best to each location according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Then use coarse rasps first, and afterwards finer ones, until it is smooth enough.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each of the other types of capillary cuts and subtle breaks, you must adapt your approach according to its direction; this is not something that can be learned by someone who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sinew is exposed, then you should take one linen cloth according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled in two or three folds, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this gently so as not to injure the sinew, then apply another bandage on top, but do not tie it too tightly, only enough to keep it in place.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it like this for one or two days until the inflammation has subsided, then untie it and apply medications such as lily roots, violet flour, incense powder, aloe vera, and similar substances; grind these into a powder and apply it to the wound, then apply healing medications without causing injury.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment in it or let any dust gather on it, for when dust gathers on the brain's tissue, it causes inflammation and carries harm to the patient; anything placed on sinew that is too harsh will cause necrosis above it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be very careful if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, and do not hesitate to doubt yourself.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness appears on the outside due to the medication applied, then take one part honey and three parts rose oil, mix them together with a cloth, and apply it to the sinew;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then continue treating him according to the appropriate methods until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose are broken at once, or just one by itself, for there are two bones there; the lower one is cartilage and does not break unless it is hit hard or twisted, but then it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then insert your little finger or a probe into the nose and place it evenly on the break at the base of the index finger, pushing outward until the nose regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	Do this gently and ensure that the patient does not feel pain due to your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then use a small rod about as thick as your finger to align it properly.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then do the same, and try to restore it on the first day if possible.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, then on the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, insert linen strips into the nostrils if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or insert another strip on the other side if the break is there; ensure that the strips are thick enough to fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Some restorers say that the strips should be moistened in butter and changed every day. I do not think this is good practice, but they should be moistened with a concoction of egg albumen and millstone powder; then leave the strip in place until the bone has healed and the cartilage has hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Sometimes feathers from a goose are used instead of strips, with a soft cloth wrapped around them to keep the break in place while the patient breathes through it; do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if inflammation occurs in the nose while you are working on it, then insert softened wax or cotton moistened with rose oil or a little diacylgonine.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if inflammation does not occur, then apply a plaster made of sesame flour and incense powder mixed with egg albumen from behind; use light bandages and do not tie the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the nose is broken into small pieces, extract them with appropriate instruments, then stitch the wound closed and treat it with healing substances such as plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with strips and apply splints until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below and there is no wound on the outside, and the break is only on the outside with no fracture inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side of the jawbone, insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if it is on the left side, use your right hand and gently insert your index finger behind the break, then align it with your other hand from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is displaced in two places, then provide traction on both sides until it is aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth are displaced or broken due to movement of the jawbone fracture, then fix them with a gold, silver, or silk thread. Apply wax on the broken jawbone and place a doubled cloth over it; then put a well-made splint or a piece of leather on top, matching the length and width of the jawbone, secure it to the cheek where possible, and instruct the patient to rest and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the alignment has changed, remove it on the third day and reposition it correctly. Apply a plaster made of flour mixed with egg albumen or sesame flour after removing the wax; then apply light linen over it. If the plaster remains effective and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals, which usually takes three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if inflammation occurs, administer the treatments we have mentioned many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, ensure that no piece of bone is missing; carefully remove it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have removed all these pieces and there are none left, then sew the wound closed if it is wide, and apply some bandages to prevent infection until it heals.
de la forcele	With tweezers
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The shoulder blade can break several times in front, towards the shoulder, and there are three ways this fracture can occur:
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	"And the work is such when there's no wound, that you should have two assistants: one to hold the arm which feels broken; and the other stretch the neck towards the part. Then place the break evenly on your two hands so that its shape is as it should be, without appearance or displacement."
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	"And if you need to stretch further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of cloth or wool, and its size according to your necessity. Then extend and lift the arm, gripping the ball with your hand so that you can align the break evenly as it should be."
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	"And if you cannot pull the head of the arm forward because it is deeply set, then the patient must lie on their back and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder. Then push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the arm is lifted."
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	"And then align the break with your two hands. If it is displaced, you must cut above it. Gently pull out the pieces and if the bone cannot meet due to any obstacle, cut one of the incisions that you have made. But place this instrument under the arm to support the joint:"
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	"And it should resemble a spoon and not be too high, with its width fitting the size of the bone and the nature of the work. It should have two holes: one wide and one narrow, corresponding to the shape of the wound you made when removing the bones:"
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	"And once you are sure that there is no hot inflammation, then close the wound. If the opening is small or if you doubt there is any hot inflammation, fill the wound with bandages and cloths according to its size."
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	"And if hot inflammation occurs, soak a bandage in rose oil mixed with honey and vinegar, and place it on top."
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	"The dressing for a bone that is without wounds or cuts is to place on the bone a plaster made of flour and ground egg white. Then apply light dressings and place a round ball under the elbow if necessary."
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	"Then take a very wide bandage about a palm's length long. Place a doubled cloth on top of the dressings and plaster. Then take a thin strip of linen about three fingers wide and long enough to wrap around this bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down."
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	"And place the strip of linen over the break. Then wrap the bandage around the neck and under the healthy shoulder and under the injured shoulder. Tuck in each end securely. When you see that the bandage holds the break well and the strip of linen does not move from its position on the broken bone, then change it daily. And when the swelling decreases, then tighten it."
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	"And make the injured person lie on their back and place a small pillow under their elbow when they sleep to lift the joint upward. Lighten the break by lifting the shoulder or tying the arm to the neck for up to twenty days if no misfortune occurs."
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	"Then start the dressing again if necessary, and continue until it is healed. It usually takes twenty-eight days to heal, but sometimes less time for some people."
de la brisure de l’espaule	"About the break of the shoulder:"
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	"It may happen that the shoulder blade breaks but does not show externally and cannot be felt except by touch. Therefore, it must be treated according to its shape and bound according to its natural form in every possible way. Then place flour mixed with ground egg white on the bone, followed by light dressings and a doubled cloth. Next, place a wide and thin strip of linen slightly wider than the shoulder blade on top, using pieces of linen bandages to fill any hollows under the strip if necessary. Then bind it firmly with a large bandage so that the strip does not move from its position. Check the dressing daily and tighten it whenever it loosens, repositioning the strip if it shifts. Make the patient lie on their side. The shoulder blade usually heals in twenty to twenty-five days. But once this time has passed, do not remove the bandage too soon, as the bone does not easily mend."
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	"And if a fragment of the bone sticks out and is not under the heart, then cut it off and proceed as we have said in treating the fracture of the collarbone to appease any hot inflammation."
de la brisure dou pis	"About the break of the arm:"
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	"The arm is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely. However, it often breaks at the elbow. When it breaks in the middle, it tends to bend downwards and causes severe pain, loss of sensation, weakness, and sometimes vomiting of blood. The hollows around the broken bone become visible and can be felt."
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back with a cushion between the shoulders. Then press the shoulders down and bring together the ribs of the two lower sides gently but firmly until the bones are aligned correctly. Then place dressings and bandages over a thin strip of salt or light wood, wrap it in cloth, and bind it to the broken bone so that it does not move. Wrap the bandage around the back and tie it securely. Check the dressing every hour and tighten it if it loosens. If it needs to be removed due to corrosion, itching, pain, or inflammation, do so quickly and reapply a new dressing. Then bind it again until it is healed."
de la brisure des costes	"About the break of the ribs:"
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	"Know that rib fractures only occur in large areas of the back and chest. They are not broken except by blows to these areas and can be felt clearly upon examination."
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	"And the treatment is that you align the break correctly and apply dressings, binding it with a bandage if necessary."
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	"And if the rib fracture leans inwards, the patient feels great pain and sharpness like that of pleurisy because the bone pierces the lung. They experience shortness of breath, weakness, and vomiting of much blood. This is a serious condition, and the ancients considered it deadly."
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	"And there are those who say that one should administer foods that cause the belly to swell in order to push the fracture back into place."
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	"We do not do this because hot inflammation may arise if it has not already been present."
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	"But if it is already present, we treat it."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	"And some say that one should place cups on the area to draw out blood forcefully, and this seems reasonable. However, there is doubt whether the cups attract impurities to the site due to the weakness of the body."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And some say that one should cover the area with a warm woolen cloth moistened in oil and place splints between the ribs to align the fracture, then treat it like pleurisy with foods and medicines."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure due to the bone piercing the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the location of the broken rib, and place one instrument underneath to guard the spleen; and then one must chip away at the bone and draw it out gently, and afterwards sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and cleanse with poultices until it is healed. And if an abscess comes afterwards, then place moistened dressings in rose oil on the location, and keep them there; and treat that location as necessary for an abscess, and have the patient lie constantly on their side where they should be until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a break of the bone of the neck occur, and rarely does it bend; and also with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and numb, and they cannot move nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that he is mortally wounded in many ways, and if he moves them and feels well when they are restrained and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be healed, if care is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if the feet are softened, and if there is any accident that is in their hands, and wind comes up on the back without control; and when one has them lying on their stomach, it also comes out without control. And when they are lying on their back and want to rise, they cannot do so. Know that he is mortally wounded: do not labor in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then it is the lesser of the two evils.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you watch if there is any hot abscess, then put rose oil or linseed oil on the spine until it is appeased; then put one of the comforting and drying poultices on it, and hold it down with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel the pain until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone comes out of joint, then cover the chest; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one stitch, then treat it with ointment for internal wounds until it is healed. And if the bone of the knee is broken, which is called the 'knee cap', put your left hand's pouch on it and hold it even with the other hand by force, then put the poultice and splint on it if necessary; then bind it up, and if there are any bones out of joint, open them up and remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	And concerning the breaking of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It can happen that the thighbone is broken, and if it happens, there will be little harm to the head. And it opens up on the long side, and inclines toward the parting of the thighs, and pain and soreness come to the person where it breaks, and it swells at that place.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you stretch your hand out until you are over the break. And know what the break is like and its shape. And if the break is only at the top, then put it back in place until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is on the long side or inclines inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that you can clearly see the restoration of that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back in place, then put a poultice on it, then put a splint made of wood or bone on it and bind the break so that it does not move. And hold the area under the ribs until the bandage is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if any hot abscess comes, do not touch it until the hot abscess is appeased. And then put on what we have said before. And then return to the restoration and bind it as it should be, if there are no bad accidents. And that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	And concerning the breaking of the elbow
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The elbow is that which is between the arm and the shoulder blade. And if it is broken, it should be restored in one of two ways: either by taking a piece of smooth wood like this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two pieces of wood together with two ropes and hang them up high. And make the patient sit on a chair. Then lay their broken arm on the wood so that it hangs down and rests in a curve of wood. Then put some heavy weight or let the minister pull it down. Then the master should put the break back in place with both hands until it is correctly aligned.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that one places the patient on their back, and they lay their hand on their neck, then commands two helpers: one to hold what is above the break of their hands, and the other to hold below all in one line, stretching each one to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then stretch one line below the break and another above it, each helper to their part. And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary to put one line in the middle under the axilla, and another towards the side, under the break; likewise if the break is towards the side, it is necessary to gently place a light line without labor until the break is level on its place and on the side; then set the break level as it should be and stretch it, so that no inflammation comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if inflammation occurs, do not stretch it until the twenty-seventh day, and put a warm moist cloth on the axilla and rose oil until the inflammation is appeased; then stretch it, and the manner of stretching is as follows: place the splint on the break, then bring the arm onto the supporter, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the bandage, and stretch it onto the supporter and onto the arm so that the arm is in line with the stars, if nothing prevents it from being stretched, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, then use stars (traction devices) and place a larger and stronger star on the break than the others, with two fingers' space between each star, and let each star be large enough to pass the break three fingers from each side; then stretch onto the stars, as I said at the beginning of this chapter about stretching on the break, but more strongly and without pulling apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the base of the stars and the stretching as we have said when restoring the broken limb, and you suspect inflammation, then leave it alone for seven days as we have said; then examine the bandage every three days to make sure that there is no pruritus or swelling around it, or that the member does not suffer from stiffness because the bandage is too tight. Then adjust it as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient lie on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place one cushion full of wool evenly underneath the supporter, and watch every hour of the day or night to make sure that the figure of the broken limb does not move or become loosened. Then adjust it by means of medication, and give the patient food as we have mentioned earlier, so that at first the food is subtle, and then becomes thicker when they begin to recover. And it is customary for the supporter and the leg to be removed after forty days in total; then one should remove the bandage and administer baths and ointments to complete the healing. And if the scar is ugly and depressed, then it may take ten days or two months to remove the bandage.
de la brisure du bras	Here is a possible translation of the passage on "la brisure du bras" (breakage of the arm) from the medical treatise "Cirurgia" by Guy de Chauliac:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones called the two "fuscile", one of which is small and extends to the wrist; the other is large and located beneath towards the little toe. Sometimes only the large "fuscile" breaks, or sometimes only the small one does, and occasionally both together do so.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, restoration is easy, as well as healing; but when the large one is broken, healing is difficult and more serious than when both are broken together. If it's only the small bone that is broken, it must be extended a little and aligned correctly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large bone that is broken, then it must be pulled more forcefully; and it should be stretched over a cushion, with the hand lifted higher than the others, and the little toe lower than the other toes, and the patient crossed upon himself, and a cushion placed before him to prevent any effort. Then the surgeon stretches his own arm below his hand or at one lien, and another surgeon holds onto another lien above. And then the surgeon sets it straight according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces missing, then each must be placed back in its proper place. If any piece is still unable to grasp the heart, and cannot be restored to its original position, then one should cut above and below the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is also a wound, I have spoken of it in the chapter on special cases; so take care accordingly.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the restoration swelling occurs, then take a bandage of waxed linen made from rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft, and tie it gently on top so that the swelling diminishes. Then remove the linen, and apply the plaster of ground mallow with plenty of egg, then place the splints, ensuring that the splint at the break is stronger and a little wider than the others. Know that there should be six splints on the arm in various arrangements: whether the break is in one bone or two; and bind more tightly above the break than elsewhere, and always loosen a little when aligning it, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages that are on the break be soft and moist, not hard nor harsh; and let the thread used for binding be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And check the member and the ligature after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accident occurs to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you should anoint the member with warm water until this itching is appeased; and let the member rest, not too tightly bound. Then begin the binding again, and if the ligature is softened and the bone still unsetted, or similar things occur, then address them accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you are careful that the nourishment cannot reach the member because it is too tightly bound, then you should loosen it a little and let it rest like this for a few days until the nourishment comes to it, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not undo the ligature until 20 days or thereabouts have passed, and then let him hang his hands around his neck, keeping his shoulders level, and take care against movement and straining, and sleep on his back. Know that this break will be restored in 30 to 35 days, or perhaps even fewer, depending on the compositions and temperaments of humors.
de la brisure de la main	Chapter 21: On the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and also on the forearms there are few fractures, but many dislocations occur.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or dislocated, then let the patient sit cross-legged and sit upright directly in front of him, evenly; then place his hand on a cloth laid out flat, and extend the broken bones by the minister, and join them evenly by the master, so that they are well-aligned. Then apply the plaster and splints if there is no swelling present, then place one splint according to the size of the affected area; and let it be wrapped in a linen bandage.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	"And if the fracture is on the inner side around the belly of the foot, make a bandage of cloths and instruct the patient to press it onto their broken foot; then hold it with a long cloth strip, and let the knot be soft as large as the sole of the hand, and secure it in place."
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	"And if the fracture is on the backside, then you must place a bandage above and another below in the sole of the foot so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the hand, and make sure the binding between the two is secure."
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	"And if the fracture occurs at any of our fingers, if it's the thumb, then align it properly; and bind it with the sole of the foot, and if you see fit place a small, straight splint to elevate the fracture and prevent movement. And if the fracture is on another finger, such as the index or one of the others, then align it and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together in one binding, whichever is better, or place a splint above like on the thumb; and beware of inflammation and arrange for hot poultice treatment, and secure whatever comes from it, as I have said."
de la cuixe brisie	"About a broken thighbone:"
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	"The thighbone is often broken and it is evident when it rotates forward or backward; and the treatment for this is to bind one tie above the fracture and another below."
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	"And the patient lies on their face, then each of the attendants extends his tie to his side equally; this is when the fracture is within the bone."
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	"And if the fracture is near the root of the thighbone, one tie should be placed towards the knee and the others below the fracture. And likewise if it is near the knee joint, then the ties should be placed near the knee with the extension downward; then the physician aligns the bone with both hands until it is in its natural shape, and then applies splints and bandages if no inflammation occurs."
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	"And if there is heat inflammation, allow it to subside before returning to your work and treatment; the binding is done in this manner."
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	"It is necessary that you wrap a hard, doubled bandage around the fracture twice or thrice, and remove any superfluities; then rotate the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the navel, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg near the knee below, and bring the ends up above; then wrap the bandage around the leg and thigh again, placing splints on the fracture and one on the shinbone; then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to make the binding even, then begin tying firmly three or four times above the fracture, and as you go higher, tie less tightly; then take the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread until you reach the foot, and bind it so that it does not move from its place; then leave it like that until no inflammation or swelling occurs."
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	"And if inflammation occurs, untie it and address whatever comes from it, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they should be removed if possible; and if not, then the space should be split open and pus drawn out; and treat it as we have said until it is healed."
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	"And sometimes the thighbone is fractured in such a way that splints are placed on it, as in the case of the arm; nevertheless, the patient does not limp when the fracture is treated in this manner."
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	"And know that the thighbone is restored in about one month, or a little less or more, according to the different constitutions."
de la ruelle dou genoil	"About the knee joint"
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	You know that the tendon of the knee often breaks but bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a crack or one hole, and this happens with every wound, even without a wound, and everyone feels this.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is like this: put what is broken back onto its two sides so that it can be assembled and moved. Then put on a splint, and if necessary, use a rounded staple to hold it in place, then tighten as needed. Then rewrap all the bandages we mentioned earlier for other fractures, such as hot compresses and similar treatments. Put whatever treatment is appropriate for each condition so that it heals properly.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that there are two bones in the leg, one of which is correctly called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and all kinds of fractures happen to it just as they do in the arm, and therefore its restoration is performed in the same way as that of the arm, and the work is done entirely.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken at once, then the leg is turned all around.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the "mustelz" bone is broken, it turns inward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	"And if the large bone is broken, great pain is felt and it is clearly visible; and it turns underneath. Then prepare an extension, place it evenly, and bind the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the break is ugly and there are many pieces, let the extension be less strong and lighter; and move it according to your ability."
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when you have completed your task, then take two strips of wood, hollowed out to fit around the leg on either side, and long enough from just below the knee downwards. Then wrap each strip with a bandage above and below, tie them together in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, which is good; some people also use one splint made of wood, long enough for the leg, and place it there to prevent movement, especially where there is a wound. And every day move the leg gently to see if there is any heat or other infection. Until then, continue treating until it is healed."
de la brisure des os dou piet	"On the breaking of bones in the foot"
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	"The ankle does not experience any fractures, but sometimes a bone in the foot and the toes can be broken, and there is often contusion in various positions."
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	"And if there is a fracture of the bone in the foot and you see the bones protruding one over the other, then place your foot on the ground like someone who wants to walk, and put your own foot now on his where the bones are raised. Then press down until they return to their original position; then apply the splint and padding. Place a small tray with two holes under the sole of the foot, then strap it tightly around the foot with bandages and other necessary materials."
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	"And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage because you will find that the bones are aligned again, whether they were broken or dislocated."
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	"And if there are any broken toes, then set them back in place as we have described for the fingers of the hand. Then place a splint along the length of the toe and slightly wider. Place the tray that I mentioned under the foot and strap it tightly around it. If there are two or three or more broken toes, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a cloth of linen, and strap the tray under the foot. And let them rest on top of the tray so that they are well supported."
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	"And you should not forget the other things that we have mentioned for other fractures. Treat each case according to its nature."
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	"On the fracture of the bone of the wrist"
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, let her sit with her legs outstretched, then lean her toward the back part, and have her held from behind. Then fill the cavity of the nature with cotton, and put in as much as one stone. Then lift the woman up little by little on the back, and then the cotton will rise until it reaches the entrance of the nature, and the bone will return with the stone. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it, and do this for about seven days or so: thus the break will be healed. And if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a tube to its opening, and put the entire bladder inside the nature. Then blow into the tube forcefully until the bladder swells inside. The nature will then return to its original state; then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the hand of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the thighbone; and those who apply themselves to this art and understand my book will not find these nearby breaks hidden. For breaking means more than one way of restoring the right path: therefore listen carefully.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	For a broken penis, take a goose's gut and put it around the penis. Then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three or four days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	If there is a break with an open wound:
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	He who has a fracture with wound, especially if it is large, as in the thigh bone or shoulder bone or similar, should be bandaged now, so that the bandages we have mentioned witness this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, you should then rinse with vinegar, or with whatever else you have available, and immediately afterwards reset the fracture that same hour, or on the following day, if a physician is not present.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a physician is present, then wait until the ninth day to reset the fracture, until the inflammation has subsided. Do not touch it on the third or fourth day either, for you would thereby cause an evil outcome
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone fracture is apparent above the chest and exposed, then it is necessary for you to carefully align it with your hands, with minimal extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not sufficient to align it with your hands, then use this tool made of iron, which is either twenty-seven or eighteen inches long, and its width should correspond to the size of the wound. It is necessary for a physician to mold three or four of these tools according to what is needed in each case of fracture; it should be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend under pressure on the member being treated, and it should have a pointed end and be thicker at its midpoint, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called a "palainche," because the leg should be placed on the head of the visible bone; push it once until it aligns with its counterpart. And if the fracture is fine and the tool cannot grip the bone properly, then you must cut off the end of the bone so that the tool can grasp it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you are unable to realign the bone as previously mentioned, then use an appropriate tool such as a chisel or knife to cut it with all your might. Then, remove any remaining sharp edges and small splinters from the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is realigned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position. Make sure it is in its proper place, then moisten a cloth with black stiptic wine and apply it properly if it is summer time; do not put any cerate or other oily substance on the wound, for it will cause corruption and gangrene. Then apply bandages after you have reset the bone, leaving the wound exposed, and cut away the surrounding skin according to the size of the wound. Be sure that the dressing does not compress the fracture; many foolish physicians have done this, causing harm or death to the patient. Let the bandage be softer and lighter than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large and you fear that some harm may come of it, as we have mentioned earlier, and if there is pain in the area, then do not apply bandages; instead, wrap it with hard cloths and tie them. After two or three days, remove what you placed on it with wine, and apply healing ointment to the wound, such as tetrafarmacon ointment or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must massage the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is warm and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	"And the limb must be positioned in such a way that the bowstring runs down easily."
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	"And even if many days pass and the bone still cannot unite but again dislocates, know that there are small fragments of bone causing this pain, so you must treat the wound with a compress and remove all these unwanted fragments."
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	"And if a fistula appears at the site or other signs of corruption, you must treat it according to what is said in the chapter above. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, as with the thighbone or shinbone and similar large bones, do not attempt to extract it, but let it be until it rots; perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if not, leave it alone."
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	"from the bruises that come from the soldering"
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.
