"We often inquire about the health of the limb after a fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb can be unpleasant; sometimes the limb cannot perform its natural functions."
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	"Therefore, be careful if the bone is fresh: if the limb swells up, apply medicines that are astringent, such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others. Take any of these things or all together and mix them with wine that is astringent or with egg yolk or with vinegar; then place it on the swelling in bandages, and tie it tightly and do not untie it for several days; then remove it and start again until the swelling has disappeared. Or you can tie it around a piece of well-made lead; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from limbs. And if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it open on top and remove the excess flesh. Or have it shaved by some barber until it is gone, and treat it until it is healed."
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	"of the limb that is weak after a dressing"
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored,
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat,
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	"When a limb is twisted after an injury,"
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	"If a limb is twisted after healing, and the bone breaks open, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and such procedures are blameworthy, and great evils arise from them, and even death may result. Nevertheless, if the dislocations and twistings are fresh, then they ought to be fomented with hot water, or mollifying herbs should be cooked, like willow leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make one mollifying plaster, like diacylгон well-made, and take the musk of willow, and confect it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply the plaster; or take figs and grind them with coltsfoot leaves and similar medicines that soften the union.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	"And sometimes the dislocation is removed by continuously rubbing for a long time with moist hands. And arrange for the limb to be moved every hour."
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	"And if the twistedness is old and hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed by iron, then it should be cut down to the bone with a delicate and light scalpel; and pay close attention and take care in treating it."
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	"Here begins the book of dislocations"
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	"A dislocation occurs when a joint is displaced from its proper place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, and the patient feels great pain and great injury."
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	"When dislocation happens to anyone, it should be immediately reduced without delay."
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	"For if one delays, the place becomes inflamed, and perhaps it cannot be put back in its proper place; therefore one should not move it while it is inflamed: often this brings about spasms and other pains."
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	"Nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be put to bed and left alone until the inflammation has subsided; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently move it back into place, and treat each limb as its joint comes back into position."
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	"And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet."
des mandibules	"jaw dislocation"
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	"Rarely does the jaw become dislocated outward, and there are two kinds of dislocation in both cases: either it is slightly displaced from its proper place and softened a little; or it is completely dislocated and hangs down towards the chest, so that saliva flows out of the mouth and he cannot hold it in nor close his mouth, and he wraps his tongue with speech."
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	"When the dislocation is small, it returns to its proper place through several positions."
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	"And if it is complete and entire, then you must quickly reduce it without delay."
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	"And in this manner the attendant should hold the patient's head, and the physician place a pouch from one of his hands at the root of the jaw dislocation within the mouth, if the dislocation is two-part; and let the other two hands be free to balance it; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions."
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	"And the physician places it back in its proper place until it returns to its original position."
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	"If the dislocation is severe, especially if it affects both jaws simultaneously, then apply warm water and oil soaks until the dislocated parts become slightly softened; do not force the reduction, as we have said."
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	"And when the dislocated parts are properly reduced and the patient's mouth is closed gently without softening it again, apply warm compresses made from oil of roses and wax, then lightly secure them with soft bandages."
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	"Then let the patient lie on his back with two pillows between his thighs so that he does not move to the right or left and does not try to chew, but takes only light food until the pain subsides and the jaws are healed."
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	"And then let him eat whatever he wishes with ease and avoid opening his mouth widely while eating or drinking until the jaws are fully healed."
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	"And if the two jaws cannot be reduced properly within an hour and are not returned to their original position, then fever and other constitutional symptoms may arise, sometimes diarrhea, sometimes vomiting of bile."
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	"When you see these signs, know that it is a serious condition; many people die from this within nine days."
de la forcelle	"of the jawbone"
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	"The jawbone cannot dislocate inwards along its length and within the throat; however, it can sometimes be dislocated outwards at the chin, which is quite noticeable."
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	"And the reduction is performed by having the patient lie on his back with arms extended; then press firmly with your palm against the displaced part until it returns to its proper place. Apply a bandage and secure it in place."
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	"And the jawbone that faces the cheek cannot dislocate. If it does so rarely, then reduce it back to its proper position as we have described. Then apply a bandage and secure it in place, and tell the patient to rest until healed."
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	"And similarly, the jawbone of the spine is reduced when it is dislocated from its proper position."
de la dislocation de l’espaule	"On shoulder dislocation"
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder dislocates in only three ways: one is that it dislocates at the part of the hip below; and the second is at the part of the breastbone; and rarely it may dislocate above.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inward for the nerves; and often it dislocates below towards the hipbone, especially in those who have little flesh, for they jump quickly; but in those with sufficient flesh, it jumps scarcely and returns scarcely.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that there is an injury or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot boil, and they believe that it has dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must examine it until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And dislocation is recognized when it is down towards the hipbone, and there is a distinction made between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the hipbone when touching the top of the shoulder it feels like an egg; and the sick person cannot bring their hand near to their neck, nor move in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly upon touching.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is only for reduction when it is recent or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the physician lifts the sick person's hand upwards, then places their elbows under the buttocks and pulls the joint forcibly upwards; and the physician lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it beneath, it will quickly return.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come back as we have said within several days afterwards, then the sick person must be bathed in warm water; and the physician should apply gently softening and soothing plasters, such as decoction of ale, fenugreek, and mallow in water, and they should be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then the sick person should be put to sleep on their back, and place under the buttocks a pillow of linen neither too soft nor too hard, then the physician places their heel upon the pillow and gently raises the diseased shoulder and pulls the hand of the sick person.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another physician should hold the head of the sick person so that it does not move downwards; then this shoulder will quickly return to its place, and if you wish to see if the reduction has been done correctly in this manner
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And it is that you should have present one man who is taller than the sick person; and he should stand directly beside the bed, and put his shoulder under the buttocks of the sick person, and lift the buttocks upwards so that the sick person hangs in the air
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another physician pulls the hand of the sick person down towards the belly. And if the sick person is too light, then hang some heavy weight with them, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And the reduction is also done in another manner: and it is that one takes a long stick of wood, the thickness of which is like a pea, and not too thick nor too thin
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then it should be placed under the sick person, but with soft cloths underneath, and the sick person lying along the length of the wood; then their hand should be extended downwards on the other side properly, and the joint will quickly return to its place.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not wish to return despite all the things that we have said, then do this cure: take a piece of wood two spans long and four fingers wide, which has a round head for easy insertion deeply under the buttocks, like this shape
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place soft cloths on the head of the wood so that the wood does not bruise the sick person, then place it under the buttocks of the sick person; extend the arm along the length of the wood and tie the bandage to the wood and at the elbow of the hand, then place the arm upon a support made from a bone as wide as possible, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whatever way that may be, then you must place under the buttocks a pillow of even wool; then apply the plaster prepared with powder from a millstone, with incense and egg white all around the shoulder and bind it firmly under the buttocks, turn the bandage over the plaster, and wrap the hand around its neck, and let the hand remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they should eat little until the member is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then they may eat more afterwards after five or six days, and move about; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place because of moisture that has come into it, or for some other reason, then you should administer cauteries at three points, as is written in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and after twenty days the joint still does not stay in place, nor can they raise their arm upwards, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set back in its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the breast and the nipples, or behind them, is caused by a blow or stretching of the hand, and another bandage should be applied; and care should be taken until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there comes pain in the member and slowness in movement, then the sick person should bathe many times until that pain is alleviated and returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Regarding dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated outward and returns inward; and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially front and back, then the dislocation has not been reduced, because one can see it well and feel it clearly; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you bring the sick elbow together with the sound one, then you can see it clearly because the joint is knocked out and cannot bend the arm nor reach the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reduce it before abscesses occur there because if an abscess occurs then the reduction will be painful and perhaps cannot be reduced entirely, especially when it is behind; such a dislocation is worse than others and causes great pain and sometimes gangrene may occur
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the reduction is when it can be done thus: you should extend their hand with both of your hands; and their arm should be spread wide, and the hands of the doctor according to the elbow around, over, and under, and push the joint into its place at the base of the thumb or at the root of the palm until it returns to its proper position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when you fold their hand onto your hand and push the elbow that is dislocated from the root of the palm towards you.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension thus: two ministers should extend the arm and hold it tightly so that it does not move during the extension. Then turn the arm on each side until you have wrapped a long and wide cloth doubly around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the physician joins the joint with his hand, he oils it with some oil to soften the joint, then forces the joint greatly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in place, he puts on a dry compress with egg yolk and presses it firmly, then places the arm around the patient's neck and leaves it there for several days before removing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly set in its place, he unties the bandage and leaves it alone; but if you see that the joint has not healed properly, then begin again with the compress and the bandage, leaving it like this for several days until it is securely placed; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels great heat after the repositioning of the joint and it moves again, then he bathes and rubs it gently and presses until it is soothed; or you place a lambskin grease on the joint, leave it there for one day and one night, then remove it and put it in warm water.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it sweats, he rubs the joint gently and then replaces the lambskin grease and enters into warm water; doing this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see that it has not returned to its proper position, place hot poultice of fresh butter on it and press firmly; then it will return to its proper disposition.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand:
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joints of the hand are dislocated, and their return is easy,
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	"And the resetting is such that you place the sick hand upon a table, and the helper extends the hand, and the physician places it evenly, so that he places his palm upon the surface of the joint, and pushes until it returns."
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	"But still you must look to see if it is well in place; then the patient places the back of his hand upon a table at extension and resetting."
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	"And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then the patient places the back of his hand upon the table, and the physician places his hand upon that surface of the joint. If it returns now, that's good."
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	"If not, then apply plaster splints to calm and fix it, leaving it thus without restarting."
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	"And if he cannot endure it, and you are unable to put it back in place after several days, then the joint remains twisted;"
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	"And does not harm the patient further than that the hand is disabled and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves or arteries are cut; there is no other remedy but to relieve by cauterization near the case, and perhaps nothing else helps."
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	"And when the hand is in place, then apply the plaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it thus."
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, then moisten with hot water, and rub it until it becomes soft."
de la dislocation des dois de la main	This appears to be a heading or title in Old French: "Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand".
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	"Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the belly;"
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	"Then extend the finger and push the dislocation back until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it was dislocated;"
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	"and leave it for two days, and then set it equal on that day; and do not bind it too tightly, as we have said, and unbind it on the third day, and make it move, and rebind it loosely. And do this often until it becomes tight;"
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	"And do everything the same way if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do as you have done here until it is healed; and do everything the same way when it is dislocated on another side."
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	This appears to be a heading or title in Old French: "Of the dislocation of the spine of the back".
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	"When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no remedy, because the patient is already dead."
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	"And the sign is that the excretions come out without voluntary effort and cannot be held back, and often some member becomes weakened or both thighs or two arms or one."
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	"And often the spine moves in four parts; that which moves at the back is called 'gilbositis':"
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	"The remedy is that you should look out if the gilbositis has come from childhood: there is no remedy or cure for it at all."
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	"And that which comes from a fall or blow or similar things, the ancient authors mention ways of remedy with big words, but they do not have great benefit in all cases;"
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	"but I have shortened it according to my intention and formed various instruments in different ways."
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	"I say that in the case of gilbositis which comes at the front, there is neither remedy nor health;"
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	"and also that which comes straight across both sides, and one cannot cure it except properly that which comes at the back, as I say;"
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	"And that the patient should be laid on his face evenly in one place, and have a bandage under him so that he does not bruise himself;"
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	"then drive a stake firmly into the ground at the head and another at the feet, and tie a bandage across the sides of the patient, and another at the hips and knees and ankles;"
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	"and two ministers should hold the bandages, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes;"
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	"and let them be tied firmly, the stake as we have said, and the surgeon should press his palms firmly on the spine until it returns."
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	"And if it does not return with this remedy, then take a board three feet long and place it under the buttocks, and let the patient lie on his side, and put the end of the board under the buttocks, then place the middle of the board on the spine;"
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	"and let the surgeon put his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see that it does not return, then do it on the opposite side."
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	"And that you should drive two stakes at the head of the patient's bed, one arm's length apart, and two others towards the feet, with a space of one palm's width between each stake, above and below;"
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	"and that each stake should have a hole in it where the rope can pass through, and that the stakes should be firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes there should be a turning stake on which the rope turns, and this turning stake should have two small stakes of one palm's length to turn the rope;"
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	"and then tie the bandage that is between the sides to the turning stake towards the head and the other bandage towards the feet at the other turning stake, and each of the ministers should turn their rope all the way around the bandages, and the master should place the spine evenly as we have said."
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"And when it is even, then place a pad made of dry wool with plenty of eggs on top of it, and then the compresses and then the tile of a table three feet long, so that it covers the area of the gilbositis and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and let the patient be nourished with subtle foods until he is healed;"
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	"And if any difficulty comes at the end of the healing process, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medications with the tile that we have mentioned above, and sometimes one should apply a plaster;"
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	"and sometimes the appearance of a bulge in the lower spine can cause one to think that it is a dislocation; but this is only the bone showing through, so there should be no assumption: perhaps it would bring death."
des dislocations de la hainche	"on dislocations of the hip"
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	"Know that at the joints of the hip and shoulder only dislocations occur, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is unstable in four directions: inside and outside, front and back; but more unstable inside than others, and little unstable in front and back."
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	"And the sign of dislocation inside is that when one joins the lame leg with the sound one, it is longer, and the lame knee opens more than the sound one, and the lame knee cannot be bent at the fire;"
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	"and the place that is swollen with heat near a boil is where it lies, because the flesh of the thigh comes there."
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who is afflicted by this is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of one who has it before him is that he stretches his leg well according to its length; nevertheless, he cannot bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot do so, and he retains his urine, and the angle swells, and when he walks, he limps on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one who has it behind him is that he cannot straighten his knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the angle is softened, and the buttock is placed under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment for this type of dislocation is that you should examine whether the dislocation is old or new, and if it has remained in its position without care, then there will be no need for treatment, and he must not have any swelling.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where dislocation is recent,
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	"And if it does not return in this manner, then you must secure one strong assistant, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or one person should tie it above the knee."
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	"And another assistant extends their hand above in such a way that they place their hands under the dislocated limb, then gently ties it with a soft bandage around the hip; and another holds the head of the bandage."
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	"And everyone extends both upward and downward simultaneously so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains hanging."
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	"This manner of extension applies to four types of dislocations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good."
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	"If not, care must be taken according to its type. When the dislocation is at the hip, one must have the patient lie on their sound side, then place the bandage over the root of the hip and under the angle, then stretch the bandage upwards towards the angle and towards the thigh."
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	"Then another assistant takes the patient's arms and embraces the great trochanter of the dislocated hip, and extends it firmly upwards; now it should return to its place. This type of dislocation is easier than the others."
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	"And if you cannot reduce it in the manner that we have described, then you must tie both of the patient's feet together with a strong soft bandage over the two heels and knees, and extend the dislocated leg two fingers more than the other."
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	"Then suspend the patient from the top of a pole, so that their feet are two arm-lengths above the ground. Then command one assistant to embrace the head of the hip, and another assistant to hang with the patient, embracing the hip firmly, for the joint will now return quickly."
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	"And when the dislocation is towards the back, the patient lies on their belly, as we have described for those with kyphosis. Then apply one bandage properly to the dislocated leg and also to the foot."
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	"Then place two wedges, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert a wedge between the thighs of the patient in the shape of an 'M'."
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	"And have moist cloths ready to prevent burns to the patient. Then each assistant extends towards themselves, and the surgeon puts the dislocation back into place with their hand."
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	"If it returns, that is good. If not, place the patient on a board and press them as we have described for kyphosis, and have the patient lie on their sound side."
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	"And when the dislocation is towards the front, one must extend the dislocated leg quickly, as I have said; then the surgeon places their knee on the angle of the dislocated hip, presses with their other hand above it, and extends it downwards towards the knee."
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	"If the dislocation is towards the back, one must not extend the patient downwards nor lift them up from the ground. Instead, they should be positioned as if the hip were dislocated backwards, as we have described for delivery on both hips:"
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	"And place them on their face, extend the bandage as we said earlier, and press down on the joint with the board."
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	"And it will be done when the patient extends their legs and they are even. Then bring the thighs together, apply the splint, and bind them with a bandage so that the hip does not move."
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	"And let them rest for three or four days, then remove the bandage and apply the splint again. If the legs are even, bind it as before and leave it on for another three days. Then remove it, allowing the limb to move gently until it is comfortable."
de la dislocation dou genoil	**Treatment of Dislocations of the Knee**
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and behind; it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you tell the patient to bend their leg at the hip, and if it does not reach the hip, know that they are dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the treatment for all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if possible, and place your back against their face, and put their foot on top of yours.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take their kneecap in your palms and pull it between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee forcefully; another method is to extend their foot until the kneecap returns to its place, and the sign is that they can easily bend their leg at the hip.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and apply the plaster, and bind the leg to the hip tightly for three or four days, then release it; during this time, the patient should not walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb is not fully healed, then apply extension forcefully as we have said in the treatment of the thigh until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	Regarding the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel can sometimes be injured and sometimes fully dislocated both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it sticks out at the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	"Such resetting is easy, and it should be gently extended with both hands when merely moved."
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	"And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright and hold his leg with one hand above the ankle."
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	"Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, then with your left hand twice, stretch it upwards and gently push the foot back into place."
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	"And do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot in place. If it returns, that's good; if not, start over again, for it may slip back."
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	"If it still cannot return in this way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, stick a staff firmly into the ground between his thighs, and tie the cloths around so that he is not injured."
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	"Then one minister pulls the thigh, while another extends the foot with both hands or a rope tied to its heel."
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	"Then each minister pulls evenly and the staff should always be between the patient's thighs to hold him steady while stretching."
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	"Then the doctor gently puts his hands on the dislocated joint and another minister pulls the healthy leg below it, and the dislocation will quickly return to its place."
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	"And when it is in place, apply the plaster and compress it strongly, bind the foot to the leg, and be careful not to tie the bandages too tightly behind the ankle."
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	"Then leave it on for two or three days, and if the bandages swell, tighten them. On the fourth day or fifth day, untie them and do not allow the patient to walk for four days."
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	"And if he walks before that time is up, it's not certain that he won't dislocate again."
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If inflammation occurs, you must calm it as we have said elsewhere until the patient is healed."
des dois	I'm here to help! Please provide me with more context or information about what you'd like assistance with regarding "des doi" (which translates to "the two of them").
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	"If the two joints are dislocated, they should be gently stretched without force, and it is an easy thing to do."
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	"If the dislocation is in any knot of the back of the foot, make the patient sit on a level surface or on two tables placed right next to each other. Place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press strongly with your foot until it returns."
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when it is even and nothing opens, place a two-pronged fork under the sole of the foot, then compress strongly, and leave it on for three days before removing it. Then let the patient rest until healed."
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	"Regarding wounds and dislocations at the same time"
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	"If a wound comes with the dislocation and one wants to reduce it, many times the patient dies:"
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	"So do not be presumptuous in treating it if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time. Be cautious, compassionate, and slow, not hasty."
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	"And at the beginning, use things to calm heat and inflammation, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of recovery;"
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	"And when you see hope, then reduce the member now before inflammation becomes too severe;"
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	"And when the member is in place, administer things to calm heat and inflammation, and treat the wound with drying ointments as it should be."
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	"If there is also a fracture or small bones displaced, reset them, and do what we have said for simple fractures."
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	"And beware of falling into despair according to what I have said, for it is better for you according to your Creator's will, and for the safety of your soul and body. Amen."
Explicit le romen de fisique	"This ends the book of physics"
